The Prophet's Immediate Call to Tawhid
Theoretical refutation of the delay requirement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why prophets do not grant a delay for reflection and how they immediately present undeniable evidence for God's existence.

Core Idea
Prophets remove the delay, not grant it.

The Mu'tazila argued that prophets must allow people time to reflect before accepting their message. But the author counters that the very nature of prophethood is to remove that delay by presenting a proof so compelling that no time is needed. Let's examine this argument.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Mu'tazilite claim
Read the first part of the passage where the author states the Mu'tazilite position: that prophets must grant a delay (مهلة) for reflection.
Notice that the author says silencing prophets only applies if one holds this view.
2
See the author's counter
The author argues that the prophet does not grant a delay but instead removes it by offering an undeniable proof of God's existence: the listener's own contingency.
The proof is that you were not, then you came to be, and you did not create yourself.
3
Understand the logic
The author explains that a request for delay only arises if the call lacks compelling evidence. A true prophet always presents such evidence first.
The passage quotes Quran 2:21 as an example of the immediate call to tawhid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الجواب عن مسألة إمهال النظر وإفحام الأنبياء، فإنما يلزم الإفحام على من قال بالمهلة، ويجب على النبي إمهال النظر وذلك مذهب المعتزلة، وأما قال بأنه لا يمهله ولا يجب عليه أن يمهله، بل يجيب بأني جئت لأرفع المهلة وأرشدك إلى معرفة المرسل بأن أخبر عنك بما لا يمكنك إنكاره وهو احتياجك إلى صانع فاطر حكيم، إذ كنت تعرف ضرورة أنك لم تكن فكنت، وما كنت بنفسك بل يكون غيرك، وهذه هي ابتداء الدعوة بـ ﴿ يا أيها الناس اعبدوا ربكم الذي خلقكم والذين من قبلكم لعلكم تتقون ﴾ [البقرة: ٢١]، فكيف يمهله ويكله إلى نفسه وهو مأمور بدعوة الناس إلى التوحيد والمعرفة حالة فحالة وشخصا فشخصا، والاستمهال إنما يتوجه إذا خلت الدعوة عن الحجة الملزمة والدلالة المفحمة، فإن من تحققت رسالته عنه في نفسها وتصدى لدعوة الناس إلى وحدانية الله تعالى لا يخلى دعوته عن الدلالة على التوحيد أولا، ثم يتحدى بالرسالة عنه ثانيا اعتبار حال جميع الأنبياء عليهم السلام في دعوتهم.

أما آدم أبو البشر فقد ثبت صدقه بإخبار الله تعالى ملائكته: ﴿ إِنِّي جَاعِلٌ فِي الْأَرْضِ خَلِيفَةً ﴾ فلم يكن في أول زمانه من كان مشركا فيدعوه إلى التوحيد، وحين أمروا بالطاعة فمن صدق الله تعالى في خبره فسجد له بأمره، ومن لم يسجد فكأنه لم يصدق فاستحق اللعنة وهو أول من كفر، وأما نوح عليه السلام فأول كلامه مع قومه: ﴿ أَنِ اعْبُدُوا اللهَ مَا لَكُم مِّنْ إِلَهِ غَيْرُهُ ﴾ [المؤمنون: ٢٣] فأثبت التوحيد ثم النبوة فقال: ﴿ أَوَ عَجِبْتُمْ أَن جَاءَكُمْ ذِكْرٌ مِّن رَّبِّكُمْ عَلَى رَجُلٍ مِّنكُمْ لِيُنذِرَكُمْ ﴾ [الأعراف: ٦٣]، وأما هود بعده فقال: ﴿ يَاقَوْمِ اعْبُدُوا اللَّهَ مَا لَكُم مِّنْ إِلَٰهٍ غَيْرُهُ ﴾ ثم قال: ﴿ إِنِّي رَسُولٌ مِّن رَّبِّ الْعَالَمِينَ ﴾ [الأعراف: ٦٧] أثبت التوحيد ثم النبوة.

أما صالح بعده قال: ﴿ يَاقَوْمِ اعْبُدُوا اللَّهَ مَا لَكُم مِّنْ إِلَٰهٍ غَيْرُهُ ﴾ ثم قال: ﴿ قَدْ جَاءَتْكُم بَيِّنَةٌ مِّن رَّبِّكُمْ هَٰذِهِ ﴾ [الأعراف: ٧٣]، وأما لوط فإنه كان يدعو الناس بدعوة الخليل وما جرى بينه وبين قومه من عبدة الأوثان والكواكب من أظهر ما يتصور وقال: ﴿ أَتَعْبُدُونَ مَا تَنْحِتُونَ * وَاللَّهُ خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ ﴾ [الصافات: ٩٥-٩٦]، وقال لأبيه آزر: ﴿ أَتَتَّخِذُ أَصْنَامًا آلِهَةً ﴾ [الأنعام: ٧٤] في قوله: ﴿ إِذْ قَالَ لِأَبِيهِ يَا أَبَتِ لِمَ تَعْبُدُ مَا لَا يَسْمَعُ وَلَا يُبْصِرُ وَلَا يُغْنِي عَنكَ شَيْئًا ﴾ [مريم: ٤٢] ثم أثبت الرسالة فقال: ﴿ يَا أَبَتِ إِنِّي قَدْ جَاءَنِي مِنَ الْعِلْمِ مَا لَمْ يَأْتِكَ فَاتَّبِعْنِي أَهْدِكَ صِرَاطًا سَوِيًّا ﴾ [مريم: ٤٣]، وكانت الدعوة جارية على لسان أولاده إلى زمن موسى عليه السلام وكان من شأنه مع فرعون ما كان إذ قال له فرعون: ﴿ وَمَا رَبُّ الْعَالَمِينَ ﴾، ﴿ فَمَن رَّبُّكُمَا يَا مُوسَى ﴾ [طه: ٤٩]، حتى حقق عليه التوحيد بتعريف وحدانيته استدلالا من أفعاله عليه في جواب: ﴿ وَمَا رَبُّ الْعَالَمِينَ ﴾، قال: ﴿ رَبُّ السَّمَاوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ وَمَا بَيْنَهُمَا ﴾ وفي جواب: ﴿ مَن رَّبُّكُمَا ﴾، قال: ﴿ رَبُّنَا الَّذِي أَعْطَى كُلَّ شَيْءٍ خَلْقَهُ ثُمَّ هَدَى ﴾ [طه: ٥٠] ثم قال بعد ما قرر التوحيد: ﴿ إِنِّي رَسُولٌ مِّن رَّبِّ الْعَالَمِينَ ﴾.
As for the answer to the issue of granting a delay for reflection and silencing the prophets: indeed, the silencing only necessarily applies to one who says that there is a delay and that it is incumbent upon the prophet to grant a delay for reflection—and that is the doctrine of the Mu'tazila. As for [our] statement that he does not grant a delay and it is not incumbent upon him to grant a delay, rather he answers: 'I have come to remove the delay and guide you to knowledge of the Sender by informing you of what you cannot deny, namely your need for a Maker, an Originator, a Wise One, since you know necessarily that you were not and then you came to be, and you did not come to be by yourself, but rather another brought you into being.' This is the beginning of the call with [the verse]: 'O mankind, worship your Lord who created you and those before you that you may become righteous' [Quran 2:21]. So how could he grant him a delay and leave him to himself, when he is commanded to call people to tawhid and knowledge case by case and person by person? Requesting a delay only arises if the call is empty of a compelling proof and a silencing evidence. For one whose mission is established in itself and who undertakes to call people to the oneness of God, the Exalted, does not leave his call devoid of evidence for tawhid first; then he challenges with the message second, considering the state of all the prophets, peace be upon them, in their call.

As for Adam, the father of humanity, his truthfulness is established by God's informing His angels: 'Indeed I am placing on the earth a vicegerent.' So in his initial time there was no polytheist for him to call to tawhid. When they were commanded to obey, whoever believed God in His report prostrated to him by His command, and whoever did not prostrate was as if he did not believe, so he deserved the curse and he was the first to disbelieve. As for Noah, peace be upon him, his first speech to his people was: 'Worship God; you have no deity other than Him' [Quran 23:23]. Thus he established tawhid, then prophethood, saying: 'Are you amazed that a reminder has come to you from your Lord upon a man from among you to warn you?' [Quran 7:63]. As for Hud after him, he said: 'O my people, worship God; you have no deity other than Him,' then he said: 'Indeed I am a messenger from the Lord of the worlds' [Quran 7:67]. He established tawhid, then prophethood.

As for Salih after him, he said: 'O my people, worship God; you have no deity other than Him,' then he said: 'There has come to you clear evidence from your Lord; this is...' [Quran 7:73]. As for Lot, he called people with the call of the Friend [Abraham], and what occurred between him and his people—worshippers of idols and stars—is among the clearest that can be imagined. He said: 'Do you worship what you carve, while God created you and what you do' [Quran 37:95-96], and he said to his father Azar: 'Do you take idols as deities?' [Quran 6:74] in [the verse]: 'When he said to his father: O my father, why do you worship that which does not hear and does not see and does not avail you anything?' [Quran 19:42]. Then he established the message, saying: 'O my father, indeed there has come to me of knowledge that which has not come to you, so follow me; I will guide you to an even path' [Quran 19:43]. And the call continued on the tongues of his descendants until the time of Moses, peace be upon him, and what was his affair with Pharaoh when Pharaoh said to him: 'And what is the Lord of the worlds?' and 'Who is your Lord, O Moses?' [Quran 20:49]. He established tawhid upon him by defining His oneness through inference from His actions in answer to 'And what is the Lord of the worlds?' He said: 'The Lord of the heavens and the earth and what is between them,' and in answer to 'Who is your Lord?' he said: 'Our Lord is He who gave everything its creation, then guided' [Quran 20:50]. Then after he had established tawhid, he said: 'Indeed I am a messenger from the Lord of the worlds.'
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazilite position that prophets must grant a delay (مهلة) for rational reflection before accepting their message. The author begins by stating that the objection of 'silencing the prophets' (إفحام الأنبياء) only applies if one holds that a delay is obligatory—which is the Mu'tazilite view. The author's own position is that the prophet does not grant a delay and is not obligated to do so. Instead, the prophet immediately presents a compelling proof: he points out that the listener necessarily knows he was created and relies on a Creator, which is an undeniable truth. This is exemplified by the Quranic verse 'O mankind, worship your Lord...' (2:21). The author argues: how can the prophet delay when he is commanded to call people to tawhid continuously? The request for delay only arises if the call lacks a convincing proof. One whose prophetic mission is established and who calls to God's oneness must first provide evidence for tawhid, then challenge with the message of prophethood. The author then supports this by examining the practice of all prophets. He lists examples: Adam's truthfulness was established by God's announcement to the angels; he had no polytheists to call. Noah first called to worship God alone, then declared prophethood. Hud first called to tawhid, then said he was a messenger. Salih did the same. Lot argued against idolatry before asserting his prophethood. Moses first taught Pharaoh about the Lord of the heavens and earth and the Giver of all things, then declared his prophethood. The pattern is consistent: tawhid is always established first, followed by the claim of prophethood. Thus, the prophets did not grant a delay but immediately presented evidence for God's oneness.

Key Terms
مهلة النظر
إفحام الأنبياء
دلالة ملزمة
المعتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophets must give people unlimited time to think before accepting their message.
Correction: Prophets immediately present undeniable evidence for God's existence, making delay unnecessary.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what makes a request for delay unnecessary?
A) The prophet's permission
B) The presence of a compelling proof in the call
C) The listener's intelligence
D) The absence of any evidence

Key Takeaway
Prophets do not grant a delay; they remove it by presenting an undeniable proof of God's oneness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at your own existence—that you were nothing and then came to be—do you still find yourself asking for more time before fully submitting to your Creator? What is that delay costing you?
?
The prophet’s call removed all excuses. What excuse are you still holding onto that prevents you from responding to the undeniable truth of God’s oneness right now?
?
If you already know deep down that you depend on a Maker for every breath, why are you not living each moment in conscious worship of Him? What are you waiting for?

Prophetic Evidence: Tawhid Before Prophethood
Prophetic examples supporting the argument.

Learning Objective
Recognize the consistent pattern of prophets establishing tawhid before declaring their prophethood.

Core Idea
Every prophet first proved God's oneness, then claimed prophethood.

The author supports his argument by surveying the prophets from Adam to Moses. Their calls all followed the same pattern: first evidence for tawhid, then the announcement of prophethood. This historical consistency refutes the Mu'tazilite requirement for a delay.

Guided Path
1
Survey the prophets mentioned
Read the examples of Adam, Noah, Hud, Salih, Lot, and Moses. Notice the sequence in each case.
Each prophet first calls to worship God alone before declaring himself a messenger.
2
Identify the common pattern
In every case, the prophet first establishes tawhid with evidence, then asserts his prophethood.
For instance, Noah said 'Worship God, you have no deity other than Him' before saying 'I am a messenger'.
3
Understand the significance
This pattern shows that prophets do not need to grant a delay because they start with an undeniable truth—tawhid—which requires no further time for reflection.
The examples demonstrate that the call to tawhid is immediate and compelling.

وأما الجواب عن مسألة إمهال النظر وإفحام الأنبياء، فإنما يلزم الإفحام على من قال بالمهلة، ويجب على النبي إمهال النظر وذلك مذهب المعتزلة، وأما قال بأنه لا يمهله ولا يجب عليه أن يمهله، بل يجيب بأني جئت لأرفع المهلة وأرشدك إلى معرفة المرسل بأن أخبر عنك بما لا يمكنك إنكاره وهو احتياجك إلى صانع فاطر حكيم، إذ كنت تعرف ضرورة أنك لم تكن فكنت، وما كنت بنفسك بل يكون غيرك، وهذه هي ابتداء الدعوة بـ ﴿ يا أيها الناس اعبدوا ربكم الذي خلقكم والذين من قبلكم لعلكم تتقون ﴾ [البقرة: ٢١]، فكيف يمهله ويكله إلى نفسه وهو مأمور بدعوة الناس إلى التوحيد والمعرفة حالة فحالة وشخصا فشخصا، والاستمهال إنما يتوجه إذا خلت الدعوة عن الحجة الملزمة والدلالة المفحمة، فإن من تحققت رسالته عنه في نفسها وتصدى لدعوة الناس إلى وحدانية الله تعالى لا يخلى دعوته عن الدلالة على التوحيد أولا، ثم يتحدى بالرسالة عنه ثانيا اعتبار حال جميع الأنبياء عليهم السلام في دعوتهم.

أما صالح بعده قال: ﴿ يَاقَوْمِ اعْبُدُوا اللَّهَ مَا لَكُم مِّنْ إِلَٰهٍ غَيْرُهُ ﴾ ثم قال: ﴿ قَدْ جَاءَتْكُم بَيِّنَةٌ مِّن رَّبِّكُمْ هَٰذِهِ ﴾ [الأعراف: ٧٣]، وأما لوط فإنه كان يدعو الناس بدعوة الخليل وما جرى بينه وبين قومه من عبدة الأوثان والكواكب من أظهر ما يتصور وقال: ﴿ أَتَعْبُدُونَ مَا تَنْحِتُونَ * وَاللَّهُ خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ ﴾ [الصافات: ٩٥-٩٦]، وقال لأبيه آزر: ﴿ أَتَتَّخِذُ أَصْنَامًا آلِهَةً ﴾ [الأنعام: ٧٤] في قوله: ﴿ إِذْ قَالَ لِأَبِيهِ يَا أَبَتِ لِمَ تَعْبُدُ مَا لَا يَسْمَعُ وَلَا يُبْصِرُ وَلَا يُغْنِي عَنكَ شَيْئًا ﴾ [مريم: ٤٢] ثم أثبت الرسالة فقال: ﴿ يَا أَبَتِ إِنِّي قَدْ جَاءَنِي مِنَ الْعِلْمِ مَا لَمْ يَأْتِكَ فَاتَّبِعْنِي أَهْدِكَ صِرَاطًا سَوِيًّا ﴾ [مريم: ٤٣]، وكانت الدعوة جارية على لسان أولاده إلى زمن موسى عليه السلام وكان من شأنه مع فرعون ما كان إذ قال له فرعون: ﴿ وَمَا رَبُّ الْعَالَمِينَ ﴾، ﴿ فَمَن رَّبُّكُمَا يَا مُوسَى ﴾ [طه: ٤٩]، حتى حقق عليه التوحيد بتعريف وحدانيته استدلالا من أفعاله عليه في جواب: ﴿ وَمَا رَبُّ الْعَالَمِينَ ﴾، قال: ﴿ رَبُّ السَّمَاوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ وَمَا بَيْنَهُمَا ﴾ وفي جواب: ﴿ مَن رَّبُّكُمَا ﴾، قال: ﴿ رَبُّنَا الَّذِي أَعْطَى كُلَّ شَيْءٍ خَلْقَهُ ثُمَّ هَدَى ﴾ [طه: ٥٠] ثم قال بعد ما قرر التوحيد: ﴿ إِنِّي رَسُولٌ مِّن رَّبِّ الْعَالَمِينَ ﴾.
As for the answer to the issue of granting a delay for reflection and silencing the prophets: indeed, the silencing only necessarily applies to one who says that there is a delay and that it is incumbent upon the prophet to grant a delay for reflection—and that is the doctrine of the Mu'tazila. As for [our] statement that he does not grant a delay and it is not incumbent upon him to grant a delay, rather he answers: 'I have come to remove the delay and guide you to knowledge of the Sender by informing you of what you cannot deny, namely your need for a Maker, an Originator, a Wise One, since you know necessarily that you were not and then you came to be, and you did not come to be by yourself, but rather another brought you into being.' This is the beginning of the call with [the verse]: 'O mankind, worship your Lord who created you and those before you that you may become righteous' [Quran 2:21]. So how could he grant him a delay and leave him to himself, when he is commanded to call people to tawhid and knowledge case by case and person by person? Requesting a delay only arises if the call is empty of a compelling proof and a silencing evidence. For one whose mission is established in itself and who undertakes to call people to the oneness of God, the Exalted, does not leave his call devoid of evidence for tawhid first; then he challenges with the message second, considering the state of all the prophets, peace be upon them, in their call.

As for Adam, the father of humanity, his truthfulness is established by God's informing His angels: 'Indeed I am placing on the earth a vicegerent.' So in his initial time there was no polytheist for him to call to tawhid. When they were commanded to obey, whoever believed God in His report prostrated to him by His command, and whoever did not prostrate was as if he did not believe, so he deserved the curse and he was the first to disbelieve. As for Noah, peace be upon him, his first speech to his people was: 'Worship God; you have no deity other than Him' [Quran 23:23]. Thus he established tawhid, then prophethood, saying: 'Are you amazed that a reminder has come to you from your Lord upon a man from among you to warn you?' [Quran 7:63]. As for Hud after him, he said: 'O my people, worship God; you have no deity other than Him,' then he said: 'Indeed I am a messenger from the Lord of the worlds' [Quran 7:67]. He established tawhid, then prophethood.

As for Salih after him, he said: 'O my people, worship God; you have no deity other than Him,' then he said: 'There has come to you clear evidence from your Lord; this is...' [Quran 7:73]. As for Lot, he called people with the call of the Friend [Abraham], and what occurred between him and his people—worshippers of idols and stars—is among the clearest that can be imagined. He said: 'Do you worship what you carve, while God created you and what you do' [Quran 37:95-96], and he said to his father Azar: 'Do you take idols as deities?' [Quran 6:74] in [the verse]: 'When he said to his father: O my father, why do you worship that which does not hear and does not see and does not avail you anything?' [Quran 19:42]. Then he established the message, saying: 'O my father, indeed there has come to me of knowledge that which has not come to you, so follow me; I will guide you to an even path' [Quran 19:43]. And the call continued on the tongues of his descendants until the time of Moses, peace be upon him, and what was his affair with Pharaoh when Pharaoh said to him: 'And what is the Lord of the worlds?' and 'Who is your Lord, O Moses?' [Quran 20:49]. He established tawhid upon him by defining His oneness through inference from His actions in answer to 'And what is the Lord of the worlds?' He said: 'The Lord of the heavens and the earth and what is between them,' and in answer to 'Who is your Lord?' he said: 'Our Lord is He who gave everything its creation, then guided' [Quran 20:50]. Then after he had established tawhid, he said: 'Indeed I am a messenger from the Lord of the worlds.'
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazilite position that prophets must grant a delay (مهلة) for rational reflection before accepting their message. The author begins by stating that the objection of 'silencing the prophets' (إفحام الأنبياء) only applies if one holds that a delay is obligatory—which is the Mu'tazilite view. The author's own position is that the prophet does not grant a delay and is not obligated to do so. Instead, the prophet immediately presents a compelling proof: he points out that the listener necessarily knows he was created and relies on a Creator, which is an undeniable truth. This is exemplified by the Quranic verse 'O mankind, worship your Lord...' (2:21). The author argues: how can the prophet delay when he is commanded to call people to tawhid continuously? The request for delay only arises if the call lacks a convincing proof. One whose prophetic mission is established and who calls to God's oneness must first provide evidence for tawhid, then challenge with the message of prophethood. The author then supports this by examining the practice of all prophets. He lists examples: Adam's truthfulness was established by God's announcement to the angels; he had no polytheists to call. Noah first called to worship God alone, then declared prophethood. Hud first called to tawhid, then said he was a messenger. Salih did the same. Lot argued against idolatry before asserting his prophethood. Moses first taught Pharaoh about the Lord of the heavens and earth and the Giver of all things, then declared his prophethood. The pattern is consistent: tawhid is always established first, followed by the claim of prophethood. Thus, the prophets did not grant a delay but immediately presented evidence for God's oneness.

Key Terms
التوحيد
الرسالة
دلالة ملزمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophets first prove their prophethood with miracles, then call to tawhid.
Correction: The examples show that prophets first establish tawhid with evidence, then assert their prophethood.

Checkpoint
What is the consistent first step in the call of the prophets mentioned?
A) Performing a miracle
B) Declaring their prophethood
C) Calling to the oneness of God (tawhid)
D) Asking for a delay

Key Takeaway
Every prophet consistently established tawhid before declaring their prophethood, demonstrating the primacy of the call to God's oneness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you share Islam with others, do you begin by establishing the oneness of God, or do you jump to other topics? How does the prophetic example challenge your current approach? What will you change starting today?
?
Think of someone you know who does not believe in God. Have you ever prioritized proving your own sincerity or knowledge over simply making God's greatness evident? How can you realign your efforts with the prophetic method?
?
The prophets called to tawhid even before proving their prophethood. In your own life, do you sometimes seek to prove yourself before making God central? What would it look like to put God's oneness first in your conversations and actions this week?

Prophethood
beginner
6 min
The Priority of Tawhid in Prophetic Da'wah
Al-Juwayni enumerates prophetic examples to derive the rule of da'wah priority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that prophets consistently began their mission with establishing tawhid (the oneness of God), and only afterward addressed prophethood, except when the audience already affirmed tawhid.

Core Idea
Prophets prioritized tawhid—only after that, prophethood.

This passage from al-Juwayni examines the method of earlier prophets through Quranic examples. From Adam to Moses, the consistent pattern was to first call to the worship of God alone, and then to establish their own prophethood. This principle guides how da'wah should be conducted based on the audience's prior beliefs.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the sequence of prophets and their messages.
Pay attention to the order of topics in each prophet's call.
2
Identify the pattern
For each prophet from Noah onward, identify the two parts: call to tawhid and then mention of prophethood. Note how Adam is an exception.
Adam's time had no idolaters, so no call to tawhid was needed.
3
Understand the principle
After the examples, al-Juwayni states the general rule: start with tawhid if the audience denies it; start with prophethood if they already affirm tawhid.
The example of Jesus with the Children of Israel illustrates the second case.
4
Reflect on application
Consider how this principle applies in different contexts. Why is establishing tawhid foundational?
This connects to the broader methodology of Islamic da'wah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما آدم أبو البشر فقد ثبت صدقه بإخبار الله تعالى ملائكته: (إِنِّي جَاعِلٌ فِي الْأَرْضِ خَلِيفَةً) فلم يكن في أول زمانه من كان مشركا فيدعوه إلى التوحيد، وحين أمروا بالطاعة فمن صدق الله تعالى في خبره فسجد له بأمره، ومن لم يسجد فكأنه لم يصدق فاستحق اللعنة وهو أول من كفر. وأما نوح عليه السلام فأول كلامه مع قومه: (أَنِ اعْبُدُوا اللَّهَ مَا لَكُمْ مِنْ إِلَهِ غَيْرُهُ) [المؤمنون: 23] فأثبت التوحيد ثم النبوة فقال: (أَوَعَجِبْتُمْ أَنْ جَاءَكُمْ ذِكْرٌ مِنْ رَبِّكُمْ عَلَى رَجُلٍ مِنْكُمْ لِيُنْذِرَكُمْ) [الأعراف: 6]. وأما هود بعده فقال: (يَا قَوْمِ اعْبُدُوا اللَّهَ مَا لَكُمْ مِنْ إِلَهِ غَيْرُهُ) ثم قال: (رَسُولٌ مِنْ رَبِّ الْعَالَمِينَ) [الأعراف: 67] أثبت التوحيد ثم النبوة. وأما صالح بعده قال: (يَا قَوْمِ اعْبُدُوا اللَّهَ مَا لَكُمْ مِنْ إِلَهِ غَيْرُهُ) ثم قال: (جَاءَتْكُمْ بَيِّنَةٌ مِنْ رَبِّكُمْ هَذِهِ) [الأعراف: 73]. وأما لوط فإنه كان يدعو الناس بدعوة الخليل وما جرى بينه وبين قومه من عبدة الأوثان والكواكب من أظهر ما يتصور وقال: (أَتَعْبُدُونَ مَا تَنْحِتُونَ وَاللَّهُ خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ) [الصافات: 95-96]، وقال لأبيه آزر: (أَتَتَّخِذُ أَصْنَامًا آلِهَةً) [الأنعام: 74] في (إِذْ قَالَ لِأَبِيهِ يَا أَبَتِ لِمَ تَعْبُدُ مَا لَا يَسْمَعُ وَلَا يُبْصِرُ وَلَا يُغْنِي عَنْكَ شَيْئًا) [مريم: 42] ثم أثبت الرسالة فقال: (يَا أَبَتِ إِنِّي قَدْ جَاءَنِي مِنَ الْعِلْمِ مَا لَمْ يَأْتِكَ فَاتَّبِعْنِي أَهْدِكَ صِرَاطًا سَوِيًّا) [مريم: 43]. وكانت الدعوة جارية على لسان أولاده إلى زمن موسى عليه السلام وكان من شأنه مع فرعون ما كان إذ قال له فرعون: (وَمَا رَبُّ الْعَالَمِينَ) (فَمَنْ رَبُّكُمَا يَا مُوسَى) [طه: 49]، حتى حقق عليه التوحيد بتعريف وحدانيته استدلالا من أفعاله عليه في جواب: (وَمَا رَبُّ الْعَالَمِينَ)، قال: (رَبُّ السَّمَاوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ وَمَا بَيْنَهُمَا) وفي جواب: (مَنْ رَبُّكُمَا)، قال: (رَبُّنَا الَّذِي أَعْطَى كُلَّ شَيْءٍ خَلْقَهُ ثُمَّ هَدَى) [طه: 50] ثم قال بعد ما قرر التوحيد: (رَسُولٌ مِنْ رَبِّ الْعَالَمِينَ). فمن كان منكرًا للتوحيد وجبت البداية معه بإثباته، ومن كان مقرا به وجبت البداية معه بإثبات النبوة؛ كحال عيسى مع بني إسرائيل إذ قال: (قَدْ جِئْتُكُمْ بِبَيِّنَةٍ مِنْ رَبِّكُمْ) [الأعراف: 105].
As for Adam, the father of mankind, his truthfulness was established by God informing His angels: 'Indeed, I will make upon the earth a vicegerent.' So there was not in his first time anyone who was an idolater that he would call him to tawhid. And when they were commanded obedience, whoever believed God in His news prostrated to him by His command, and whoever did not prostrate, it was as if he did not believe, so he deserved the curse, and he was the first to disbelieve. As for Noah, upon him peace, the first of his speech to his people was: 'Worship God; you have no god other than Him' [Al-Mu'minun: 23]. So he established tawhid, then prophethood, saying: 'Are you amazed that a reminder from your Lord has come to you upon a man from you to warn you?' [Al-A'raf: 6]. As for Hud after him, he said: 'O my people, worship God; you have no god other than Him,' then he said: 'A messenger from the Lord of the worlds' [Al-A'raf: 67]. He established tawhid, then prophethood. As for Salih after him, he said: 'O my people, worship God; you have no god other than Him,' then he said: 'There has come to you a clear proof from your Lord, this [she-camel]' [Al-A'raf: 73]. As for Lot, he was calling people with the call of the Friend (Abraham), and what occurred between him and his people, the worshippers of idols and stars, is among the clearest things imaginable. He said: 'Do you worship what you carve while God created you and what you do?' [As-Saffat: 95-96]. And he said to his father Azar: 'Do you take idols as gods?' [Al-An'am: 74] in 'When he said to his father: O my father, why do you worship that which does not hear, does not see, and does not benefit you at all?' [Maryam: 42]. Then he established the message saying: 'O my father, indeed there has come to me of knowledge that which has not come to you, so follow me; I will guide you to a straight path' [Maryam: 43]. And the call continued upon the tongues of his descendants until the time of Moses, upon him peace, and his affair with Pharaoh was what it was when Pharaoh said to him: 'And what is the Lord of the worlds?' and 'Who is your Lord, O Moses?' [Ta-Ha: 49] until he established tawhid for him by defining His oneness through deduction from His actions, in answer to 'And what is the Lord of the worlds?' he said: 'Lord of the heavens and the earth and what is between them,' and in answer to 'Who is your Lord?' he said: 'Our Lord is He who gave everything its creation, then guided' [Ta-Ha: 50]. Then he said, after he had established tawhid: 'A messenger from the Lord of the worlds.' So whoever denies tawhid, the beginning with him must be with establishing it, and whoever affirms it, the beginning with him must be with establishing prophethood, as was the case of Jesus with the Children of Israel when he said: 'I have come to you with a clear proof from your Lord' [Al-A'raf: 105].
Source pages p. 427

Commentary
This passage is a classification and proof of prophetic method. The author presents examples of earlier prophets (Adam, Noah, Hud, Salih, Lot, Abraham, Moses, Jesus) to show that their da'wah consistently began with establishing tawhid (oneness of God) before proving their prophethood. The only exception is the case where the audience already affirms tawhid; then prophethood is addressed first. The author argues that since Adam's time there were no idolaters yet, so his call did not target tawhid explicitly, but later prophets always started with tawhid. The key point is that the priority in da'wah depends on the audience's state of belief. The author then generalizes: if the audience denies tawhid, the da'i must start by establishing tawhid; if they affirm tawhid, then start with proving prophethood. This is illustrated with the example of Jesus, who came to the Children of Israel (who already believed in God) and therefore began with establishing his prophethood through clear signs.

النبوة
الدعوة
الصدق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think prophets always began their mission with prophethood, not tawhid.
Correction: The passage shows that prophets consistently started with tawhid, except when the audience already believed in One God.

Checkpoint
According to the author, when should a da'i begin with establishing tawhid?
A) Always, regardless of the audience
B) Only when the audience denies tawhid
C) Only when the audience affirms tawhid
D) Only when the audience is from the People of the Book

Key Takeaway
The method of the prophets teaches us to prioritize the message of tawhid when addressing those who deny it, and to move directly to prophethood when addressing monotheists.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to invite someone to Islam today, would you start with tawhid or with proofs of prophethood? Why? And does your answer change depending on the person's background? How does the prophetic method challenge your own approach?
?
Think of a person you know who does not believe in God. Have you ever truly prioritized calling them to tawhid, or have you been distracted by secondary issues? What will you do differently after this lesson?
?
The prophets did not compromise on starting with tawhid. Is there an area in your life where you are putting something else before the oneness of God? What would it look like to truly prioritize tawhid in that area today?

Prophethood

The Prophet's Method: Starting with Tawhid
Describes the Prophet starting with tawhid then prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Prophet Muhammad would sometimes begin his call by establishing tawhid and then proving his prophethood through the challenge of the Quran.

Core Idea
The Prophet's verses combine tawhid and prophethood proofs into one powerful call.

This lesson examines a key feature of the Prophet's da'wah methodology. When addressing idolaters, he often started by affirming the oneness of God and the need to worship Him, then immediately linked that to his own prophethood by presenting the Quran as a miracle. This dual approach made his message self-contained and compelling.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about the first method
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice the structure: tawhid first, then prophethood.
The passage cites Quran 2:21-22 and the challenge verse.
2
Identify the two stages
The Prophet first establishes tawhid by arguing for a Creator and Provider. Then he moves to prophethood by challenging the idolaters to produce a surah like the Quran.
3
Observe the interconnection of proofs
Note that the verse's meaning points to tawhid, while its eloquent wording points to the truth of his prophethood.
The same verse carries both proofs.
4
Reflect on the effectiveness
Think about why starting with tawhid might be effective for idolaters. It establishes a common ground before introducing the proof of prophethood.
This method respects the listener's prior beliefs.

ولما كانت دعوة سيد البشر محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم أكمل، ورسالته أرفع وأجل كان يبتدئ تارة مع عبدة الأصنام بإثبات التوحيد، ثم بالنبوة: (يَا أَيُّهَا النَّاسُ اعْبُدُوا رَبَّكُمُ الَّذِي خَلَقَكُمْ) أثبت احتياجهم ضرورة إلى فاطر، وشاركهم في ذلك من قبلهم (مِنْ قَبْلِكُمْ لَعَلَّكُمْ) كما قرر احتياجهم إلى الخالق في وجودهم قرر احتياجهم إلى رازق في بقائهم: (الَّذِي جَعَلَ لَكُمُ الْأَرْضَ فِرَاشًا وَالسَّمَاءَ بِنَاءً) [البقرة: 22] الآية، ثم قرر بعد ذلك نبوته: (وَإِنْ كُنْتُمْ فِي رَيْبٍ مِمَّا نَزَّلْنَا عَلَى عَبْدِنَا فَأْتُوا بِسُورَةٍ مِنْ مِثْلِهِ) الآية بمعناها دالة على التوحيد، وبظاهر لفظها البليغ ونظمها الأنيق دالة على صدق دعواه وتحديه. ولربما يبتدئ بدعوى الرسالة ثم يضمنها حقائق التوحيد: (يَا أَيُّهَا النَّاسُ إِنِّي رَسُولُ اللَّهِ إِلَيْكُمْ جَمِيعًا الَّذِي لَهُ مُلْكُ السَّمَاوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا هُوَ يُحْيِي وَيُمِيتُ) الآية، حتى كانت الآية بعذوبة ألفاظها ورطوبة عباراتها الخارجة عن نظم الشعراء ونثر الفصحاء الخارقة لعاداتهم الجارية وعباراتهم الفائقة أوضح دلالة على رسالته وصدق لهجته وكانت معانيها الحقيقية وحقائقها المعنوية دالة على التوحيد واقترنت الدلالتان اقترانا لا يمكن للمستمع الاستمهال، وليس ذلك أمراً بالتقليد، فإن التقليد قبول قول الغير من غير حجة، وفيها تقرر حجتان.
And since the call of the master of mankind, Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, was more perfect, and his message was higher and more sublime, he would sometimes begin with the idolaters by establishing tawhid, then prophethood: (O mankind, worship your Lord who created you) He established their necessary need for a Creator, and included them with those before them (those before you that you may become righteous). Just as he established their need for the Creator in their existence, he established their need for a Provider in their survival: (who made for you the earth a bed and the sky a structure) [Al-Baqarah: 22]—the verse. Then he established after that his prophethood: (And if you are in doubt about what We have sent down upon Our servant, then produce a surah like it) – the verse. Its meaning is indicative of tawhid, and by its apparent eloquent wording and elegant composition it is indicative of the truth of his claim and his challenge. And perhaps he would begin with the claim of message then include within it the realities of tawhid: (O mankind, indeed I am the messenger of God to you all, to whom belongs the dominion of the heavens and the earth; there is no god except Him; He gives life and causes death) – the verse. So the verse, with the sweetness of its wording and the freshness of its expressions, which are outside the poetry of poets and the prose of eloquent speakers, breaking their customary habits and surpassing their expressions, was the clearest indication of his message and the truth of his speech, and its true meanings and conceptual realities were indicative of tawhid. The two indications were conjoined in such a conjunction that the listener could not [separate] them. And that is not a matter of taqlid (blind imitation), for taqlid is accepting the saying of another without proof, and in it [the verse] two proofs are established.
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This passage explains the unique method of Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) in combining proofs of tawhid and prophethood in a single verse or in close conjunction. The author notes that sometimes the Prophet would start with establishing tawhid (e.g., 'O mankind, worship your Lord who created you') and then move to proving his prophethood by the challenge of producing a like surah. In other cases, he would begin by claiming prophethood (e.g., 'I am the messenger of God to you all') and within the same verse include statements of tawhid (e.g., 'there is no god except Him'). The author argues that this combination is more powerful because the verse itself—by its eloquence and miraculous nature—proves the truth of his prophethood, while its content simultaneously proves tawhid. This dual proof is so intertwined that the listener cannot pause or hesitate. The author then clarifies that this is not taqlid (blind acceptance of authority), because taqlid is accepting a statement without proof, whereas here two proofs are actually presented: one through the verse's meaning (tawhid) and one through its miraculous form (prophethood). Thus the listener is not blindly imitating but is presented with evidence.

Key Terms

النبوة
التحدي

Checkpoint
What did the Prophet establish first for the idolaters according to this method?
A) Prophethood
B) Tawhid
C) Both together
D) None

Key Takeaway
The Prophet often began by establishing tawhid before proving his prophethood through the Quranic challenge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you invite others to Islam, do you first establish the reality of the Creator and His provision, or do you jump straight to rules and rituals? Where does your emphasis betray a lack of trust in the method of the Prophet?
?
If the Quran's very wording proves its divine origin and points to tawhid, why do you sometimes treat the Quran as merely a book of laws rather than the living proof of God's existence and your own accountability?
?
The Prophet connected creation and provision directly to worship. In your own life, do you see your daily sustenance as evidence of the Creator's right to be worshipped, or have you separated your belief in God from your gratitude and obedience?

The Prophet's Method: Starting with Prophethood
Describes the Prophet starting with prophethood and including tawhid, and refutes taqlid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet sometimes began by claiming prophethood and included tawhid within the same verse, and how this combined proof is not taqlid.

Core Idea
A single verse can contain both the proof of prophethood and the realities of tawhid.

In this lesson, we explore another method of the Prophet's call: starting directly with the claim of prophethood, but embedding the truths of tawhid within the same verse. The author shows that the eloquence of the verse itself proves his prophethood, while its content proves tawhid. This dual proof is so tightly joined that the listener cannot pause, and the author clarifies that this is not blind imitation but evidence-based.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about starting with prophethood
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the verse cited (Quran 7:158) and how it contains both tawhid and the prophethood claim.
2
Identify the two proofs in the verse
The verse's miraculous wording and eloquence prove prophethood; its meanings prove tawhid. Identify each.
3
Understand the conjoining of proofs
The author says the two indications are so conjoined that the listener cannot separate them. Reflect on why this is powerful.
4
Discuss the refutation of taqlid
The author clarifies that this method is not taqlid because two proofs are presented. Understand the distinction.
Taqlid is accepting a statement without proof. Here, proofs are provided.

How Miracles Remove Doubt for All
Answer clarifying how miracles dispel doubt for experts and laypeople.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how miracles dispel doubt for both experts and laypeople, and why widespread transmission suffices to establish prophetic truthfulness.

Core Idea
Miracles remove doubt through expert verification and widespread transmission.

In this passage, the author answers the third objection by explaining that miracles effectively remove doubt for all people, whether experts or common folk. He argues that those with expertise are the most convinced when a miracle defies their expectations, and laypeople rely on the widespread reports of miracles. The prophet is not required to show a miracle to each individual; rather, the truth of his message is transmitted through reliable chains of narration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main claim
The passage begins by stating that anyone who doubts a claimant must have that doubt removed. Then it focuses on how miracles achieve this for experts and laypeople.
2
Understand the role of experts
The author argues that people with expertise in the properties of things and awareness of tricks are the hardest to convince; but when they see a miracle contrary to their expectations, they become the most accepting.
3
See how laypeople are convinced
For common people, even if illusions cause doubt initially, miracles remove that doubt because they are more remarkable than any trick. The prophet does not need to show a miracle to each person; widespread transmission suffices.
4
Learn the concept of istifāḍah and tawātur
Once the prophet's truthfulness is established through miracles witnessed by many, his statements reach others through widespread reports (istifāḍah) and continuous chains (tawātur), both in his time and later through narration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الجواب عن السؤال الثالث أن نقول : كل من عارضه شك في صدق المتحدي وجب إراحته، لكن المعجزة إذا ظهرت لأهل الخبرة وحصل لهم العلم بذلك وهو جم غفير فأخرى أن لا يبقى شك لأهل الصناعات الأخر، وإن أشد الناس إنكارا من كان عنده خبرة وبصيرة بخواص الأشياء وأحوال أهل المخرقة والتخيل، وإذا ظهرت المعجزة على خلاف ما توهموه فهو أولى الناس بالقبول. وأما العامة فالتخيلات والمخاريق إذا أورثت لهم شكا في الحال، فأولى أن لا يعتريهم ريب في مقال أصحاب المعجزات فيلزمهم الإقرار بتصديقه، ويلزم غيرهم من العامة إذا سمعوا منهم جلية الأمر الاعتراف به من غير توقف ولا ريب، ولا يجب على النبي عليه السلام تتبع آحاد الناس وإفراد كل واحد بمعجزة خاصة، وإذا تقرر صدقه فنسبة قوله إلى من صح عنده كنسبته إلى غيره ; إما في زمانه وهو في قطر آخر باستفاضة الخبر إليه والمواترة عليه ، وإما في غير زمانه بالنقل والاستفاضة والشيوع.
As for the answer to the third question, we say: Everyone who is confronted with doubt concerning the truthfulness of the claimant must be relieved of that doubt. But if the miracle appears to people of expertise and they attain knowledge of it, and they are a numerous multitude, then it is more fitting that no doubt remains for the people of other crafts. And indeed the most severely denying of people are those who have experience and insight into the properties of things and the states of the people of trickery and illusion; when the miracle appears contrary to what they imagined, he is the most deserving of people for acceptance. As for the common people, if illusions and tricks caused them doubt in that situation, then it is more fitting that doubt should not befall them concerning the statement of the miracle-workers, so they are required to affirm and believe him. And it is required of other common people that if they hear from them the clarity of the matter, they acknowledge it without pause or doubt. And it is not incumbent upon the Prophet, peace be upon him, to follow individual people and to single out each one with a specific miracle. And once his truthfulness is established, the relation of his statement to the one for whom it is sound with him is like its relation to others; either in his time when he is in another region, by the widespread transmission (istifāḍah) of the report to him and its tawātur upon him, or in other than his time, by narration, widespread transmission (istifāḍah), and dissemination.
Source pages p. 437

Commentary
This passage is the answer to the third objection concerning the effect of miracles on doubt. The author argues that if someone doubts the truthfulness of a claimant to prophethood, it is necessary to relieve that doubt. When a miracle appears to experts who have certain knowledge of it, and they are many, then there is even less reason for doubt among people of other professions. The most stubborn deniers are those with experience and insight into the properties of things and the tricks of illusionists; when the miracle contradicts their expectations, they are the first to accept. As for the common people, if tricks and illusions caused them doubt initially, then it is even more fitting that they should not feel doubt about the statements of miracle-workers, so they must acknowledge and believe. Moreover, the prophet is not required to chase down each individual and present a separate miracle to each one. Once his truthfulness is established, the transmission of his statement to those who hear it in his time through widespread reports (istifāḍah) and tawātur is the same as to others, and in later times through narration and widespread dissemination.

الشك
أهل الخبرة
المتحدي

Misconception: Only experts can verify miracles; laypeople cannot be sure.
Correction: The author explains that laypeople also become convinced through widespread transmission (istifāḍah and tawātur) without needing to witness the miracle directly.

Answer to the Fifth Objection: Multiple Ways to Recognize a True Prophet
Answer to the fifth objection: miracles are not the only proof of prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that identifying a prophet does not rely solely on miracles; God has multiple means including necessary knowledge, circumstantial evidence, and direct communication.

Core Idea
A prophet can be known by many paths, not only miracles.

This passage answers the objection that without miracles, prophethood cannot be verified. The author explains that God may create necessary knowledge, provide non-supernatural indicators, or speak directly to chosen recipients. These multiple ways show that miracles are not the exclusive proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the Passage and Translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation to get a sense of the author's argument. Note the structure: it directly addresses the fifth objection.
Pay attention to the key terms like 'ʿilm ḍarūrī' (necessary knowledge) and 'qarāʾin' (indicators).
2
Identify the Three Alternative Means
The passage lists three ways God can make a prophet known without miracles: (1) creating necessary knowledge, (2) setting up non-supernatural indicators (amārāt), and (3) direct divine communication. Find each in the text.
The indicators may be based on circumstantial and verbal evidence (qarīnat al-ḥāl wa al-maqāl).
3
Examine the Example of the Angels
The author gives an example of direct communication: God informing the angels about Adam's vicegerency. This shows that even without a miracle, the prophets' truthfulness can be established through divine speech.
The verse from Al-Baqara (2:30) is cited as evidence.
4
Understand the Principle of Variability
Notice that the passage says evidence may work for one person but not another. This highlights that God's ways of guiding people are diverse and tailored.
This counters the objection that miracles are a universal and necessary proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الجواب عن السؤال الخامس نقول : لا ينحصر طريق التعريف في المعجزات، بل يجوز أن يخلق لهم علمًا ضروريًا بصدق النبي، فلا يحتاج المدعو إلى طلب المعجزة ليعرف بها صدقه، أو ينصب لهم أمارات أخر غير خارقة للعادة، لكن يتبين لواحد بحكم قرينة الحال والمقال صدقه والقرائن لا تنحصر في طريق واحد ورب قرينة أورثت علمًا لشخص ولم تورث علما لغيره، أو يخبر من استأهله لسماع كلامه فيعلم صدقه، كما أخبر الملائكة: (إِنِّي جَاعِلٌ فِي الْأَرْضِ خَلِيفَةً) [البقرة: 30]، وإذا ثبت صدقه عندهم؛ إما بالخبر أو بتعليم الأسماء لزم.
As for the answer to the fifth question, we say: The means of identification is not limited to miracles. Rather, it is possible for Him to create for them necessary knowledge (ʿilman ḍarūriyyan) of the prophet's truthfulness, so the one called does not need to seek the miracle to know his truthfulness. Or He may set up for them other indicators not supernatural, but it becomes clear to one, by the rule of circumstantial and verbal evidence, his truthfulness. And evidences are not confined to one path, and perhaps an evidence bequeaths knowledge to one person and does not bequeath knowledge to another. Or He informs whoever deserves to hear His speech, so he knows his truthfulness, just as the angels were informed: 'Indeed, I will make upon the earth a successor' (Al-Baqara: 30). And when his truthfulness is established for them, either by report or by teaching of the names, it is necessary.
Source pages p. 439

Commentary
This passage is an answer to a specific objection (the fifth question). The objector likely argued that without miracles, prophethood cannot be known. The author replies that miracles are not the only way. God can create necessary knowledge (ʿilm ḍarūrī) in people, so they instinctively know the prophet is true. Alternatively, God may provide non-supernatural indicators (amārāt) such as circumstantial and verbal evidence (qarīnat al-ḥāl wa al-maqāl), which can vary from person to person. Another way is direct divine communication, like God informing angels of Adam's vicegerency. Once the prophet's truthfulness is established—by report or by teaching—it becomes binding. Thus, the reliance on miracles is not exclusive.

Key Terms
التعريف
المعجزات
علم ضروري
القرائن
خارق للعادة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Miracles are the only way to verify a prophet.
Correction: God has multiple means including necessary knowledge, circumstantial evidence, and direct communication.

Beyond Miracles: Multiple Ways to Recognize a True Prophet
The author lists alternative means to know a prophet's truthfulness beyond miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that recognizing a true prophet does not depend solely on miracles; there are several other valid means including direct knowledge, circumstantial evidence, and reports from previous prophets.

Core Idea
Miracles are not the only way to know a prophet; God provides multiple paths to certainty.

The author now addresses the fifth objection, which assumes that miracles are the only way to verify a prophet's truthfulness. He argues that this assumption is false. In this passage, he lists alternative means—direct divine knowledge, non-supernatural indicators, and reports from earlier prophets—and supports his argument with examples from the Torah, Gospel, and Quran. This expands our understanding of how prophethood can be recognized.

Read the passage and translation

2
Identify the three alternative ways
The author lists three alternative ways to recognize a prophet: 1) direct necessary knowledge from Allah, 2) non-supernatural circumstantial indicators, and 3) reports from previous truthful sources. Find these in the text.
These are not mutually exclusive; any of them can suffice.

And as for the answer to the fifth question, we say: The method of recognition is not limited to miracles, but it is possible that He creates for them necessary knowledge of the truthfulness of the prophet, so the one who is reminded does not need to seek a miracle to know his truthfulness through it, or He sets up for them other indicators not supernatural, but it becomes evident to one by virtue of the context of the situation and speech his truthfulness, and indicators are not limited to one way, and perhaps an indicator causes knowledge for a person and does not cause knowledge for another, or one informs whom He has made worthy to hear His speech and thus he knows his truthfulness, just as the angels informed: 'Indeed I am placing in the earth a caliph,' and when his truthfulness is established with them, either by report or by teaching of the names, his attestation becomes incumbent upon everyone who comes after them, and when one whose truthfulness has been established by some evidence informs about another truthful successor, his attestation becomes obligatory. And likewise, the report of every truthful one is glad tidings for those after him, and an announcement to the creation of signs in his creation, form, speech, and action, and it is obligatory upon everyone who hears that to attest him by the report of the first. And for this reason the Revelation informed about such a state on the tongue of Jesus, peace be upon him: 'with a messenger coming after me whose name is Ahmad,' and on the tongue of Moses, peace be upon him: 'the unlettered prophet whom they find written with them in the Torah and the Gospel' the verse, and on the tongue of Abraham, peace be upon him: 'Our Lord, and send among them a messenger' the verse, and his signs in the Torah and the Gospel are more than can be counted. And indeed, Moses had a house of images, i.e., images of the prophets and saints, peace be upon him, which he would enter and study the images every Sabbath. Therefore his miracles were limited to manifesting the matter to the unlettered of the Arabs, excluding the People of the Book from the Jews and Christians, for they were veiled by what was established with them of reports from the truthful ones.
Source pages p. 439

Commentary
This passage is an answer to the fifth objection. The author argues that the method of recognizing a true prophet is not confined to miracles. He lists several possibilities: 1) Allah could create direct necessary knowledge of the prophet's truthfulness in the listener, so no miracle is needed. 2) He could provide non-supernatural indicators (أمارات) that, through circumstantial evidence (قرينة الحال والمقال), yield certainty for some but not others. 3) He could inform directly, as when Allah told the angels 'I am placing a caliph on earth,' and when that report establishes a prophet's truthfulness, all subsequent hearers must accept it. The author then gives examples from earlier prophets: Jesus announced Ahmad, Moses announced the unlettered prophet, Abraham prayed for a messenger. He mentions that Moses had a house of images of prophets and saints, which served as evidence. He concludes that the Prophet Muhammad's miracles were primarily for the unlettered Arabs, while the People of the Book already had sufficient evidence from previous scriptures and reports.

Theoretical Knowledge and Its Necessary Foundation
The author answers the sixth question by explaining the relationship between theoretical and necessary knowledge with application to prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why all theoretical knowledge must be grounded in necessary knowledge and how knowledge of prophethood can be immediate through circumstantial evidence.

Core Idea
All theoretical knowledge ultimately rests on necessary knowledge, but the starting point can be near or far.

In this passage, the author addresses the sixth objection by establishing a foundational epistemological principle: every theoretical claim must trace back to something self-evident. He then applies this principle to prophethood, arguing that the evidence for prophethood can be immediate, not requiring a long chain of reasoning. Let's examine how.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the key terms: علم نظري and علم ضروري. The flow may be unfamiliar at first.
The passage contains a small scribal note: 'ريما' is likely 'ربما' (sometimes).
2
Identify the general principle
The author states that every theoretical knowledge must be based on necessary knowledge. This is the core epistemological rule. Write it down in your own words.
Necessary knowledge is self-evident or directly known.
3
Understand the two possibilities
The necessary knowledge can be 'far in its starting point' (بعيد المبدأ) meaning many intermediate steps are needed, or 'near' (قريب المبدأ) meaning it is immediately accessible.
The author uses this to show variety in how theoretical depends on necessary.
4
Apply to prophethood
If knowledge of prophethood is obtained through circumstantial evidence (قرائن الأحوال), it is near the starting point. The challenger's claim is directly testable: he is either truthful or lying.
This counters the objection that prophethood requires a long theoretical chain.
5
Reflect on the significance
Consider why this matters: The author defends the immediacy of belief in prophethood, making it accessible without extensive reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الجواب عن السؤال السادس نقول : كل علم نظري لا بد وأن يستند إلى علم ضروري ، ولكن الضروري ريما يكون بعيد المبدأ، وإنما يستند إليه النظري بعد نظريات كثيرة، وربما يكون قريب المبدأ فيستند إليه في أول المرتبة، والعلم بصدق النبوات إن عددناه من جنس العلوم الحاصلة بقرائن الأحوال فهو في أول المرتبة يصل إليه، فيقال : هذا المتحدي إما أن يكون صادقا، وإما أن يكون كاذبا
And as for the answer to the sixth question, we say: Every theoretical knowledge must necessarily be based on necessary knowledge, but the necessary knowledge sometimes is far in its starting point, and theoretical knowledge is only based upon it after many theoretical steps, and sometimes it is near in its starting point, so it is based upon it at the first level. And knowledge of the truthfulness of prophethood, if we consider it among the genus of knowledge obtained through circumstantial evidence, then at the first level one reaches it, so it is said: This challenger is either truthful or lying.
Source pages p. 440

Commentary
This passage is an answer to the sixth objection. The author makes a general epistemological point: all theoretical knowledge (علم نظري) must ultimately rest on necessary knowledge (علم ضروري). However, the necessary knowledge can be either 'distant in its starting point' (بعيد المبدأ), requiring many intermediate theoretical steps, or 'near in its starting point' (قريب المبدأ), so it can be accessed directly at the first stage. He applies this to knowledge of prophethood: if we classify it as the kind of knowledge obtained through circumstantial evidence (قرائن الأحوال), then it is actually near the starting point—one can reach it immediately by considering the challenge (التحدي). So it is not a distant theoretical knowledge that requires a long chain; rather, it is immediate. The challenger's claim is either truthful or lying, and the evidence is right there.

Key Terms
علم نظري
علم ضروري
قرائن الأحوال
مبدأ قريب
مبدأ بعيد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Knowledge of prophethood is purely theoretical, requiring a long chain of reasoning.
Correction: The author argues that if considered as knowledge from circumstantial evidence, it is immediate because the necessary evidence (the challenger's claim) is near at hand.

Checkpoint

D) It is impossible to attain without a miracle

Key Takeaway
All theoretical knowledge must trace back to necessary knowledge, and knowledge of prophethood, when based on circumstantial evidence, is immediate because the necessary evidence is near at hand.

Prophethood Confirmed by Prior Prophecies
Arguing prophethood is confirmed by prior prophecies

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the prophethood of Muhammad is confirmed through the announcements and signs given by earlier prophets as recorded in the Quran.

Core Idea
Prophets are confirmed by the truthful reports of those before them.

This passage from a classical kalam work argues that belief in a prophet does not rest solely on miracles—it can be established through the testimony of earlier truthful figures. The author explains a general principle and then applies it to Muhammad, showing how previous prophets like Jesus, Moses, and Abraham foretold his coming.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once silently, then read the English translation. Note the logical flow from general principle to specific examples.
This is a single continuous argument.
2
Identify the core principle
The author states that if a person whose truthfulness is established reports about a later truthful person, it becomes obligatory to believe in that later person. This is the key underlying argument.
3
Examine the Quranic evidence
The passage cites three Quranic verses: Jesus foretelling Ahmad, Moses describing the unlettered prophet, and Abraham's prayer for a messenger. Notice how each verse is used as a report from a truthful prophet.
4
Understand the conclusion about miracles
The author concludes that because the People of the Book already had convincing scriptural prophecies, Muhammad's miracles were primarily for the unlettered Arabs.
This explains the audience of his miracles.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تصديقه على كل من خلف بعدهم، وإذا أخبر من ثبت صدقه بدليل ما عن صادق آخر يخلفه وجب تصديقه. وكذلك الخبر عن كل صادق بشارة لمن بعده، وإعلاما للخلق بآيات في خلقه وصورته وقوله وفعله وجب على كل من سمع ذلك تصديقه بإخبار الأول، ولهذا أخبر التنزيل عن مثل هذه الحالة على لسان عيسى عليه السلام: (بِرَسُولٍ يَأْتِي مِنْ بَعْدِي اسْمُهُ أَحْمَدُ) [الصف: 6] وعلى لسان موسى عليه السلام: (النَّبِيَّ الْأُمِّيَّ الَّذِي يَجِدُونَهُ مَكْتُوبًا عِنْدَهُمْ فِي التَّوْرَاةِ وَالْإِنْجِيلِ) [الأعراف: 157] الآية، وعلى لسان الخليل عليه السلام: (رَبَّنَا وَابْعَثْ فِيهِمْ رَسُولًا) [البقرة: 129] الآية، وأماراته في التوراة والإنجيل أكثر من أن تحصى، ولقد كان لموسى عليه السلام بيت صور؛ أعني صور الأنبياء والأولياء عليه السلام يدخله فيطالع الصور كل سبت، فلو لم يظهر النبي معجزة قط كان ما مضى من الدلائل كافيا له، فلهذا اقتصرت معجزاته على إظهار الأمر للأميين من العرب دون أهل الكتاب من اليهود والنصارى، فإنهم كانوا محجوبين بما ثبت عندهم من الأخبار عن الصادقين.
Believing him is incumbent upon everyone who comes after them. And if one whose truthfulness has been established by some evidence reports about another truthful person who succeeds him, it is obligatory to affirm him. Similarly, the report of every truthful one is a glad tiding for those after him, and an announcement to creation through signs in his creation, form, speech, and action; it is obligatory upon everyone who hears that to affirm him based on the report of the first. Thus the Revelation reported such a situation on the tongue of Jesus, peace be upon him: 'a messenger who will come after me, whose name is Ahmad' (Surah al-Saff, 6), and on the tongue of Moses, peace be upon him: 'the unlettered prophet whom they find written with them in the Torah and the Gospel' (Surah al-A'raf, 157) the verse, and on the tongue of Abraham, peace be upon him: 'Our Lord, and raise among them a messenger' (Surah al-Baqarah, 129) the verse. And his signs in the Torah and Gospel are too numerous to count. And Moses, peace be upon him, had a house of images—that is, images of the prophets and saints—which he would enter and examine every Sabbath. So even if the prophet had never manifested a miracle, the previous evidences would have been sufficient for him. For this reason his miracles were limited to making the matter evident to the unlettered Arabs, not to the People of the Book from the Jews and Christians, for they were already convinced by what had been established with them from the reports of the truthful ones.
Source pages p. 440

Commentary
This passage argues that the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him) is confirmed by prior prophecies and scriptural descriptions. The author states that if a person whose truthfulness is established (e.g., a previous prophet) reports about a later truthful person (a future prophet), then it is obligatory to believe in that later prophet. This principle is applied to Muhammad: previous prophets like Jesus, Moses, and Abraham gave glad tidings and descriptions of him. The author cites Quranic verses where Jesus foretells a messenger named Ahmad, where Moses mentions a prophet described in the Torah and Gospel, and where Abraham prays for a messenger to be raised. He then notes that Moses even had a house with images of prophets, implying he would recognize the coming prophet. The argument concludes that because the People of the Book already had sufficient scriptural evidence, Muhammad's miracles were directed primarily at the polytheistic Arabs who lacked such prior testimony.

Proof of Prophethood: Necessary Knowledge from Miracles
Distinguishing whether the knowledge from miracles is immediate or theoretical, with both paths leading to certainty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the occurrence of a miracle at the hands of a claimant to prophethood yields necessary knowledge of his truthfulness, whether through circumstantial evidence or the argument from specification.

Core Idea
Miracles provide immediate necessary knowledge, not mere theoretical reasoning.

The previous question challenged whether the proof of prophethood is certain. Imam Shahrastani now answers by showing that the knowledge derived from miracles is either immediate or theoretical, but in either case it is necessary and certain. He distinguishes two approaches: the first based on circumstantial evidence, the second on the logic of specification. Both lead to the same conclusion: after witnessing a miracle, denial is mere obstinacy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Let the author's argument unfold naturally.
Pay attention to the two key terms: qara'in al-ahwal and dilalat al-takhsis.
2
Understand the two approaches
Identify the two ways the author says knowledge of prophethood can be obtained: through circumstantial evidence (qara'in al-ahwal) and through specification (dilalat al-takhsis). Notice how each leads to necessary knowledge.
3
Analyze the logical core
Focus on the statement: a challenger is either truthful or lying; it is impossible that he is lying because of the miracle. This is the heart of the argument for necessary knowledge.
The conjunction of miracle, claim, and absence of counter-miracle produces certainty.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The author ends by saying that the disputant's denial does not remove the necessity; after the miracle, denial is mere obstinacy. Consider why this is a powerful response to skeptics.
This shows that the knowledge is not based on subjective acceptance but on objective evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الجواب عن السؤال السادس نقول: كل علم نظري لا بد وأن يستند إلى علم ضروري، ولكن الضروري ربما يكون بعيد المبدأ، وإنما يستند إليه النظري بعد نظريات كثيرة، وربما يكون قريب المبدأ فيستند إليه في أول المرتبة، والعلم بصدق النبوات إن عددناه من جنس العلوم الحاصلة بقرائن الأحوال فهو في أول المرتبة يصل إليه، فيقال: هذا المتحدي إما أن يكون صادقًا، وإما أن يكون كاذبًا، وبطل أن يكون كاذبًا لحصول الخارق للعادة على يده وعلى وفق دعواه من غير أن يعارضه معارض، واقتران هذه المعاني مما يستعقب علمًا ضروريًا بصدقه، فيدعي الضرورة هاهنا لا في أول الدعوى، وإن عددناه من جنس العلوم الحاصلة بوجه دليل التخصيص بالتصديق، فالعلم الحاصل به كالعلم الحاصل بكونه مريدًا فإن التخصيص يدل على أنه مريد، وهذا التخصيص بعينه يدل على أنه مريد، هذا المراد بعينه، وكون المنازع على رأس الإنكار لا يدفع الضرورة الواقعة في العلم، فإنه بعد ظهور الآية معاند عنادا ظاهرا.
As for the answer to the sixth question, we say: every theoretical knowledge must necessarily be based on necessary knowledge, but the necessary may be remote in origin, and the theoretical may be based upon it only after many theoretical steps, and it may be close in origin and thus based upon it at the first stage. The knowledge of the truthfulness of prophecies—if we count it among the type of knowledge obtained through circumstantial evidence (qara'in al-ahwal)—then it is reached at the first stage. So it is said: this challenger is either truthful or lying. And it is impossible that he is lying because a miracle (al-khariq lil-'adah) occurs at his hand in accordance with his claim without any counter-miracle opposing it. The conjunction of these meanings necessitates a necessary knowledge of his truthfulness. Thus he claims necessity here, not at the beginning of the claim. And if we count it among the type of knowledge obtained through the aspect of the indication of specification (dilalat al-takhsis) to belief, then the knowledge obtained through it is like the knowledge that he is willing (murid), for specification indicates that he is willing, and this very specification indicates that he is willing, this very intended meaning. And the fact that the disputant persists in denial does not repel the necessity that occurs in knowledge, for after the manifestation of the miracle he is clearly obstinate.
Source pages p. 440

Commentary
This passage provides the answer to the sixth question (likely about whether the proof of prophethood is necessary or theoretical knowledge). The author explains that all theoretical knowledge must ultimately rest on necessary knowledge, though the necessary basis may be near or far. He then considers two ways of understanding the knowledge of a prophet's truthfulness. First, if we regard it as arising from circumstantial evidence (qara'in al-ahwal), then the reasoning is immediate: a challenger claims prophethood, and if a miracle occurs at his hands consistent with his claim and without any opposing miracle, then it is impossible he is lying, so the knowledge of his truthfulness is necessary. This necessity arises not at the first moment of the claim but after the miraculous event. Second, if we regard it as arising from the indication of specification (dilalat al-takhsis)—analogous to how we know God is willing (murid) through specific actions—then the knowledge is similarly necessary. The author concludes that even if an opponent continues to deny, that does not remove the necessity of the knowledge; after the miracle, his denial is mere obstinacy.

Key Terms
علم نظري
علم ضروري
الخارق للعادة
قرائن الأحوال
دليل التخصيص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the proof of prophethood is purely theoretical and based on probability.
Correction: The author insists that the knowledge from miracles is necessary, not theoretical. The miracle itself, with the claim and absence of counter-miracle, makes lying impossible, producing immediate certainty.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what makes the knowledge of the prophet's truthfulness necessary?
A) The prophet's good character and moral teachings.
B) The occurrence of a miracle at his hands in accordance with his claim, without any counter-miracle.
C) The majority of people believing in him.
D) The logical impossibility of a liar performing a miracle.

Key Takeaway
A miracle accompanying a prophetic claim provides necessary knowledge of the claimant's truthfulness, not merely theoretical probability.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The author says that obstinate denial does not negate the necessity of knowledge. Is there an area of your faith where you have been stubborn, refusing to accept a clear truth because it would require a change in your life? Will you commit to surrendering that stubbornness today?
?
If you realized that the proof of prophethood is as clear as knowing that a person is willing based on their actions, would your relationship with the Prophet be different? What concrete step will you take this week to act on that certainty?

Prophethood Requires Prior Establishment of God as Commander
Establishing that prophethood requires first proving God is a commander.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the possibility of prophethood depends on first establishing that God is a commander and prohibitor.

Core Idea
Prophethood only makes sense if God is a commander.

The author begins by laying down a crucial prerequisite: before we can accept any prophet, we must first accept that God issues commands and prohibitions. Without this, prophethood has no logical foundation. This lesson unpacks that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the opening statement slowly. Notice the conditional logic: 'only after establishing that God is a commander...'
The Arabic uses 'إنما يمكن إثباتها بعد إثبات'.
2
Identify the logical prerequisite
The author says that whoever does not establish God as commander cannot establish prophethood. Ask yourself: why is this step necessary?
Think about what a prophet does: he conveys commands.
3
Understand the first command to the prophet
The passage then states the first command that God directs to His servants: it is to the messenger to call to tawhid. This shows the content of the prophetic message.
The call to tawhid is central.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن النبوة والرسالة إنما يمكن إثباتها بعد إثبات كون الباري تعالى آمراً ناهيا مكلفا واجب الطاعة، ومن لم يثبت لكونه آمرا ناهيا لم يمكنه إثبات النبوة، وأول أمر يتوجه منه تعالى على عباده فإنما يتوجه أولا على رسوله بالدعوة إلى التوحيد بأنه لا إله غيره؛ أي لا خالق ولا آمر غيره على عباده باستماع دعوته، والنظر في معجزته. والنبي يصح أولا صدقه في جميع أقواله، ثم يؤدي رسالته، ولا يتصور نبي قط إلا وأن تكون آية الصدق معه؛ لأن حقيقة النبوة هو صدق القول مع ثبوت الآية، فلو قدر نبي خاليًا عن الآية فكأنه لا نبوة له بعد، لكن الآيات قد تكون آيات مخصوصة على كل مسألة وقول يدعي ذلك، وذلك مثل دلالته على التوحيد بأن الإله واحد في خلقه وأمره لا شريك له.
Know that prophethood and messengerhood can only be established after establishing that the Most High Creator is a commander, a prohibitor, a giver of obligations, deserving of obedience. And whoever does not establish that He is a commander and prohibitor cannot establish prophethood. And the first command that proceeds from Him, Most High, to His servants is directed first to His messenger: the call to tawhid, that there is no god but Him—i.e., no creator and no commander other than Him, upon His servants to listen to his call and to reflect on his miracle. And the prophet is first verified as truthful in all his statements, then he delivers his message. And a prophet is never conceived except that the sign of truthfulness is with him, because the reality of prophethood is truthfulness of speech together with the establishment of the miracle. So if a prophet were supposed devoid of the miracle, it would be as if he has no prophethood at all. But miracles may be specific to each issue and statement that he claims, such as his indication of tawhid that the deity is one in His creation and command, no partner with Him.

Commentary
This passage deals with the prerequisites for proving prophethood. The author states that prophethood can only be established after first establishing that God is a commander and prohibitor who obligates and deserves obedience. Without establishing that God issues commands, one cannot logically prove the need for prophets. The first command God directs to His servants is to His messenger, calling to tawhid—that there is no god but Him, i.e., no creator and no commander besides Him—and to listen to the messenger and reflect on his miracle. The author then defines the nature of a prophet: he is first verified as truthful in all his words, then he delivers his message. The essence of prophethood (haqiqat al-nubuwwa) is truthfulness of speech combined with the establishment of a miracle. Without a miracle, there is no prophethood. However, miracles are specific to each claim and issue, e.g., the miracle that indicates tawhid, showing that God is one in creation and command, with no partner.

Prophethood logically depends on the prior recognition of God as a commander who issues obligations.

The Reality of Prophethood: Truthfulness and Miracles
Defining prophethood as truthful speech plus miracle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the essence of prophethood is truthfulness of speech combined with a confirming miracle.

Core Idea
No prophet without a miracle; miracle is constitutive of prophethood.

After establishing the prerequisite of God as commander, the author now defines what makes a prophet a prophet. He explains that a prophet is first verified as truthful, and then delivers his message. But crucially, the reality of prophethood consists of truthful speech plus a miracle. Without a miracle, there is no prophethood. This lesson explores that definition.
