The Miracle Yields Necessary Knowledge of Truthfulness
Al-Shahrastani proves that a miracle yields necessary knowledge of a prophet's truthfulness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a miracle, when performed in accordance with a prophetic claim, produces necessary knowledge of the prophet's truthfulness, and why this knowledge is analogous to the knowledge of God's will derived from specification.

Core Idea
A miracle matching a claim yields certain, not probable, knowledge of truthfulness.

In this passage from Nihayat al-Aqdam, al-Shahrastani presents a concise argument for the epistemic force of miracles. He asserts that when a miracle occurs on the hand of a claimant in accordance with his claim, without any counter-miracle, the conjunction of these factors necessarily produces certain knowledge ('ilm daruri) of his truthfulness. He compares this to the proof of specification (dalil al-takhsis) by which we know God's will, and he addresses the objection that a persistent denier might still reject the miracle. Read the passage carefully to grasp the logical structure.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to get an overall sense. Notice the key terms: خارق العادة (miracle), علم ضروري (necessary knowledge), دليل التخصيص (proof of specification).
2
Identify the core argument
The author states that it is invalid for a miracle-performer to be a liar because the conjunction of miracle and claim entails necessary knowledge. Identify the three conditions mentioned: miracle occurs, on his hand, in accordance with claim, no opposition.
3
Understand the analogy
The author compares this knowledge to the knowledge of God's will obtained through specification. How does this analogy strengthen the argument? Why is specification a valid comparison?
4
Address the objection
The author responds to the potential objection that a denier might still be unconvinced. What is his reply? How does he refute the possibility of genuine doubt after a manifest miracle?
5
Reflect on the necessity
The author emphasizes that necessity (darura) is claimed at the moment of the miracle, not at the initial claim. Why is this distinction important?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبطل أن يكون كاذبا لحصول الخارق للعادة على يده وعلى وفق دعواه من غير أن يعارضه معارض، واقتران هذه المعاني مما يستعقب علمًا ضروريًا بصدقه، فيدعي الضرورة هاهنا لا في أول الدعوى، وإن عددناه من جنس العلوم الحاصلة بوجه دليل التخصيص بالتصديق، فالعلم الحاصل به كالعلم الحاصل بكونه مريدا فإن التخصيص يدل على أنه مريد، وهذا التخصيص بعينه يدل على أنه مريد، هذا المراد بعينه، وكون المنازع على رأس الإنكار لا يدفع الضرورة الواقعة في العلم، فإنه بعد ظهور الآية معاند عنادا ظاهرا.
And it is invalid for him to be a liar because of the occurrence of the miraculous (al-khariq lil-'ada) on his hand and in accordance with his claim without anyone opposing him, and the conjunction of these meanings entails necessary knowledge ('ilm daruri) of his truthfulness. So necessity (darura) is claimed here, not at the beginning of the claim. And if we count it as a type of knowledge obtained by way of the proof of specification (dalil al-takhsis) for confirmation, then the knowledge obtained by it is like the knowledge obtained that He is willing (murid); for specification indicates that He is willing; this very specification indicates that He is willing, this intended meaning itself. And the opponent's persistence in denial does not repel the necessity occurring in knowledge, for after the manifestation of the miracle (aya), he is obstinate with manifest obstinacy.
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This passage is a proof that the occurrence of a miracle establishes necessary knowledge (ilm daruri) of a prophet's truthfulness. The author argues that a miracle performed on the hand of someone claiming prophethood, in accordance with his claim, and without opposition, necessarily produces certain knowledge that he is truthful. This necessity (darura) is claimed at the moment of the miracle, not at the initial claim. He compares this knowledge to the knowledge of God's will derived from the proof of specification (takhsis): just as specific patterns in creation indicate that God is willing, the conjunction of miracle and claim directly indicates truthfulness. The objection that a denier might still reject the miracle is refuted: once the miracle is manifest, denial is merely obstinacy, not a counterargument.

Key Terms
خارق العادة (al-khariq lil-'ada)
علم ضروري ('ilm daruri)
دليل التخصيص (dalil al-takhsis)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Miracles only produce probable or persuasive knowledge, not certain knowledge
Correction: The passage argues that the conjunction of miracle and claim yields necessary, certain knowledge.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the conjunction of a miracle and a claim yield necessary knowledge?
A) Because the miracle is always of a type that cannot be replicated
B) Because the conjunction of miracle and claim is analogous to the proof of specification (takhsis) for God's will
C) Because the opponent's denial proves the claim false
D) Because the prophet's character is already known to be good

Key Takeaway
A miracle performed in accordance with a claim, without opposition, yields necessary knowledge of the prophet's truthfulness, analogous to the certainty of specification.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Prophet's miracle produced necessary knowledge, do you actually possess that necessary certainty in your heart? Or is your belief merely inherited, without the direct experience of that proof?
?
When you encounter people who deny the prophethood despite clear evidence, do you recognize that their denial is obstinacy (عناد) rather than intellectual doubt? How does that change your response to them?
?
The knowledge of the Prophet's truthfulness is compared to the knowledge that God is willing. Do you live as if you have that same level of certainty? If not, what is holding you back from embracing it fully?

Prerequisites for Prophethood and Its Definition
Al-Shahrastani states the prerequisites for proving prophethood and defines it as truthfulness with a miracle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical prerequisites for establishing prophethood and its essential definition as truthful speech accompanied by a miracle.

Core Idea
Prophethood is defined by truthful speech confirmed by a miracle.

Before we can discuss prophethood, we must first establish that God is a commanding and prohibiting being. Al-Shahrastani outlines this necessary groundwork and then provides a precise definition of what makes a prophet. This passage clarifies that a miracle is not merely a sign but an integral part of the definition of prophethood itself.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp the logical flow from prerequisite to definition.
2
Identify the prerequisites
Note the first condition: that God is a Commander and Prohibitor. Why is this necessary?
Without it, the concept of a messenger is meaningless.
3
Understand the definition
The passage states the reality of prophethood is truthfulness of speech with a miracle. This is the core idea.
4
Consider the implications
What if a prophet had no miracle? The passage says it would be as if he had no prophethood. Reflect on this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن النبوة والرسالة إنما يمكن إثباتها بعد إثبات كون الباري تعالى آمراً ناهيا مكلفا واجب الطاعة، ومن لم يثبت لكونه أمرًا ناهيا لم يمكنه إثبات النبوة، وأول أمر يتوجه منه تعالى على عباده فإنما يتوجه أولا على رسوله بالدعوة إلى التوحيد بأنه لا إله غيره؛ أي لا خالق ولا آمر غيره على عباده باستماع دعوته، والنظر في معجزته والنبي يصح أولا صدقه في جميع أقواله، ثم يؤدي رسالته، ولا يتصور نبي قط إلا وأن تكون آية الصدق معه؛ لأن حقيقة النبوة هو صدق القول مع ثبوت الآية، فلو قدر نبي خاليًا عن الآية فكأنه لا نبوة له بعد.
Know that prophethood (nubuwwa) and messengerhood (risala) can only be established after establishing that the Exalted Creator is a commander (amir), a prohibitor (nahi), a giver of obligation (mukallif), and worthy of obedience (wajib al-ta'a). And whoever does not establish that He is a commander and prohibitor cannot establish prophethood. And the first command that proceeds from Him Almighty to His servants proceeds first to His messenger by calling to tawhid (al-tawhid), that there is no god but Him, i.e., no creator and no commander other than Him, upon His servants to listen to his call and to consider his miracle (mu'jiza). And the prophet is first verified as truthful in all his statements, then he delivers his message. And there is never any prophet except that a sign of truthfulness (ayat al-sidq) is with him, because the reality (haqiqa) of prophethood is truthfulness of speech (sidq al-qawl) with the confirmation of a miracle (thubut al-aya). So if a prophet were supposed devoid of a miracle, it would be as if he has no prophethood after that.
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This passage presents the logical prerequisites for establishing prophethood. First, one must establish that God is a Commander and Prohibitor who obligates and is to be obeyed, because prophethood involves conveying commands and prohibitions. Without this divine attribute, the concept of a messenger is meaningless. Then it describes the first divine command to the messenger: to call people to tawhid—that there is no creator or commander besides God. People must listen to him and examine his miracle. The prophet's truthfulness is verified first, then he delivers his message. The core definition: the reality of prophethood is truthful speech accompanied by a confirming miracle. A supposed prophet without a miracle would have no prophethood; miracles are inseparable.

Key Terms
نبوة (nubuwwa)
آية الصدق (ayat al-sidq)
توحيد (tawhid)

A) Having a large number of followers
B) Being able to perform any miracle
C) Truthfulness of speech with the confirmation of a miracle
D) Being descended from a prophetic lineage

Key Takeaway
The reality of prophethood is truthful speech accompanied by a confirming miracle, without which prophethood is invalid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Prophetic Infallibility: Minor Sins and Tark al-Awla
Al-Shahrastani discusses that prophets are protected from minor sins as well, and introduces tark al-awla.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that prophets are protected from both major and minor sins, and that only tark al-awla (leaving the preferable) is permissible for them, though even that carries great weight.

Core Idea
Prophets are guarded from all sins; only leaving the preferable counts as a shortcoming.

This passage from Al-Shahrastani's Nihayat al-Aqdam tackles a crucial question: Are prophets protected from minor sins as well as major ones? The author affirms that they are, and introduces the concept of 'tark al-awla' — leaving the more virtuous choice — as the only permissible type of shortcoming for prophets. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this position and the deeper spiritual principle it reveals.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully to grasp the main argument.
Pay attention to the phrase 'al-asahh' (the most correct view) — it signals the author's preferred position.
2
Understand the proof for minor sins
Notice how the author argues that repeated minor sins become major sins, and uses the analogy of intoxicants to support the prohibition of small amounts.
This logical argument strengthens the case for infallibility from all sins.
3
Define tark al-awla
Identify what the author considers permissible for prophets: leaving the preferable in cases where two options are equally permissible or equally forbidden.
This is not a sin but a lesser choice.
4
Grasp the strictness and the secret
Understand that even tark al-awla is treated with extreme strictness for prophets, and that every slip contains a great secret.
The quote 'hasanat al-abrar sayyi'at al-muqarrabin' illustrates the high standard.
5
Apply the lesson
Reflect on the advice to look beyond outward appearances to inner realities when evaluating prophetic actions.
This discourages simplistic judgments.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والأصح أنهم معصومون عن الصغائر عصمتهم عن الكبائر، فإن الصغائر إذا توالت صارت بالاتفاق كبائر، وما أسكر كثيره فقليله حرام، لكن المجوز عليهم عقلا وشرعا مثل ترك الأولى من الأمرين المتقابلين جوازا وجوازا وحظرًا وحظرًا، ولكن التشديد عليهم في ذلك القدر يوازي التشديد على غيرهم في كبائر الأمور، وحسنات الأبرار سيئات المقربين وتحت كل زلة يجري عليهم سر عظيم، فلا تلتفت إلى ظواهر الأحوال، وانظر إلى سرائر المآل.
And the most correct view (al-asahh) is that they are protected (ma'sumun) from minor sins (sagha'ir) just as they are protected from major sins (kaba'ir). For minor sins if repeated become major sins by consensus. And whatever intoxicates in large quantity, a little of it is forbidden (haram). But what is permissible (mujawwaz) for them, rationally and legally, is like leaving the preferable (tark al-awla) from two opposing matters: permissible and permissible, or forbidden and forbidden. But the strictness (tashdid) upon them in that measure equals the strictness upon others in major sins. And the good deeds of the righteous (hasanat al-abrar) are the evil deeds of those brought near (sayyi'at al-muqarrabin). And under every slip (zalla) a great secret (sirr 'azim) runs for them. So do not pay attention to the outward appearances of states (zawahir al-ahwal), but look at the inner secrets of the end (sara'ir al-ma'al).
Source pages p. 442

Commentary
This passage addresses the extent of prophetic infallibility ('isma). The author declares that the most correct position is that prophets are protected from minor sins (sagha'ir) just as they are from major sins (kaba'ir). A proof is given: repeated minor sins become major sins by consensus. The analogy of intoxicants is used: if a large amount is forbidden, a small amount is also forbidden. However, the author clarifies that what is rationally and legally permissible for prophets is not sin but rather 'leaving the preferable' (tark al-awla)—choosing a permissible option when a more virtuous one was available. Even this is treated with extreme strictness, comparable to major sins in others. The author then quotes a saying: 'The good deeds of the righteous are the evil deeds of those brought near (God),' meaning that what is virtuous for ordinary people is considered a shortcoming for prophets. With every slip, there is a profound secret (sirr 'azim) for them. The conclusion advises looking beyond outward appearances to the inner realities.

Key Terms
صغائر (sagha'ir)
كبائر (kaba'ir)
ترك الأولى (tark al-awla)
سر (sirr)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That prophets can commit minor sins without consequence.
Correction: The passage asserts that prophets are protected from all sins, major and minor, and only tark al-awla is possible, which is not a sin but a lesser choice.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the most correct view (al-asahh) regarding prophetic infallibility?
A) Prophets are only protected from major sins
B) Prophets are protected from both major and minor sins
C) Prophets are allowed to commit minor sins
D) Prophets are not protected from any sins

Key Takeaway
Prophets are protected from all sins, and only leaving the preferable (tark al-awla) is permissible, but even that carries great weight and should not be judged by outward appearances.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage teaches that what is good for ordinary people can be a shortcoming for the elite. In your life, where do you settle for the permissible (halal) but not the best, while knowing you could do more? What specific area can you commit to raising your standard this week, and how will you hold yourself accountable?
?
You are told not to judge by outward appearances but to look at the inner secrets. Think of a time when you quickly judged someone's action as wrong. How might that action have contained a 'great secret' or wisdom you failed to see? Will you repent for that judgment and ask Allah to help you look deeper next time?
?
If prophets faced extreme strictness for merely leaving the preferable, what does that imply about your own negligence regarding major sins? How does this truth stir your heart to take your repentance more seriously and to increase your taqwa starting today?

Prophetic Miracles and Infallibility
The author explains that miracles indicate truthfulness and that prophets are infallible.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that prophetic miracles serve as general proofs of a prophet's truthfulness, which entails their infallibility from both major and minor sins, and that the omission of the better (tark al-awlā) is treated with exceptional strictness.

Core Idea
Prophetic infallibility covers major and minor sins, and even omitting the better is treated with severity.

This passage from a classical theological work establishes the link between prophetic miracles and the doctrine of infallibility (ʿiṣma). The author argues that miracles prove a prophet's truthfulness in all matters, which would be undermined if the prophet could sin. He then clarifies the extent of this infallibility, asserting that it covers both major and minor sins, and introduces the subtle concept of 'tark al-awlā'—the omission of a better action—as a category that is permissible for prophets yet carries a stringent accountability.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and Translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage carefully, then read the literal translation. Let the author's own wording and flow settle in before you analyse.
Notice the dense, compact style typical of classical kalām works.
2
Identify the Link Between Miracles and Infallibility
The author states that miracles (āyāt) are general signs proving the prophet's truthfulness in all words and actions. Ask yourself: why would this proof require infallibility?
The answer: if the prophet could lie or sin, the miracle would lose its evidentiary force.
3
Understand the Extent of Infallibility
The passage declares that the more correct view (al-aṣaḥḥ) is that prophets are infallible from minor sins just as from major sins. Note the reasoning: minor sins repeated become major, and the principle 'whatever much intoxicates, a little is forbidden'.
This differs from some views that allowed minor sins.
4
Reflect on Tark al-Awlā
The author allows prophets to omit the better (tark al-awlā) when choosing between two equal options, but emphasises that the strictness on them equals that on others for major sins. Consider why this strictness highlights their high rank.
The phrase 'good deeds of the righteous are the evil deeds of those brought near' illustrates the elevated standard.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد تكون الآيات عامة تدل على صدق قوله في جميع أقواله وأحواله، وتلك الآيات قد تكون من جنس الأقوال كآيات الكتاب وقد تكون من جنس الأفعال كآيات الإحياء وقلب الجماد حيوانًا، وبالجملة فدلالة الصدق لا تنفك عن حالة ومقالة طرفة عين، وذلك هو المعنى بالعصمة الواجبة للأنبياء عليهم السلام؛ لأن العصمة لو ارتفعت بطلت الدلالة وتناقضت الدعوى، خصوصا فيما أرسلوا به إليهم وكلف الناس تصديقه في أقواله ومتابعته في أفعاله، والأصح أنهم معصومون عن الصغائر عصمتهم عن الكبائر، فإن الصغائر إذا توالت صارت بالاتفاق كبائر، وما أسكر كثيره فقليله حرام، لكن المجوز عليهم عقلا وشرعا مثل ترك الأولى من الأمرين المتقابلين جوازا وجوازا وحظرًا وحظرًا، ولكن التشديد عليهم في ذلك القدر يوازي التشديد على غيرهم في كبائر الأمور، وحسنات الأبرار سيئات المقربين وتحت كل زلة يجري عليهم سر عظيم، فلا تلتفت إلى ظواهر الأحوال، وانظر إلى سرائر المآل.
And the signs (āyāt) may be general, indicating the truthfulness of his speech in all his words and states. And those signs may be of the kind of words, like the verses of the Book, and may be of the kind of actions, like the signs of bringing to life and turning an inanimate object into an animal. And in sum, the indication of truthfulness is not separated from a state and a statement for the blink of an eye. And that is the meaning of the infallibility (ʿiṣma) obligatory for the prophets, peace be upon them; because if infallibility were removed, the indication would become invalid and the claim would be contradictory, especially in what they were sent with to them and the people are required to believe in his words and follow his actions. And the more correct view is that they are infallible from minor sins just as they are infallible from major sins, for minor sins if they are repeated become major sins by agreement. And whatever much of it intoxicates, a little of it is forbidden. But that which is permissible for them rationally and legally is like omitting the better (tark al-awlā) from two opposing matters: permissible and permissible, and forbidden and forbidden. But the strictness upon them in that amount is equivalent to the strictness upon others in major matters. And the good deeds of the righteous are the evil deeds of those brought near. And under every slip runs a great secret for them. So do not pay attention to the outward appearances of states, but look to the inner secrets of the outcome.
Source pages p. 442

Commentary
This passage discusses the nature of prophetic miracles and the doctrine of prophetic infallibility (ʿiṣma). The author begins by stating that signs (āyāt) can be general, proving the truthfulness of the prophet in all his words and actions. These signs can be verbal, like the verses of the Quran, or physical, like miracles of reviving the dead or turning inanimate objects into animals. The indication of truthfulness is perpetual, never leaving the prophet even for an instant. This is the meaning of infallibility (ʿiṣma) that is obligatory for prophets. If infallibility were lifted, the evidence for their truthfulness would collapse and the claim to prophethood would become contradictory, especially concerning the message they were sent with, which people are obliged to believe and follow. The author then states the more correct position (al-aṣaḥḥ) that prophets are protected from minor sins just as they are from major sins. The reason given is that minor sins, if repeated, become major sins by consensus. Additionally, the principle is cited: 'Whatever much of which intoxicates, a little of it is forbidden.' However, the author notes that what is permissible for prophets rationally and legally is the omission of the better action (tark al-awlā) when choosing between two permissible or two forbidden acts. But the strictness upon them in such matters is equivalent to the strictness upon ordinary people in major sins. The author then adds that 'the good deeds of the righteous are the evil deeds of those brought near', indicating the high standard for prophets. Beneath every slip of a prophet there is a great secret, so one should not judge by outward appearances but look to the inner secrets of the outcome.

عصمة
ترك الأولى
صغائر
كبائر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that prophets can commit minor sins without consequence, as long as they repent.
Correction: The author explicitly states that the more correct view is that prophets are infallible from minor sins just as from major sins. He argues that minor sins, if repeated, become major, and uses the principle that if the much of something is forbidden, the little is also forbidden.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the more correct view (الأصح) regarding prophetic infallibility?
A) Prophets are infallible only from major sins.
B) Prophets are infallible from both major and minor sins.
C) Prophets are infallible only in matters of delivering the message.
D) Prophets are not infallible from minor sins if they repent.

Key Takeaway
Prophetic infallibility is comprehensive, covering both major and minor sins, and even the omission of the better is treated with strictness, reflecting the high status of prophets.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The author warns not to judge by outward appearances but to look for inner secrets. When you see a believer committing what you think is a mistake, do you immediately assume the worst? How can you train yourself to see the hidden wisdom and good intentions first—even when it's hard?
?
If even the best of creation are held to such a high standard that omitting a better action is treated like a major sin, where in your life are you settling for 'good enough' when you could choose the best for Allah? Name one specific area where you need to raise your standard today.
?
The good deeds of the righteous are considered minor failures for those close to Allah. Does this humble you or make you complacent? What 'evil deeds' (in the form of missed opportunities for closeness) are you tolerating in your worship and character right now?

The Twentieth Principle: Topics Covered
The author enumerates the topics of the twentieth principle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scope of the twentieth principle and the key topics it addresses, from proving prophethood to discussing eschatology and abrogation.

Core Idea
The twentieth principle covers a wide range of theological topics centered on Muhammad's prophethood.

The author introduces the twentieth principle by enumerating the core topics it will address. This overview sets the stage for the detailed arguments that follow. Rather than entering into proofs immediately, the author lists the subjects, giving the reader a roadmap of the discussion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage listing topics
Read the first part of the passage where the author lists the many topics of the twentieth principle. Notice how each topic is introduced.
2
Identify the main categories
The topics include: prophethood and miracles, samiyyat (eschatological matters), faith and disbelief, imamate, abrogation, and finality. Group them mentally.
These are all part of samiyyat (matters heard from revelation).
3
Understand the purpose
This list is not exhaustive but shows the comprehensive nature of the principle. It prepares the reader for the arguments that establish these doctrines.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القاعدة العشرون في إثبات نبوة نبينا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم وبيان معجزاته ووجه دلالة الكتاب العزيز على صدقه، وجمل من الكلام في السمعيات من الأسماء والأحكام، وحقيقة الإيمان والكفر، والقول في التكفير والتضليل، وبيان سؤال القبر والحشر والبعث والميزان والحساب والحوض والشفاعة والصراط والجنة والنار، وإثبات الإمامة، وبيان كرامة الأولياء من الأمة، وبيان جواز النسخ في الشرائع، وأن هذه الشريعة ناسخة للشرائع كلها، وأن محمدًا المصطفى صلى الله عليه وسلم خاتم الأنبياء وبه ختم الكتاب، وإذا حققنا القول في النبوات وبيان صدقهم بالمعجزات، فالأنبياء عليهم السلام ممن ورد اسمه في الكتاب ومن لم يرد واجبو الطاعة ويجب على كل مكلف الإيمان بالله وملائكته وكتبه ورسله، وإنما ثبت صدق من تقدم على نبينا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم اسمًا فاسما وشخصا فشخصاً بما ظهر عليه من الآيات، وبما أخبر من ثبت صدقه عندنا، وإنما يتحقق ختم الأنبياء عندنا بخبر النبي الصادق عليه السلام، وبما أخبر القرآن أنه خاتم النبيين ومن أنكر نبوته من أهل الكتاب وغيرهم من المشركين فلا متمسك لهم إلا القول بإحالة النسخ والقدح في وجه المعجزة.
The twentieth principle: On establishing the prophethood of our Prophet Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, and explaining his miracles and the aspect of the evidence of the Mighty Book for his truthfulness, and a portion of speech on the matters heard (al-samʿiyyāt) concerning names and rulings, and the reality of faith and disbelief, and the statement on declaring someone an unbeliever (takfīr) and declaring someone misguided (taḍlīl), and explaining the questioning in the grave, the resurrection, the gathering, the balance, the reckoning, the Basin, the intercession, the Path, Paradise and Hellfire, and establishing the imamate, and explaining the miracle (karāma) of the saints (awliyāʾ) of the community, and explaining the permissibility of abrogation (naskh) in the laws, and that this Law (sharīʿa) abrogates all laws, and that Muḥammad the Chosen, may God bless him and grant him peace, is the Seal of the Prophets and with him the Book is sealed. And if we examine thoroughly the discourse on prophecies and the explanation of their truthfulness by miracles, then the prophets, peace be upon them, whether their names appear in the Book or not, are obligatory to obey, and it is incumbent upon every legally responsible person to believe in God, His angels, His books, and His messengers. And the truthfulness of those who came before our Prophet Muhammad, peace be upon him, is established only name by name and person by person by what appeared of signs from them, and by what the one whose truthfulness is established with us has informed. And the finality of the prophets is established with us only by the report of the truthful prophet, peace be upon him, and by what the Quran has informed that he is the Seal of the Prophets. And whoever denies his prophethood from the People of the Book and others among the polytheists has no recourse except the statement of the impossibility of abrogation and casting doubt on the aspect of the miracle.
Source pages p. 443

Commentary
This passage begins a new section titled 'The Twentieth Principle'. The author first lists the topics that will be covered in this principle, which include: proving the prophethood of Muhammad, his miracles, the evidence of the Quran, discussion of al-samʿiyyāt (matters heard from revelation) such as the names of God and rulings, the reality of faith and disbelief, the rulings on takfīr and taḍlīl, eschatological topics like the grave, resurrection, judgment, etc., the imamate, the miracles of saints, abrogation, the fact that Islam abrogates all previous laws, and that Muhammad is the Seal of the Prophets. After this enumeration, the author provides a key argument: When we thoroughly examine prophethood and the proof of prophets through miracles, we find that all prophets – those mentioned in the Quran and those not mentioned – are obligatory to obey. Every legally responsible person must believe in God, angels, books, and messengers. The truthfulness of earlier prophets is established in two ways: first, by the miracles that appeared from them; second, by the testimony of the one whose truthfulness is established for us – namely, Prophet Muhammad. Thus, the truthfulness of previous prophets is ultimately dependent on the truthfulness of Muhammad. Likewise, the finality of prophethood (that Muhammad is the last prophet) is established by the report of the truthful prophet himself and by the Quran's statement that he is the Seal of the Prophets. The author concludes that those who deny Muhammad's prophethood, whether from the People of the Book or polytheists, have no argument left except to claim the impossibility of abrogation or to cast doubt on the miracle (i.e., the Quran). This shows that the denial of prophethood stems from either rejection of abrogation or skepticism about the miracle.

Key Terms
القاعدة العشرون
السمعيات
تكفير
تضليل
خاتم النبيين
نسخ
معجزة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the twentieth principle only deals with prophethood.
Correction: It actually covers a wide range of topics including samiyyat, imamate, abrogation, and eschatology.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT listed as a topic of the twentieth principle in this passage?
A) The reality of faith and disbelief
B) The questioning in the grave
C) The proofs for the existence of God
D) The imamate

Key Takeaway
The twentieth principle is a comprehensive discussion covering prophethood, samiyyat, eschatology, imamate, abrogation, and finality of prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This principle covers a vast range of topics—from proofs of prophethood to the details of the afterlife. What area of your faith do you most neglect, and what would it look like for you to take it as seriously as the others listed here?
?
The list includes 'the reality of faith and disbelief.' Are you confident that your faith is more than inherited culture or routine? If you had to defend its reality before God, what evidence from your life would you present?
?
It ends by affirming that Muhammad is the Seal of the Prophets. In what ways do you still seek guidance from other sources—people, ideologies, or your own desires—rather than submitting fully to his message? What will you change today to make his authority final in your life?

Establishing the Prophethood and Finality of Muhammad
The author argues that the truth of all prophets depends on Muhammad's truthfulness, and finality is established by Quran and prophet.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the truthfulness of all prophets is ultimately based on Muhammad's prophethood and how the finality of prophethood is established through Quran and prophetic report.

Core Idea
Muhammad's truthfulness is the foundation for believing in all previous prophets.

After listing the topics, the author presents a crucial argument: the truth of earlier prophets is not independent but relies on the truthfulness of Muhammad, which is established by his miracles. Furthermore, the finality of prophethood is proven by the Quran and the prophet's own statement. This argument shows the central role of Muhammad in the entire prophetic tradition.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument carefully
Read the second part of the passage starting from 'وإذا حققنا'. Notice the conditional structure and the conclusion.
The author uses a logical chain.
2
Identify the two foundations
The truth of earlier prophets is based on two things: their own miracles and the testimony of Muhammad. Then finality is based on Muhammad's report and the Quran.
These are distinct proofs.
3
Reflect on the opponents' position
The author mentions that those who deny Muhammad have no argument except rejecting abrogation or doubting the miracle. Understand why these are the only options.

Correction: The author shows it relies on Muhammad's truthfulness, which is established by miracles.

Proof of Prophethood via the Quran's Eloquence
Shahrastani presents a four-level analogy to demonstrate the Quran's miraculous eloquence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four-level analogy that Shahrastani uses to prove that the Quran is a unique miracle, establishing the truthfulness of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him).

Core Idea
The Quran's eloquence is not just superior; it is outside the category of human speech entirely.

Shahrastani begins his proof of prophethood by focusing on the Quran itself. He argues that its eloquence is so unique that it must come from God. To make this point, he constructs a graded analogy starting from human speech in general, moving to Arabic, then to the Prophet's own speech, and finally to the Quran. This passage lays the foundation for the doctrine of i'jaz (inimitability).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Notice the repeated pattern of 'tamayyaza' (distinguished) and 'sharaf' (honor).
This passage is dense with Quranic and hadith quotations.
2
Identify the four levels of distinction
Find each level: (1) humans distinguished from animals by speech, (2) Arabic distinguished from other languages, (3) the Prophet's speech distinguished from Arabic, (4) the Quran distinguished from all speech including the Prophet's. Note how each level builds on the previous.
The fourth level is the climax: 'outside the category of the speech of the Arabs and also outside his words.'
3
Understand the role of divine honor
Each distinction is presented as a divine honor (sharaf/karama) with Quranic support. Recognize that this graded dignity points to the Quran's ultimate status.
Allah honors humans, Arabs, the Prophet, and finally the Quran itself.
4
Reflect on the proof for prophethood
Ask yourself: How does this analogy prove that Muhammad is a true prophet? The argument is that the Quran's eloquence is beyond human capacity, so it must be from Allah, confirming Muhammad's message.
This is the first part of a longer argument for prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أهل الحق : الدليل على صدق نبينا عليه السلام الكتاب الذي جاء به هدى للناس وبينات من الهدى والفرقان ووجه دلالته على صدقه من حيث لفظه البليغ ومعناه المبين فنقول : كما تميز نوع الإنسان عن أنواع الحيوانات بالنطق المعبر عن الفكر، وصار ذلك شرفا وكرامة له كما قال تعالى : وَلَقَدْ كَرَّمْنَا بَنِى ءَادَمَ ﴾ كذلك تميز لسان العرب ولغتهم من سائر الألسن واللغات بأسلوب آخر من عذوبة اللسان ورطوبة اللفظ وسهولة المخارج، والتعبير عن متن المعنى الدائر في الضمير بأوضح عبارة وأصح تفسير، وصار ذلك شرفًا وكرامة لهم كما قال تعالى : ( بِلِسَانٍ عَرَبِىٍّ مُّبِينٍ ). وكذلك تميز لسان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم من لسان العرب بأسلوب آخر من الفصاحة المبينة والبلاغة الفائقة والبراعة المطابقة لما في ضميره من المعاني المبينة والحقائق الرزينة، كما لا يخفى على من أنصف واعتبر واختبر كلماته واستبصر وصار ذلك شرفا وكرامة كما قال : ( لِتُبَيِّنَ لِلنَّاسِ مَا نُزِلَ إِلَيْهِمْ ﴾ ، وقال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: «أنا أفصح العرب، وأنا أفصح من نطق بالضاد». وكذلك تميز القرآن عن سائر كلماته بأسلوب آخر خارج عن جنس كلام العرب وعن كلماته أيضا، وبنوع آخر من الفصاحة والجزالة والنظم والبلاغة
The people of truth (Ahl al-Haqq) said: The proof of the truthfulness of our Prophet (peace be upon him) is the Book which he brought, a guidance for the people and clear proofs of guidance and criterion (al-Furqan). And the aspect of its indication of his truthfulness is in terms of its eloquent wording and its evident meaning. We say: Just as the human species is distinguished from the species of animals by speech which expresses thought, and that became an honor and dignity for him, as Allah the Exalted said: 'And We have honored the children of Adam' (17:70); similarly, the tongue of the Arabs and their language is distinguished from all other tongues and languages by another style of sweetness of tongue, moistness of expression, ease of articulation, and expression of the essence of meaning circulating in the conscience with the clearest expression and the most correct interpretation, and that became an honor and dignity for them, as Allah the Exalted said: 'In a clear Arabic tongue' (26:195). And likewise, the tongue of the Prophet (peace be upon him) is distinguished from the tongue of the Arabs by another style of manifest eloquence, surpassing rhetoric, and proficiency matching the manifest meanings and weighty realities in his conscience, as is not hidden from one who is fair, considers, tests his words, and gains insight, and that became an honor and dignity for him, as He said: 'So that you may make clear to the people what was sent down to them' (16:44), and the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'I am the most eloquent of the Arabs, and I am the most eloquent of all who spoke the Ḍād.' And likewise, the Qur'an is distinguished from all his [the Prophet's] words by another style outside the category of the speech of the Arabs and also outside his words, and by another type of eloquence, majesty, composition, and rhetoric.
Source pages p. 444

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of a proof for the truthfulness of Muhammad (saw) based on the Quran's eloquence. It is presented as the view of Ahl al-Haqq. The author states that the proof is the Quran itself, focusing on its eloquent wording and clear meaning. Then he constructs a four-level analogy to show the unique status of the Quran. First, humans are distinguished from animals by articulate speech (nutq), which is an honor (sharaf) as mentioned in the Quran. Second, the Arabic language is distinguished from other languages by its sweetness, ease, and clarity of expression, again honored by the Quran. Third, the Prophet's own speech is distinguished from ordinary Arabic by its supreme eloquence and rhetoric, as evidenced by his hadith. Fourth, the Quran is distinguished even from the Prophet's own words by being outside the category of Arabic speech entirely—it is a separate type of eloquence, majesty, composition, and rhetoric. This graded argument establishes the Quran as a unique miracle, proving the prophethood of Muhammad. The passage does not complete the argument but sets up the foundation for the doctrine of i'jaz (inimitability).

دلالة
فصاحة
بلاغة

لسان

Correction: The passage builds a graded analogy from human speech to the Quran, each level showing a greater distinction, with the final level declaring the Quran outside all human speech categories.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The Quran's eloquence is not merely superior Arabic; it is a different category of speech, proving its divine origin and the truth of Muhammad's prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The Prophet's own speech was the peak of Arab eloquence, yet the Quran is beyond even that. If you truly believed that every verse is not from this world, how would your heart respond to it right now? What would change in your daily life if you treated the Quran as literally otherworldly speech?
?
This passage builds an argument from honor: from humans to Arabs to the Prophet to the Quran. Where do you place the Quran in the hierarchy of your own attention and love? Is it at the top, or have you let something else occupy that place? Commit today: read one verse standing, facing the qibla, and ask yourself if you are hearing the words of your Creator.

The Qur'an's Uniqueness Through Stepwise Analogy
Juwayni's analogical argument for the Qur'an's inimitability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Juwayni uses a stepwise analogy to demonstrate that the Qur'an's eloquence surpasses all human speech, proving its divine origin.

Core Idea
The Qur'an's uniqueness is established by its superiority over each level of speech.

Juwayni begins his proof by showing that just as humans are distinguished from animals by speech, and Arabic from other languages, and the Prophet's speech from other Arabs, so the Qur'an is even beyond the Prophet's speech. This layered comparison prepares the listener to recognize the Qur'an's miraculous nature.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
2
Identify the four levels of distinction
The passage presents four levels: humans vs animals, Arabic vs other languages, Prophet's speech vs Arabs, and Qur'an vs Prophet's speech. List them and note how each level is contrasted.
3
Reflect on the analogy
Notice that each level builds on the previous. The Qur'an's distinction is even greater than the Prophet's over other Arabs. Ask yourself why this progression matters for proving prophethood.
4
Understand the conclusion
The passage ends by stating that the Qur'an is completely outside the genre of human speech. This sets up the challenge (tahaddi) in the next lesson.
The phrase 'outside the genre of Arab speech' is key.

الحيوانات بالنطق المعبر عن الفكر، وصار ذلك شرفا وكرامة له كما قال تعالى : وَلَقَدْ كَرَّمْنَا بَنِى ءَادَمَ كذلك تميز لسان العرب ولغتهم من سائر الألسن واللغات بأسلوب آخر من عذوبة اللسان ورطوبة اللفظ وسهولة المخارج، والتعبير عن متن المعنى الدائر في الضمير بأوضح عبارة وأصح تفسير، وصار ذلك شرفًا وكرامة لهم كما قال تعالى : بِلِسَانٍ عَرَينٍ مُّبِينٍ . وكذلك تميز لسان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم من لسان قال : لِتُبَيِّنَ لِلنَّاسِ مَا نُزِلَ إِلَيْهِمْ ، وقال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: «أنا أفصح العرب، وأنا أفصح من نطق بالضاد». وكذلك تميز القرآن عن سائر كلماته بأسلوب آخر خارج عن جنس كلام العرب وعن كلماته أيضا، وبنوع آخر من الفصاحة والجزالة والنظم والبلاغة ما لم تعهده العرب في نظمهم ونثرهم وسجعهم وشعرهم، بحيث لو قوبل أفصح كلماتهم بسورة واحدة من القرآن كان التفاوت بينهما أكثر من التفاوت بين لسان العرب وبين سائر الألسن، ولو خاير بين كلمات النبي نفسه وبين ما نزل عليه من الكتاب المهيمن على الكتب كلها كان الفرق بينهما فرق ما بين القدم والفرق، والصرف بينهما صرف ما بين الولاية والصرف، فعلم ضرورة وقطعًا أن الذي جاء به وحي يوحى إليه، وتنزيل ينزل عليه دلالة له على صدقه ومعجزة له على فصحاء العرب وبلغاء أهل اللسان وشعراء ذلك الزمان، فتحدى بذلك تحدي التعجيز عن الإتيان بمثله كتاباً وقرآنًا : قُلْ فَأْتُوا بِكِتَبٍ مِنْ عِندِ اللَّهِ هُوَ أَهْدَى مِنْهُمَا، ثم ثنى ذلك فقال : فأتوا بحديث مثله، ولما عجزوا عن الإتيان مثله نزل عن ذلك حين قال القوم : إنه افتراه، فقال: قُلْ فَأْتُوا بِعَشْرِ سُوَرٍ مِثْلِهِ مُفْتَرَيَت ونزل عن العشر إلى سورة مثله فقال تعالى : وَإِن كُنتُمْ فِي رَيْبٍ مِّمَّا نَزَّلْنَا عَلَى عَبْدِنَا فَأْتُوا بِسُورَةٍ مِّن مِثْلِهِ وَادْعُوا شُهَدَاءَكُم مِّن دُونِ اللَّهِ إِن كُنتُمْ صَادِقِينَ . ولما ظهر عجزهم وبان خزيهم أنذرهم صاحب التنزيل وحذرهم المتحدي بالدليل: فَإِن لَّمْ تَفْعَلُوا وَلَن تَفْعَلُوا فَاتَّقُوا النَّارَ الَّتِي وَقُودُهَا النَّاسُ
The people of truth said: The evidence for the truthfulness of our Prophet, peace be upon him, is the Book that he brought, a guidance for the people and clear proofs of guidance and criterion. And the aspect of its indication of his truthfulness is in terms of its eloquent wording and its clear meaning. So we say: Just as the human species was distinguished from the species of animals by speech expressing thought, and that became an honor and dignity for him, as the Exalted said: 'And We have certainly honored the children of Adam' (al-Isra 17:70); similarly, the tongue of the Arabs and their language was distinguished from all other tongues and languages by another style: sweetness of tongue, smoothness of pronunciation, ease of articulation, and expression of the essence of the meaning circulating in the mind with the clearest phrase and the soundest interpretation, and that became an honor and dignity for them, as the Exalted said: 'In a clear Arabic tongue' (al-Shu'ara 26:195). And similarly, the tongue of the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, was distinguished from the tongue of the Arabs by another style: manifest eloquence, surpassing rhetoric, and skill matching the clear meanings and weighty truths in his mind, as is not hidden from one who is fair, considers, tests his words, and gains insight. And that became an honor and dignity, as He said: 'So that you may make clear to the people what was sent down to them' (al-Nahl 16:44), and the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, said: 'I am the most eloquent of the Arabs, and I am the most eloquent of those who speak the ḍād.' And similarly, the Qur'an was distinguished from all his words by another style, outside the genre of Arab speech and also outside his words, and by another type of eloquence, majesty, composition, and rhetoric that the Arabs had not known in their ordered prose, prose, rhymed prose, and poetry, such that if the most eloquent of their words were compared to a single sura of the Qur'an, the disparity between them would be greater than the disparity between the tongue of the Arabs and all other tongues. And if one were to choose between the very words of the Prophet and what was revealed to him of the Book that dominates all books, the difference between them would be the difference between the foot and the foot? and the distinction between them would be the distinction between the guardianship and the distinction? So it was known necessarily and decisively that what he brought was a revelation inspired to him, and a sending down sent down upon him, as evidence of his truthfulness and a miracle for him against the eloquent Arabs, the rhetoricians of the people of the tongue, and the poets of that time. So he challenged thereby a challenge of incapacitation to produce something like it as a book and a Qur'an: 'Say: Then bring a Book from God that is better guided than these two' (al-Qasas 28:49). Then he repeated that saying: 'Then bring a hadith like it' (al-Tur 52:34). And when they were unable to produce its like, he descended from that when the people said he had fabricated it, and he said: 'Say: Then bring ten surahs like it fabricated' (Hud 11:13). And he descended from ten to one surah like it, and the Exalted said: 'And if you are in doubt about what We have sent down upon Our servant, then bring a surah the like of it and call your witnesses besides God, if you are truthful' (al-Baqarah 2:23). And when their inability became apparent and their disgrace became manifest, the Owner of the revelation warned them and the challenger warned them with the evidence: 'But if you do not — and you will never do — then fear the Fire whose fuel is people' (al-Baqarah 2:24).
Source pages p. 444

Commentary
This passage is a proof of the Prophet Muhammad's truthfulness based on the inimitability (i'jaz) of the Qur'an. The author begins by stating the position of 'the people of truth' (ahl al-haqq) that the evidence for the Prophet's truthfulness is the Qur'an itself, which is a guidance and clear proofs. Then he unpacks the argument in a stepwise analogy.

First, he establishes a principle: God distinguished humans from animals by the gift of articulate speech (nutq) expressing thought, which is an honor. Similarly, He distinguished the Arabic language from other languages by its unique sweetness, smoothness, and clarity in expressing inner meanings — another honor. Likewise, He distinguished the Prophet's own speech from other Arab speech by its superior eloquence (fasaaha) and rhetoric (balaaghah), as the Prophet himself claimed to be the most eloquent of the Arabs.

Then he presents the main point: the Qur'an is distinguished even from the Prophet's own words by a style that is entirely outside the genre of human speech. The Qur'an's eloquence, majesty, composition, and rhetoric surpass anything the Arabs had ever produced in prose, poetry, or rhymed prose. The disparity between the most eloquent Arabic speech and a single sura of the Qur'an is greater than the disparity between Arabic and all other languages. Moreover, the difference between the Prophet's own words and the Qur'an is immense — he uses a striking analogy: 'the difference between the foot and the foot?' (meaning a huge difference), and 'the distinction between the guardianship and the distinction?' (perhaps alluding to the difference between prophethood and ordinary speech). Thus, it is known necessarily and decisively that the Qur'an is divine revelation, not human speech, and it serves as a miracle (mu'jiza) for the Prophet.

Finally, he narrates the challenge (tahaddi) process: The Prophet challenged the Arabs to produce a book like the Qur'an (Q 28:49), then a hadith like it (Q 52:34), then ten surahs (Q 11:13), and finally a single sura (Q 2:23). Despite their hostility and motivation to disprove him, they failed utterly. Their inability and disgrace became evident, so God warned them of Hellfire (Q 2:24). This historical failure proves the Qur'an's divine origin and the Prophet's truth.

The argument is cumulative: each level of distinction (human speech vs. animal, Arabic vs. other languages, Prophetic speech vs. Arab speech, Qur'an vs. Prophetic speech) builds the case that the Qur'an is utterly unique and therefore miraculous.

Key Terms
إعجاز القرآن (i'jaz al-Qur'an)
الفصاحة (fasaaha)
البلاغة (balaaghah)
النطق (nutq)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Qur'an's uniqueness is solely about its eloquence (fasaaha) in a quantitative sense.
Correction: The passage shows the Qur'an's superiority is qualitative: it is 'outside the genre of Arab speech' and surpasses even the Prophet's own words, indicating divine origin.

Checkpoint
What distinguishes humans from animals according to the passage?
A) Intellect
B) Speech expressing thought (nutq)
C) Writing
D) Religion

Key Takeaway
The Qur'an's eloquence is so far beyond human capacity that it can only be from God, as shown by a four-level analogy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Qur'an, do you consciously feel that its words are utterly beyond human capability? How can you train yourself to sense this gap and let it deepen your awe?
?
The passage says the gap between the Qur'an and the Prophet's own speech is greater than between Arabic and all other languages. If you have ever been moved by a translation of the Qur'an, how much more should the original affect you? What will you do to connect with the Arabic?
?
Juwayni's argument requires you to compare—have you ever compared the Qur'an to any human speech and felt its superiority? If not, what might be holding you back from that recognition, and how can you honestly seek it?

The Challenge of the Qur'an (Tahaddi)
Juwayni's presentation of the Qur'anic challenge (tahaddi) and its proof of prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical challenge (tahaddi) posed by the Qur'an and how the Arabs' failure to meet it confirms its divine origin.

Core Idea
The Arabs' inability to produce even one sura proves the Qur'an is from God.

After establishing the Qur'an's unique eloquence, Juwayni recounts the famous challenge: the Prophet called on the Arabs to produce a similar book, then a hadith, then ten suras, then one sura — and they failed. This historical fact solidifies the argument for divine origin.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation, noting the sequence of challenges and the Qur'anic verses cited.
2
Identify the four stages of the challenge
The challenge descends from a book to a hadith to ten suras to one sura. List them in order.
3
Understand the significance of the descent
The Prophet gradually lowered the requirement, showing that even the smallest part of the Qur'an is inimitable. The Arabs' failure at each stage proves their incapacity.
4
Connect to the conclusion
The passage ends with a warning of Hellfire for those who disbelieve despite clear evidence. Reflect on how this challenge directly demonstrates the Prophet's truthfulness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

الحيوانات بالنطق المعبر عن الفكر، وصار ذلك شرفا وكرامة له كما قال تعالى : وَلَقَدْ كَرَّمْنَا بَنِى ءَادَمَ كذلك تميز لسان العرب ولغتهم من سائر الألسن واللغات بأسلوب آخر من عذوبة اللسان ورطوبة اللفظ وسهولة المخارج، والتعبير عن متن المعنى الدائر في الضمير بأوضح عبارة وأصح تفسير، وصار ذلك شرفًا وكرامة لهم كما قال تعالى : بِلِسَانٍ عَرَينٍ مُّبِينٍ . وكذلك تميز لسان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم من لسان العرب بأسلوب آخر من الفصاحة المبينة والبلاغة الفائقة والبراعة المطابقة لما في ضميره من المعاني المبينة والحقائق الرزينة، كما لا يخفى على من أنصف واعتبر واختبر كلماته واستبصر وصار ذلك شرفا وكرامة كما قال : لِتُبَيِّنَ لِلنَّاسِ مَا نُزِلَ إِلَيْهِمْ ، وقال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: «أنا أفصح العرب، وأنا أفصح من نطق بالضاد». وكذلك تميز القرآن عن سائر كلماته بأسلوب آخر خارج عن جنس كلام العرب وعن كلماته أيضا، وبنوع آخر من الفصاحة والجزالة والنظم والبلاغة ما لم تعهده العرب في نظمهم ونثرهم وسجعهم وشعرهم، بحيث لو قوبل أفصح كلماتهم بسورة واحدة من القرآن كان التفاوت بينهما أكثر من التفاوت بين لسان العرب وبين سائر الألسن، ولو خاير بين كلمات النبي نفسه وبين ما نزل عليه من الكتاب المهيمن على الكتب كلها كان الفرق بينهما فرق ما بين القدم والفرق، والصرف بينهما صرف ما بين الولاية والصرف، فعلم ضرورة وقطعًا أن الذي جاء به وحي يوحى إليه، وتنزيل ينزل عليه دلالة له على صدقه ومعجزة له على فصحاء العرب وبلغاء أهل اللسان وشعراء ذلك الزمان، فتحدى بذلك تحدي التعجيز عن الإتيان بمثله كتاباً وقرآنًا : قُلْ فَأْتُوا بِكِتَبٍ مِنْ عِندِ اللَّهِ هُوَ أَهْدَى مِنْهُمَا، ثم ثنى ذلك فقال : فأتوا بحديث مثله، ولما عجزوا عن الإتيان مثله نزل عن ذلك حين قال القوم : إنه افتراه، فقال: قُلْ فَأْتُوا بِعَشْرِ سُوَرٍ مِثْلِهِ مُفْتَرَيَت ونزل عن العشر إلى سورة مثله فقال تعالى : وَإِن كُنتُمْ فِي رَيْبٍ مِّمَّا نَزَّلْنَا عَلَى عَبْدِنَا فَأْتُوا بِسُورَةٍ مِّن مِثْلِهِ وَادْعُوا شُهَدَاءَكُم مِّن دُونِ اللَّهِ إِن كُنتُمْ صَادِقِينَ . ولما ظهر عجزهم وبان خزيهم أنذرهم صاحب التنزيل وحذرهم المتحدي بالدليل: فَإِن لَّمْ تَفْعَلُوا وَلَن تَفْعَلُوا فَاتَّقُوا النَّارَ الَّتِي وَقُودُهَا النَّاسُ
The people of truth said: The evidence for the truthfulness of our Prophet, peace be upon him, is the Book that he brought, a guidance for the people and clear proofs of guidance and criterion. And the aspect of its indication of his truthfulness is in terms of its eloquent wording and its clear meaning. So we say: Just as the human species was distinguished from the species of animals by speech expressing thought, and that became an honor and dignity for him, as the Exalted said: 'And We have certainly honored the children of Adam' (al-Isra 17:70); similarly, the tongue of the Arabs and their language was distinguished from all other tongues and languages by another style: sweetness of tongue, smoothness of pronunciation, ease of articulation, and expression of the essence of the meaning circulating in the mind with the clearest phrase and the soundest interpretation, and that became an honor and dignity for them, as the Exalted said: 'In a clear Arabic tongue' (al-Shu'ara 26:195). And similarly, the tongue of the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, was distinguished from the tongue of the Arabs by another style: manifest eloquence, surpassing rhetoric, and skill matching the clear meanings and weighty truths in his mind, as is not hidden from one who is fair, considers, tests his words, and gains insight. And that became an honor and dignity, as He said: 'So that you may make clear to the people what was sent down to them' (al-Nahl 16:44), and the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, said: 'I am the most eloquent of the Arabs, and I am the most eloquent of those who speak the ḍād.' And similarly, the Qur'an was distinguished from all his words by another style, outside the genre of Arab speech and also outside his words, and by another type of eloquence, majesty, composition, and rhetoric that the Arabs had not known in their ordered prose, prose, rhymed prose, and poetry, such that if the most eloquent of their words were compared to a single sura of the Qur'an, the disparity between them would be greater than the disparity between the tongue of the Arabs and all other tongues. And if one were to choose between the very words of the Prophet and what was revealed to him of the Book that dominates all books, the difference between them would be the difference between the foot and the foot? and the distinction between them would be the distinction between the guardianship and the distinction? So it was known necessarily and decisively that what he brought was a revelation inspired to him, and a sending down sent down upon him, as evidence of his truthfulness and a miracle for him against the eloquent Arabs, the rhetoricians of the people of the tongue, and the poets of that time. So he challenged thereby a challenge of incapacitation to produce something like it as a book and a Qur'an: 'Say: Then bring a Book from God that is better guided than these two' (al-Qasas 28:49). Then he repeated that saying: 'Then bring a hadith like it' (al-Tur 52:34). And when they were unable to produce its like, he descended from that when the people said he had fabricated it, and he said: 'Say: Then bring ten surahs like it fabricated' (Hud 11:13). And he descended from ten to one surah like it, and the Exalted said: 'And if you are in doubt about what We have sent down upon Our servant, then bring a surah the like of it and call your witnesses besides God, if you are truthful' (al-Baqarah 2:23). And when their inability became apparent and their disgrace became manifest, the Owner of the revelation warned them and the challenger warned them with the evidence: 'But if you do not — and you will never do — then fear the Fire whose fuel is people' (al-Baqarah 2:24).
Source pages p. 444

Commentary
This passage is a proof of the Prophet Muhammad's truthfulness based on the inimitability (i'jaz) of the Qur'an. The author begins by stating the position of 'the people of truth' (ahl al-haqq) that the evidence for the Prophet's truthfulness is the Qur'an itself, which is a guidance and clear proofs. Then he unpacks the argument in a stepwise analogy.

First, he establishes a principle: God distinguished humans from animals by the gift of articulate speech (nutq) expressing thought, which is an honor. Similarly, He distinguished the Arabic language from other languages by its unique sweetness, smoothness, and clarity in expressing inner meanings — another honor. Likewise, He distinguished the Prophet's own speech from other Arab speech by its superior eloquence (fasaaha) and rhetoric (balaaghah), as the Prophet himself claimed to be the most eloquent of the Arabs.

Then he presents the main point: the Qur'an is distinguished even from the Prophet's own words by a style that is entirely outside the genre of human speech. The Qur'an's eloquence, majesty, composition, and rhetoric surpass anything the Arabs had ever produced in prose, poetry, or rhymed prose. The disparity between the most eloquent Arabic speech and a single sura of the Qur'an is greater than the disparity between Arabic and all other languages. Moreover, the difference between the Prophet's own words and the Qur'an is immense — he uses a striking analogy: 'the difference between the foot and the foot?' (meaning a huge difference), and 'the distinction between the guardianship and the distinction?' (perhaps alluding to the difference between prophethood and ordinary speech). Thus, it is known necessarily and decisively that the Qur'an is divine revelation, not human speech, and it serves as a miracle (mu'jiza) for the Prophet.

Finally, he narrates the challenge (tahaddi) process: The Prophet challenged the Arabs to produce a book like the Qur'an (Q 28:49), then a hadith like it (Q 52:34), then ten surahs (Q 11:13), and finally a single sura (Q 2:23). Despite their hostility and motivation to disprove him, they failed utterly. Their inability and disgrace became evident, so God warned them of Hellfire (Q 2:24). This historical failure proves the Qur'an's divine origin and the Prophet's truth.

The argument is cumulative: each level of distinction (human speech vs. animal, Arabic vs. other languages, Prophetic speech vs. Arab speech, Qur'an vs. Prophetic speech) builds the case that the Qur'an is utterly unique and therefore miraculous.

Key Terms
التحدي (tahaddi)
التعجيز (ta'jiz)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The challenge was only for poets to produce similar poetry.
Correction: The challenge included a book, a hadith, and surahs, covering all forms of speech, not just poetry.

Checkpoint
What was the first challenge mentioned in the passage?
A) Bring ten surahs
B) Bring one surah
C) Bring a book like it
D) Bring a hadith like it

Key Takeaway
The Arabs' failure to meet the Qur'an's challenge, even for a single sura, proves its divine origin and the Prophet's truthfulness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Qur'an's challenge stands eternally: 'and you will never do'. Have you ever truly pondered this challenge as directed at you, not just at the Arabs? What prevents you from responding with absolute certainty that this book is from God? Will you not make a firm resolve today to engage with it as the decisive proof it claims to be?
?
The Arabs were masters of eloquence and yet failed. You may not be a poet, but you hold the same Qur'an in your hands. If you truly believed it is the inimitably revealed word of God, would your daily relationship with it change? What would be different? Commit to one specific change in how you read or listen to the Qur'an starting today.
?
God warns: 'Fear the Fire whose fuel is people.' The failure to respond to the challenge leads to eternal loss. Do you realize that your own response to the Qur'an—whether through study, acceptance, or rejection—carries that same weight? Are you content to treat it as merely a text, or will you let it judge your soul and transform your life?

The Skeptical Dilemma on Prophethood
Objection from deviant thinkers on prophethood's nature

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the dilemma posed by skeptics regarding whether prophethood is an inherent attribute or a divine declaration, and why this question challenges the coherence of prophetic claims.

Core Idea
Is prophethood an inner attribute or a divine label?

This passage presents a critical objection from those who question the very concept of prophethood. They frame a dilemma: either prophethood is a real attribute within the prophet, or it is merely God's declaration. Both options seem problematic to them. Reading this objection helps us appreciate the theological challenge that Muslim scholars had to address.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Note that it is the beginning of an objection from 'the people of deviation'.
The passage cuts off mid-sentence.
2
Identify the two horns of the dilemma
The objection asks: does 'messengership' refer to an attribute subsisting in the prophet's essence, or does it refer to God's act of informing that he is a messenger?
These are the two options: sifa qā'ima or ikhbār.
3
Consider why both options are problematic
If it is an attribute, what is that attribute? If it is divine informing, how can God speak to a human? The objector implies neither is satisfactory.
The difficulty lies in conceiving how a human can have a prophetic attribute or how God can communicate directly.
4
Recognize the incomplete nature of the passage
This lesson only covers the objection; the author's answer is not included. Be aware that the full argument requires subsequent pages.
This is a deliberate split to focus on the objection itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أهل الزيغ : إذا قال النبي : إني رسول الله إليكم ، وأنه أنزل علي كتابا أقرأه عليكم ، فما المعنى بالرسالة عن الله تعالى؟ وما معنى قوله : إني نبي الله ؟ أفترجع الرسالة والنبوة إلى صفة قائمة بذاته بها يستحق أن يخاطب الناس بالأوامر والنواهي عن الله تعالى أم ترجع إلى إخبار الله تعالى أنه رسولي؟ فإن كان الأول فما حقيقة تلك الصفة؟ وإن كان الثاني فكيف يتصور أن يكلم الله بشرًا، فإن الذي
The people of deviation said: When the prophet says: 'I am the messenger of God to you,' and that He revealed to him a book which he recites to them, what is the meaning of the message from God Almighty? And what is the meaning of his saying: 'I am the prophet of God'? Does the message and prophethood refer to an attribute subsisting in his essence by which he deserves to address people with commands and prohibitions from God Almighty, or do they refer to God Almighty informing that he is My messenger? If the first, then what is the reality of that attribute? And if the second, then how can it be imagined that God speaks to a human? For that which...
Source pages p. 459

Commentary
This passage presents an objection from 'the people of deviation' (ahl al-zaygh) regarding the nature of prophethood. The objection is framed as a dilemma: when a prophet claims to be God's messenger, does 'messengership' (risala) and 'prophethood' (nubuwwa) refer to an inherent attribute (sifa) within the prophet that qualifies him to convey commands and prohibitions, or do they refer simply to God's act of informing that he is a messenger? If it is an inherent attribute, what is that attribute? If it is a divine act of communication, how can God speak to a human? The passage breaks off, leaving the objection unanswered in this window. The argument challenges the coherence of prophetic claims by questioning whether prophethood is something intrinsic or merely a declaration, and whether divine speech to a human is conceivable.

Key Terms
رسالة
نبوة
صفة
إخبار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What two options does the objection present for the nature of prophethood?
A) That it is a miracle or a rational proof
B) That it is an attribute of the prophet or an act of divine informing
C) That it is acquired or innate
D) That it is physical or spiritual

Key Takeaway
The objection forces us to clarify whether prophethood is an intrinsic quality or a relational declaration from God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear someone claim divine authority, do you demand evidence? How does this dilemma challenge your own assumptions about what makes a messenger credible? Will you now investigate the basis of such claims before accepting them?
?
This objection exposes a tension between prophethood as an intrinsic quality and as a divine declaration. In your own understanding, which side do you lean toward, and why? Have you ever thought deeply about how God communicates with prophets?
?
The skeptics asked a piercing question. If you were asked by a sincere seeker to explain the reality of prophethood, how would you answer using this passage? What would you say about the attribute or the divine speech? Let this question push you to clarify your own conviction.

The Rationalist Objections to Prophethood
The people of deviation raise six rational objections to prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key rationalist objections raised against the claims of prophethood, including the nature of revelation, angelic descent, and eschatological concepts.

Core Idea
Prophethood is challenged on rational grounds: how can God speak, angels descend, and bodily resurrection occur?

Before we examine the Islamic response, we must first understand the objections posed by rationalist thinkers. They questioned the very coherence of prophethood, revelation, and the afterlife. This passage presents their most incisive criticisms.

Guided Path
1
Read the objections carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the sequence of questions.
The objections are presented as a series of logical dilemmas.
2
Identify each distinct objection
List out the six main questions: 1) Is prophethood an attribute or an announcement? 2) How does God speak? 3) What is revelation? 4) How can an angel descend? 5) How can the Prophet ascend? 6) How can bodily resurrection be rational?
Each objection builds on the previous one.
3
Reflect on the rationalist presuppositions
Consider the assumption that if a claim is not rationally conceivable, it cannot be required to be proven. What worldview does this reflect?
This is a key argument against miracles in general.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أهل الزيغ: إذا قال النبي: إني رسول الله إليكم، وأنه أنزل علي كتابًا أقرأه عليكم، فما المعني بالرسالة عن الله تعالى؟ وما معنى قوله: إني نبي الله؟ أفترجع الرسالة والنبوة إلى صفة قائمة بذاته بها يستحق أن يخاطب الناس بالأوامر والنواهي عن الله تعالى أم ترجع إلى إخبار الله تعالى أنه رسولي؟ فإن كان الأول فما حقيقة تلك الصفة؟ وإن كان الثاني فكيف يتصور أن يكلم الله بشرًا، فإن الذي يسمعه البشر من الكلام حروف وأصوات، وعندكم كلامه ليس بحرف ولا صوت؟ وإن كان وحيا من الله تعالى فما معنى الوحي؟ وكيف يتصور أن ينزل ملك على صورة البشر؟ فإن كان الملك شخصًا جسمانيا، فيجب أن يكون على صورة بشر حتى يكلمه بكلام البشر، وإن كان جوهرًا روحانيا فكيف يتصور أن يتشخص ويظهر بشخص جسماني؟ أليس نفس الدعوى إذا لم تكن معقولة في نفسها لم يجز مطالبته بالبرهان عليها، فلا نزول الملك معقول، ولا نزول القرآن الذي هو كلامه معقول؛ بل هما مستحيلان عند العقلاء بأسرهم، وأيضًا فإنه ادعى بعد ذلك صعوده إلى السماء، والجسماني الكثيف يستحيل أن يصعد، والأجرام العلوية لا تقبل الخرق، وإذا اشتمل كلامه على ما يستحيل في العقل حكم ببطلان أصل دعواه إلى غير ذلك مما ادعى أنه شاهد العوالم، وأخبر عن حشر الأجسام والإحياء في القبور والميزان والصراط والحوض بعد ذلك، فإن هذه غير معقولة، بل قبولها على الوجه الذي يدعيه مستحيل. قال أهل الحق: النبوة ليست صفة راجعة إلى نفس النبي، ولا درجة يبلغ إليها أحد بعلمه وكسبه، ولا استعداد نفسه يستحق به اتصالا بالروحانيات، بل رحمة من الله تعالى ونعمة يمن بها على من يشاء من عباده، وكما قال نوح عليه السلام: وَلَا أَقُولُ لَكُمْ عِندِي خَزَايِنُ اللَّهِ وَلَا أَعْلَمُ الْغَيْبَ وَلَا أَقُولُ إِنِّي مَلَك [الأنعام: ٥٠]
The people of deviation said: When the prophet says, 'I am the messenger of God to you, and He has sent down to me a book that I recite to you,' what is meant by the message (al-risāla) from God? And what is the meaning of his saying, 'I am the prophet of God'? Does the message and prophethood (al-nubuwwa) refer to an attribute subsisting in his essence by which he deserves to address people with commands and prohibitions from God, or do they refer to God's informing that he is His messenger? If the first, then what is the reality of that attribute? And if the second, then how can it be conceived that God speaks to a human, for what humans hear of speech is letters and sounds, and according to you His speech is not a letter nor a sound? And if it is a revelation (waḥy) from God, then what is the meaning of revelation? And how can it be conceived that an angel descends in the form of a human? For if the angel is a physical person, then he must be in the form of a human so that he can speak to him with human speech, and if he is a spiritual substance (jawhar rūḥānī), then how can it be conceived that he becomes embodied and appears in a physical form? Is it not that if the claim itself is not rationally conceivable, it is not permissible to demand proof for it? So neither the descent of the angel is rational, nor the descent of the Qur'an which is His speech is rational; rather, both are impossible in the view of all rational people. Also, he claimed after that his ascent to heaven, and the dense physical body cannot ascend, and the celestial bodies do not admit of penetration. And if his speech contains what is rationally impossible, the invalidity of his entire claim is judged, besides other things that he claimed to have witnessed of the worlds, and he informed about the gathering of bodies, the reviving in graves, the balance, the path, and the basin after that—for these are not rationally conceivable; rather, accepting them in the manner he claims is impossible. The people of truth said: Prophethood is not an attribute referring to the prophet himself, nor a rank attained by anyone through his knowledge and acquisition, nor a preparedness of his soul by which he deserves connection with spiritual beings; rather, it is a mercy from God and a grace that He bestows upon whomever He wills among His servants, just as Noah (peace be upon him) said: 'And I do not say to you that I have the treasures of God, nor do I know the unseen, nor do I say that I am an angel.' [Qur'an 11:31]
Source pages p. 459

Commentary
This passage presents the objections of the people of deviation (ahl al-zaygh) against the claims of prophethood, followed by the response of the people of truth (ahl al-ḥaqq). The objection is a series of questions: they ask whether prophethood is an attribute in the prophet or merely an announcement from God. If it is an attribute, what is its reality? If it is an announcement, how can God speak to a human when His speech is not composed of letters and sounds? They also question the nature of revelation (waḥy) and the descent of an angel—if the angel is physical, it must take human form; if it is spiritual, how does it become embodied? They argue that if the claim itself is inconceivable, it cannot be required to be proven. They then mention the prophet's claim of ascension, which they deem impossible for a dense body, and the resurrection, balance, path, and basin as rationally impossible. The response from the people of truth is simple: prophethood is not a human attainment or an inherent attribute; it is a mercy and grace from God that He bestows on whom He wills. They cite the verse of Noah to show that even prophets acknowledge their human limitation and that prophethood is a divine gift, not a human achievement.

Key Terms
الرسالة
النبوة
الوحي
الملك
جوهر روحاني
الصعود
الحشر
الميزان
الصراط
الحوض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the objections raised by the people of deviation?
A) How can God speak to a human if His speech is not letters and sounds?
B) How can an angel descend in human form?
C) How can the Prophet perform miracles?
D) How can a dense body ascend to heaven?

Key Takeaway
The people of deviation raised a series of rational objections challenging the coherence of prophethood, revelation, and the afterlife.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear someone argue that prophethood is irrational, do you feel a hidden doubt? What specific objection from this passage—if any—makes you uncomfortable, and why?
?
If you cannot fully grasp how God speaks without letters or how angels descend, does that ever make you question the truth of the Qur'an? What would it take for you to trust God's power over your own understanding?
?
The people of deviation refused to accept what their minds could not conceive. In what area of your life are you demanding rational proof before submitting to God's command? Will you obey even what seems rationally impossible to you?
