The Ash'ari Response: Prophethood as Divine Grace
The people of truth define prophethood as a divine grace, not a human attribute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari response that prophethood is not a human attainment but a divine mercy and grace.

Core Idea
Prophethood is a pure gift from God, not a human achievement or inherent attribute.

The people of truth answer the rationalist objections by redefining the nature of prophethood. They assert that prophethood is not something a person can earn or an attribute they possess; it is entirely a bestowal from God.

Guided Path
1
Read the response carefully
Read the Arabic passage once. Then read the translation. Notice the structure: three negations followed by an affirmation.
The response is concise and categorical.
2
Identify the three negations
The people of truth deny that prophethood is: (1) an attribute in the prophet, (2) a rank attained by knowledge and effort, (3) a preparedness of the soul. Underline these in the text.
Each negation directly counters a possible understanding.
3
Understand the positive definition
They affirm that prophethood is a mercy (rahma) and grace (niʿma) from God, bestowed on whomever He wills. Reflect on the implications: it is entirely God's choice.
This is the core of the Ash'ari doctrine on prophethood.
4
Connect with the Quranic verse
The verse from Noah (11:31) is cited to emphasize the prophet's human limitations and that divine gifts are not in human control.
Noah says he does not have treasures of God, nor knows the unseen, nor is an angel.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أهل الزيغ: إذا قال النبي: إني رسول الله إليكم، وأنه أنزل علي كتابًا أقرأه عليكم، فما المعني بالرسالة عن الله تعالى؟ وما معنى قوله: إني نبي الله؟ أفترجع الرسالة والنبوة إلى صفة قائمة بذاته بها يستحق أن يخاطب الناس بالأوامر والنواهي عن الله تعالى أم ترجع إلى إخبار الله تعالى أنه رسولي؟ فإن كان الأول فما حقيقة تلك الصفة؟ وإن كان الثاني فكيف يتصور أن يكلم الله بشرًا، فإن الذي يسمعه البشر من الكلام حروف وأصوات، وعندكم كلامه ليس بحرف ولا صوت؟ وإن كان وحيا من الله تعالى فما معنى الوحي؟ وكيف يتصور أن ينزل ملك على صورة البشر؟ فإن كان الملك شخصًا جسمانيا، فيجب أن يكون على صورة بشر حتى يكلمه بكلام البشر، وإن كان جوهرًا روحانيا فكيف يتصور أن يتشخص ويظهر بشخص جسماني؟ أليس نفس الدعوى إذا لم تكن معقولة في نفسها لم يجز مطالبته بالبرهان عليها، فلا نزول الملك معقول، ولا نزول القرآن الذي هو كلامه معقول؛ بل هما مستحيلان عند العقلاء بأسرهم، وأيضًا فإنه ادعى بعد ذلك صعوده إلى السماء، والجسماني الكثيف يستحيل أن يصعد، والأجرام العلوية لا تقبل الخرق، وإذا اشتمل كلامه على ما يستحيل في العقل حكم ببطلان أصل دعواه إلى غير ذلك مما ادعى أنه شاهد العوالم، وأخبر عن حشر الأجسام والإحياء في القبور والميزان والصراط والحوض بعد ذلك، فإن هذه غير معقولة، بل قبولها على الوجه الذي يدعيه مستحيل. قال أهل الحق: النبوة ليست صفة راجعة إلى نفس النبي، ولا درجة يبلغ إليها أحد بعلمه وكسبه، ولا استعداد نفسه يستحق به اتصالا بالروحانيات، بل رحمة من الله تعالى ونعمة يمن بها على من يشاء من عباده، وكما قال نوح عليه السلام: وَلَا أَقُولُ لَكُمْ عِندِي خَزَايِنُ اللَّهِ وَلَا أَعْلَمُ الْغَيْبَ وَلَا أَقُولُ إِنِّي مَلَك [الأنعام: ٥٠]
The people of deviation said: When the prophet says, 'I am the messenger of God to you, and He has sent down to me a book that I recite to you,' what is meant by the message (al-risāla) from God? And what is the meaning of his saying, 'I am the prophet of God'? Does the message and prophethood (al-nubuwwa) refer to an attribute subsisting in his essence by which he deserves to address people with commands and prohibitions from God, or do they refer to God's informing that he is His messenger? If the first, then what is the reality of that attribute? And if the second, then how can it be conceived that God speaks to a human, for what humans hear of speech is letters and sounds, and according to you His speech is not a letter nor a sound? And if it is a revelation (waḥy) from God, then what is the meaning of revelation? And how can it be conceived that an angel descends in the form of a human? For if the angel is a physical person, then he must be in the form of a human so that he can speak to him with human speech, and if he is a spiritual substance (jawhar rūḥānī), then how can it be conceived that he becomes embodied and appears in a physical form? Is it not that if the claim itself is not rationally conceivable, it is not permissible to demand proof for it? So neither the descent of the angel is rational, nor the descent of the Qur'an which is His speech is rational; rather, both are impossible in the view of all rational people. Also, he claimed after that his ascent to heaven, and the dense physical body cannot ascend, and the celestial bodies do not admit of penetration. And if his speech contains what is rationally impossible, the invalidity of his entire claim is judged, besides other things that he claimed to have witnessed of the worlds, and he informed about the gathering of bodies, the reviving in graves, the balance, the path, and the basin after that—for these are not rationally conceivable; rather, accepting them in the manner he claims is impossible. The people of truth said: Prophethood is not an attribute referring to the prophet himself, nor a rank attained by anyone through his knowledge and acquisition, nor a preparedness of his soul by which he deserves connection with spiritual beings; rather, it is a mercy from God and a grace that He bestows upon whomever He wills among His servants, just as Noah (peace be upon him) said: 'And I do not say to you that I have the treasures of God, nor do I know the unseen, nor do I say that I am an angel.' [Qur'an 11:31]
Source pages p. 459

Commentary
This passage presents the objections of the people of deviation (ahl al-zaygh) against the claims of prophethood, followed by the response of the people of truth (ahl al-ḥaqq). The objection is a series of questions: they ask whether prophethood is an attribute in the prophet or merely an announcement from God. If it is an attribute, what is its reality? If it is an announcement, how can God speak to a human when His speech is not composed of letters and sounds? They also question the nature of revelation (waḥy) and the descent of an angel—if the angel is physical, it must take human form; if it is spiritual, how does it become embodied? They argue that if the claim itself is inconceivable, it cannot be required to be proven. They then mention the prophet's claim of ascension, which they deem impossible for a dense body, and the resurrection, balance, path, and basin as rationally impossible. The response from the people of truth is simple: prophethood is not a human attainment or an inherent attribute; it is a mercy and grace from God that He bestows on whom He wills. They cite the verse of Noah to show that even prophets acknowledge their human limitation and that prophethood is a divine gift, not a human achievement.

Key Terms
النبوة
رحمة
نعمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophethood can be attained through spiritual discipline or inherent merit.
Correction: The passage clarifies it is purely a divine gift, not earned or deserved.

Checkpoint
According to the people of truth, what is prophethood?
A) An attribute of the prophet's soul.
B) A rank attained by knowledge and effort.
C) A mercy and grace from God.
D) A natural connection with spiritual beings.

Key Takeaway
Prophethood is a divine grace, not a human attribute or achievement.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If prophethood is purely a gift from God and not something earned, how does that challenge your assumption that you can earn God's favor through your own efforts? What does that mean for how you approach your relationship with God today?
?
Noah, a great prophet, denied having any special powers or inherent status. Do you ever catch yourself feeling entitled to God's blessings because of your actions or identity? How can you let go of that entitlement and see everything as a gift?
?
Think of a blessing you deeply desire. Based on this lesson, can you truly demand it from God? Instead, how will you humbly ask for it as a mercy, and what will you do to cultivate gratitude for what you already have?

Rational Objections to Revelation and Angel Descent
The author presents the first two rational objections against revelation and angelic descent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational objections raised against the possibility of revelation and angelic descent in human form.

Core Idea
Rational consistency is demanded of prophetic claims, including revelation and angelic visitation.

The passage presents the first set of adversarial arguments against prophethood. The objector questions how divine revelation can involve human language if God's speech is not composed of letters and sounds, and challenges the plausibility of an angel appearing as a human being. These objections are based on rational principles that the opponent insists must be satisfied.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two objections
Read the passage and find the objections concerning revelation and angel descent. Note how they are connected.
2
Understand the dilemma
The angel is presented with a dilemma: if corporeal, it must be human; if spiritual, it cannot become corporeal. Analyze why this is seen as a contradiction.
3
Recognize the conclusion
The objector concludes that both revelation and angel descent are impossible according to all rational people. Consider the implications for the prophetic claim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يسمعه البشر من الكلام حروف وأصوات، وعندكم كلامه ليس بحرف ولا صوت؟ وإن كان وحيا من الله تعالى فما معنى الوحي؟ وكيف يتصور أن ينزل ملك على صورة البشر؟ فإن كان الملك شخصا جسمانيا فيجب أن يكون على صورة بشر حتى يكلمه بكلام البشر، وإن كان جوهرا روحانيا فكيف يتصور أن يتشخص ويظهر بشخص جسماني؟ أليس نفس الدعوى إذا لم تكن معقولة في نفسها لم يجز مطالبته بالبرهان عليها، فلا نزول الملك معقول، ولا نزول القرآن الذي هو كلامه معقول؛ بل هما مستحيلان عند العقلاء بأسرهم. وأيضا فإنه ادعى بعد ذلك صعوده إلى السماء، والجسماني الكثيف يستحيل أن يصعد، والأجرام العلوية لا تقبل الخرق، وإذا اشتمل كلامه على ما يستحيل في العقل حكم ببطلان أصل دعواه. إلى غير ذلك مما ادعى أنه شاهد العوالم، وأخبر عن حشر الأجسام والإحياء في القبور والميزان والصراط والحوض بعد ذلك، فإن هذه غير معقولة، بل قبولها على الوجه الذي يدعيه مستحيل.
He hears from speech letters and sounds, but according to you His speech is not letters or sound? If it is revelation from God, what is the meaning of revelation? How can it be conceived that an angel descends in human form? If the angel is a corporeal entity, then it must be in human form so as to speak to him with human speech. If it is a spiritual substance, how can it be conceived that it becomes individuated and appears in a corporeal form? Is it not the case that if the claim itself is not rationally conceivable, it is not permissible to demand proof for it? So neither the descent of the angel is rational, nor the descent of the Qur'an which is His speech is rational; rather both are impossible according to all rational people. Moreover, he claimed ascension to heaven, but a dense corporeal body cannot ascend, and the celestial bodies do not admit penetration. If his speech contains what is rationally impossible, then his entire claim is judged false. And other things he claimed to have witnessed of the worlds, and informed about the gathering of bodies, revival in graves, the balance, the path, and the pool thereafter — these are not rational, rather accepting them in the manner he claims is impossible.
Source pages p. 460

Commentary
This passage presents a series of rational objections against the claims of prophethood. It lists several supposed impossibilities: that God's speech, if it is not letters and sounds, cannot be heard by humans; that revelation itself is incomprehensible; that an angel descending in human form is either a corporeal entity that must be human-shaped or a spiritual entity that cannot become corporeal; that claiming ascension is impossible because bodies cannot penetrate the heavens; and that the doctrines of bodily resurrection, scales, etc., are rationally impossible. The style is rhetorical and accusatory, aiming to show that the prophet's claims are self-contradictory and irrational. The passage ends with the assertion that these doctrines are not only irrational but that their acceptance as claimed is impossible.

Key Terms
الوحي
ملك
جسماني
جوهر روحاني

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: These objections are the author's own position.
Correction: The passage presents adversarial arguments that the author will likely refute later.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the descent of the angel considered problematic?
A) The angel must be a human to speak human speech.
B) The angel cannot be both corporeal and spiritual.
C) The angel's descent is impossible because angels are spiritual.
D) The angel's descent is impossible because God's speech is not letters.

Key Takeaway
The objector uses apparent physical and conceptual contradictions to argue that revelation and angelic descent are rationally impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever found yourself doubting the rational plausibility of Islamic beliefs, such as the descent of angels or the nature of the Quran? When that happens, do you approach the doubt with humility or do you let it shake your faith? What would it take for you to trust Allah's wisdom over your own limited understanding?
?
Imagine the objector's argument were true—that the claim of revelation is inherently irrational. How would that affect your daily relationship with the Quran? In what ways do you already experience the Quran as something beyond mere human speech?
?
The objector says, 'If a claim is not rationally conceivable, it is not permissible to demand proof.' On what basis do you accept matters of faith that go beyond your reason? Are there areas in your life where you demand rational proof before submitting to Allah's command? What would it cost you to surrender that demand today?

Rational Objections to Ascension and Eschatological Doctrines
The author continues with rational objections to the ascension and eschatological beliefs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational objections raised against the Prophet's ascension and the doctrines of bodily resurrection, scales, path, and pool.

Core Idea
Claims of bodily ascension and eschatological events are deemed rationally impossible by the objector.

The passage continues with objections to the Prophet's ascension to heaven, arguing that a dense body cannot ascend and the celestial spheres are impenetrable. It then extends the critique to other eschatological doctrines such as resurrection, scales, path, and pool, declaring them rationally inconceivable. The objector uses this as a basis to reject the entire prophetic claim.

Guided Path
1
Examine the ascension objection
Read the part about ascension. Identify why the objector thinks a dense body cannot ascend and why the heavens do not admit penetration.
2
Note the general principle
The objector states that if any part of the prophet's message contains a rational impossibility, the entire claim is false. Understand how this principle is applied.
3
Review the list of eschatological doctrines
Find the list: resurrection, scales, path, pool. Consider why each is deemed 'not rational' and why acceptance as claimed is 'impossible'.

He hears from speech letters and sounds, but according to you His speech is not letters or sound? If it is revelation from God, what is the meaning of revelation? How can it be conceived that an angel descends in human form? If the angel is a corporeal entity, then it must be in human form so as to speak to him with human speech. If it is a spiritual substance, how can it be conceived that it becomes individuated and appears in a corporeal form? And other things he claimed to have witnessed of the worlds, and informed about the gathering of bodies, revival in graves, the balance, the path, and the pool thereafter — these are not rational, rather accepting them in the manner he claims is impossible.

It lists several supposed impossibilities: that God's speech, if it is not letters and sounds, cannot be heard by humans; that revelation itself is incomprehensible; that an angel descending in human form is either a corporeal entity that must be human-shaped or a spiritual entity that cannot become corporeal; that claiming ascension is impossible because bodies cannot penetrate the heavens; and that the doctrines of bodily resurrection, scales, etc., are rationally impossible. Prophethood as Divine Mercy: Definition and the Prophet's Prior Virtue
The author defines prophethood as a divine gift and affirms the prophet's prior moral excellence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that prophethood is a divine mercy and favor, not a rank acquired by personal effort, and that the prophet's prior virtue is a gift from God that qualifies him for this role.

Core Idea
Prophethood is not earned—it is a pure gift of divine mercy.

This lesson defines prophethood from the orthodox Sunni perspective, emphasizing that it is not an attribute or rank that can be attained through knowledge, effort, or innate disposition. Instead, it is a mercy from God that He bestows upon whom He wills. The passage also affirms that the prophets, especially Muhammad (peace be upon him), possessed natural moral excellence before their mission, which was part of God's preparation for their role.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the strong opening negation followed by the affirmative statement.
2
Identify the core definition
The passage begins with three negations and one affirmation. Find them. The definition is the foundation of the entire lesson.
The negation of prophethood being an attribute, rank, or disposition is crucial.
3
Examine the Quranic proofs
The author cites verses from Noah and the Prophet Muhammad to show that prophets disclaim special knowledge and angelic status. Understand how these verses support the definition.
These verses highlight the human nature of prophets while affirming their mission.
4
Understand prior virtue as divine preparation
The passage then asserts that the Prophet had perfection in innate disposition and character before his mission. This is not a contradiction; it is part of God's choice. See how the verses about leniency and the objection about a 'great man' illustrate this.
Prior virtue is a gift, not a cause, of prophethood.
5
Conclude with the chosen status of prophets
The passage ends by stating that prophets are God's chosen and His proof. Reflect on the overall message that prophethood is entirely a divine mercy.
The word 'خيرة' (chosen) emphasizes God's selection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أهل الحق: النبوة ليست صفة راجعة إلى نفس النبي، ولا درجة يبلغ إليها أحد بعلمه وكسبه، ولا استعداد نفسه يستحق به اتصالا بالروحانيات، بل رحمة من الله تعالى ونعمة يمن بها على من يشاء من عباده. وكما قال نوح عليه السلام: ولا أقول لكم عندي خزائن الله ولا أعلم الغيب ولا أقول إني ملك [الأنعام: ٥٠] إلى غيره من الأنبياء، وسيد البشر صلى الله عليه وسلم قال كما قال الأول: قل سبحان ربي هل كنت إلا بشرا رسولا [الإسراء: ٩٣]، قل لا أملك لنفسي نفعا ولا ضرا إلا ما شاء الله ولو كنت أعلم الغيب لاستكثرت من الخير وما مسني السوء إن أنا إلا نذير وبشير لقوم يؤمنون [الأعراف: ١٨٨]. لعمري لا تعدم نفس النبي ومزاجه كمالية في الفطرة، وحسنا في الأخلاق، وصدقا وأمانة في الأقوال والأفعال قبل بعثه؛ لأنه بها استحق النبوة أو وصل بسببها إلى الاتصال بالملائكة وقبول الوحي. كما قال تعالى: فبما رحمة من الله لنت لهم ولو كنت فظا غليظ القلب لانفضوا من حولك [آل عمران: ١٥٩]، وكما قال القوم: لولا نزل هذا القرآن على رجل من القريتين عظيم، قال سبحانه: أهم يقسمون رحمة ربك [الزخرف: ٣٢]، فشخص النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم شخص الرحمة ورحمة مشخصة، ورسالته إلى الخلق رحمة ونعمة، كما قال تعالى: وما أرسلناك إلا رحمة للعالمين [الأنبياء: ١٠٧]، يعرفون نعمة الله ثم ينكرونها وأكثرهم الكافرون [النحل: ٨٣]. والأنبياء خيرة الله في خلقه، وحجة الله على عباده، والوسائل إليه وأبواب رحمته وأسباب نعمته، الله يصطفي من الملائكة رسلا ومن الناس [الحج: ٧٥]، إن الله اصطفى آدم ونوحا [آل عمران: ٣٣] الآية، فكما يصطفيهم من الخلق قولا
The people of truth said: Prophethood is not an attribute referring to the prophet's own self, nor a rank that anyone attains by his knowledge or effort, nor a disposition of his own soul by which he deserves connection to spiritual beings; rather it is a mercy from God Almighty and a favor that He bestows upon whomever He wills among His servants. Just as Noah, peace be upon him, said: 'I do not say to you that I possess the treasures of God, nor do I know the unseen, nor do I say that I am an angel' [Qur'an 6:50] – and similarly other prophets, and the master of mankind, may God bless him and grant him peace, said as the first said: 'Say: Glorified be my Lord! Am I anything but a human messenger?' [Qur'an 17:93], 'Say: I do not possess for myself benefit or harm except what God wills. Had I known the unseen, I would have increased in good, and no evil would have touched me. I am only a warner and a bringer of good tidings to a people who believe' [Qur'an 7:188]. Indeed, the soul and temperament of the Prophet do not lack perfection in innate disposition, goodness in character, truthfulness and trustworthiness in words and deeds before his mission; because by these he deserved prophethood or through them he attained connection to the angels and reception of revelation. As God Almighty said: 'It was by mercy from God that you were lenient with them; had you been harsh and hard-hearted, they would have scattered from around you' [Qur'an 3:159], and as the people said: 'Why was this Qur'an not sent down upon a great man from the two towns?' He, exalted, said: 'Do they distribute the mercy of your Lord?' [Qur'an 43:32]. So the person of the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, is the person of mercy and a personalized mercy, and his mission to creation is mercy and favor, as God Almighty said: 'And We did not send you except as a mercy to the worlds' [Qur'an 21:107], 'They recognize the favor of God then deny it, and most of them are disbelievers' [Qur'an 16:83]. The prophets are the chosen of God among His creation, and God's proof against His servants, and the means to Him, and the doors of His mercy, and the causes of His favor. 'God chooses from the angels messengers and from mankind' [Qur'an 22:75]. 'Indeed, God chose Adam and Noah' [Qur'an 3:33] – the verse. So as He chooses them from creation...
Source pages p. 461

Commentary
This passage is the response of the orthodox (Ahl al-Haqq) to the objections. It begins by stating the correct doctrine: prophethood is not a natural attribute or acquired rank; it is purely a divine mercy and favor. The author then supports this by quoting Quranic verses where prophets disclaim knowledge of the unseen and deny being angels, emphasizing their human nature. Then the passage discusses the Prophet's character before his mission, affirming that he possessed perfection in innate disposition, goodness, truthfulness, and trustworthiness, and that these qualities were instrumental in his receiving prophethood. The author then quotes verses showing that the Prophet's leniency was a mercy from God, and that the choice of the Prophet was a divine decision, not based on human opinion. The passage concludes by stating that prophets are God's chosen and His proof, and that God selects messengers from angels and men.

Key Terms

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophets earn their rank through personal effort and virtue.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that prophethood is not attained by knowledge, effort, or innate disposition, but is a pure mercy from God.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for prophethood?
A) It is acquired through knowledge and effort.
B) It is a natural disposition of the soul.
C) It is a mercy and favor from God.
D) It is inherited from ancestors.

Key Takeaway
Prophethood is a divine mercy, not a human achievement; the prophet's character was prepared by God as part of that mercy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If prophethood is a pure gift that no human can earn, what does that mean for your own pride in your religious deeds? Where have you been trusting your effort more than God's mercy? Will you today ask God to make your deeds a means of His mercy, not a source of pride?
?
The Prophet denied knowledge of the unseen, yet you live planning years ahead as if the future is in your hands. When was the last time you genuinely acknowledged that you do not know what tomorrow holds? How would your decisions change if you lived in that reality right now?
?
The verse says 'They recognize the favor of God then deny it.' Think of one favor—your health, your faith, your family—that you know is from God but you sometimes act as if you earned it. What concrete step will you take today to thank God for that favor without claiming ownership?

The Prophet's Innate Perfection and Divine Selection
Explains the Prophet's pre-prophetic perfection and God's selection of prophets

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Prophet Muhammad possessed perfect innate qualities before his prophethood, and that Allah's selection of prophets involves both verbal appointment and creating them with perfect dispositions.

Core Idea
Prophets are chosen for their innate perfection, not made perfect only after prophethood.

This passage from al-Sanusi establishes that the Prophet Muhammad was already perfect in character, truthfulness, and trustworthiness before receiving revelation. This perfection was the basis for his being chosen for prophethood. The author uses Quranic evidence to show that prophets are Allah's chosen ones, both in their creation and their appointment.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the flow: an initial assertion, followed by Quranic verses, then a summary statement about divine selection.
Pay attention to the repeated theme of 'mercy'.
2
Identify the two aspects of selection
The passage mentions two ways Allah chooses prophets: 'by word' (appointment to prophethood) and 'by deed' (creating them with perfect innate qualities). Find the sentence that makes this distinction.
Look for the phrase 'قولا' and 'فعلا'.
3
Reflect on the Quranic proofs
The author cites several verses. Consider how each supports the claim that prophets are perfect before their mission. Which verse directly responds to the disbelievers' objection?
Verse 43:32 is key: 'Do they distribute the mercy of your Lord?'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لعمري لا تعدم نفس النبي ومزاجه كمالية في الفطرة، وحسنا في الأخلاق، وصدقا وأمانة في الأقوال والأفعال قبل بعثه؛ لأنه بها استحق النبوة أو وصل بسببها إلى الاتصال بالملائكة وقبول الوحي كما قال تعالى: ﴿فَبِمَا رَحْمَةٍ مِّنَ اللَّهِ لِنتَ لَهُمْ وَلَوْ كُنتَ فَظًّا غَلِيظَ الْقَلْبِ لَانفَضُّوا مِنْ حَوْلِكَ﴾ [آل عمران: 159]، وكما قال القوم: ﴿لَوْلَا نُزِلَ هَذَا الْقُرْءَانُ عَلَى رَجُلٍ مِّنَ الْقَرْيَتَيْنِ عَظِيمٍ﴾، قال سبحانه: ﴿أَهُمْ يَقْسِمُونَ رَحْمَتَ رَبِّكَ﴾ [الزخرف: 32]، فشخص النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم شخص الرحمة ورحمة مشخصة، ورسالته إلى الخلق رحمة ونعمة، كما قال تعالى: ﴿وَمَا أَرْسَلْنَكَ إِلَّا رَحْمَةً لِلْعَلَمِينَ﴾ [الأنبياء: 107]، ﴿يَعْرِفُونَ نِعْمَتَ اللَّهِ ثُمَّ يُنكِرُونَهَا وَأَكْثَرُهُمُ الْكَفِرُونَ﴾ [النحل: 83]. والأنبياء خيرة الله في خلقه، وحجة الله على عباده، والوسائل إليه وأبواب رحمته وأسباب نعمته ﴿الله يصطفي من الملائكة رسلا ومن الناس﴾ [الحج: 75]، ﴿إِنَّ اللَّهَ اصْطَفَى ءَادَمَ وَنُوحًا﴾ [آل عمران: 33] الآية، فكما يصطفيهم من الخلق قولا بالرسالة والنبوة، يصطفيهم من الخلق فعلا بكمال الفطرة ونقاء الجوهر وصفاء العنصر وطيب الأخلاق وكرم الأعراق، فيرقيهم مرتبة مرتبة حتى إذا بلغ أشده وبلغ أربعين سنة، وكملت قوته النفسانية وتهيأت لقبول الأسرار الإلهية بعث إليهم ملكا وأنزل عليهم كتابا.
By my life, the soul and temperament of the Prophet lacks not perfection in innate disposition, goodness in morals, truthfulness and trustworthiness in words and deeds before his mission; for by these he deserved prophethood or attained thereby connection with angels and acceptance of revelation, as Allah said: 'So by mercy from Allah you were lenient with them; and if you had been rude and harsh-hearted, they would have dispersed from about you' [3:159]; and as the people said: 'Why was this Qur'an not sent down upon a great man from the two cities?' He said: 'Do they distribute the mercy of your Lord?' [43:32]; so the person of the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, is the person of mercy and a specific mercy, and his message to creation is mercy and grace, as He said: 'And We have not sent you except as a mercy to the worlds' [21:107]; 'They recognize the grace of Allah then deny it, and most of them are disbelievers' [16:83]. And the prophets are Allah's chosen ones among His creation, His proof against His servants, the means to Him, the doors of His mercy, and the causes of His grace: 'Allah chooses from the angels messengers and from mankind' [22:75]; 'Indeed Allah chose Adam and Noah' [3:33]; so just as He chooses them from creation by word through the message and prophethood, He chooses them from creation by deed through perfection of innate disposition, purity of substance, clarity of element, goodness of morals, and nobility of lineage, elevating them rank by rank until when he reaches his prime and attains forty years, and his psychic power is perfected and prepared for receiving divine secrets, He sends to them an angel and reveals to them a book.
Source pages p. 461

Commentary
This passage is a proof that the Prophet Muhammad possessed perfection in innate disposition (firrah), good morals, truthfulness, and trustworthiness even before his prophethood. These qualities were the reason he deserved prophethood and enabled communion with angels and reception of revelation. The author cites several Quranic verses: first, that Allah's mercy made the Prophet gentle, otherwise people would have left him; second, that the disbelievers questioned why the Qur'an was not sent on a great man from either of the two cities, and Allah replied that they do not distribute His mercy, implying that the Prophet is the mercy personified. Then the author states that prophets are Allah's chosen ones, His proof, and the means to His mercy. He quotes verses indicating that Allah chooses messengers from angels and from people, and that He specifically chose Adam, Noah, and others. The key idea is that Allah's selection of prophets is twofold: verbally by appointing them to prophethood and mission, and actually by creating them with perfect innate disposition, purity, good morals, and noble lineage. Then He raises them gradually until the age of forty when their psychic powers are complete and they are ready to receive divine secrets, after which an angel is sent to them with a book.

رحمة

Misconception: Prophets were not perfect in character before their prophethood; they were made perfect only after receiving revelation.
Correction: The passage asserts that the Prophet already possessed perfection in innate disposition, morals, truthfulness, and trustworthiness before his mission, and that this qualified him for prophethood.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet was perfect in character before prophethood, and Allah's selection of prophets is both by appointment and by creating them with perfect dispositions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
The Prophet is called 'a person of mercy'. Is mercy flowing from your tongue and actions in your daily interactions, even with those who annoy you? When was the last time you deliberately chose gentleness when harshness was easier?
?
If Allah's selection is based both on His decree and on the inner reality of the person, what does your current inner state say about your readiness for any responsibility He might give you? Are you living as if your character matters now, or are you coasting?

How Angels Appear to Prophets
Refutes three misconceptions and presents correct view of angelic appearance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why angels do not undergo physical transformation when appearing to prophets, and how they instead manifest by divine power.

Core Idea
Angels appear to prophets by power, not by physical change.

Many have speculated about how an angel, a luminous spiritual being, can appear in human form to a prophet. This passage from al-Shahrastani's Nihayat al-Aqdam refutes three common misconceptions and presents the correct theological understanding grounded in Quranic evidence. Let's examine the arguments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three false views
Read the beginning of the passage where the author lists three incorrect theories about angelic embodiment. Notice each one: densification, annihilation, and transformation.
2
Understand why they are impossible
The author states each is impossible. Consider why—these would imply change or destruction of the angel's essence, which is incompatible with its nature.
3
Recognize the correct view
Focus on the statement that luminous substances have the power to appear in any form. This is supported by Quranic verses about Gabriel appearing to Mary.
The verses are from Surah Maryam and Surah al-An'am.
4
Compare with the soul-body analogy
The author gives an example: the soul's attachment to the body. But note the difference: angelic manifestation is instantaneous and perfect, while soul-body attachment is gradual.
5
Reflect on the implication
Consider how this view preserves the angel's true nature while allowing prophets to see them. This resolves apparent paradoxes in prophetic encounters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا تظن أن الملك يتجسد شخصا؛ بمعنى أنه يتكاثف بعد ما كان جسما لطيفا تكاثف الهواء اللطيف غيما، كما ظنه قوم، ولا أنه تعدم حقيقته ويوجد شخص آخر، ولا أنه تنقلب حقيقته إلى حقيقة أخرى، فإن كل ذلك محال. بل الجواهر النورانية خصت بقوة الظهور بأي شخص أرادوا كما قال تعالى: ﴿فَأَرْسَلْنَا إِلَيْهَا رُوحَنَا فَتَمَثَّلَ لَهَا بَشَرًا سَوِيًّا﴾ [مريم: 17]، وكما قال: ﴿ولو جعلناه ملكا لجعلناه رجلا﴾ [الأنعام: 9]، ولا نجد له مثالا في هذا العالم إلا تمثل تعلق أرواحنا بأجسادنا، غير أن التمثل يستدعي شخصا كامل في الحال، والتعلق يستدعي شخصا يتكون مرتبة فمرتبة سلالة ونطفة وعلقة.
And do not think that the angel becomes embodied as a person, meaning that it becomes dense after having been a subtle body, as when a subtle air condenses into a cloud, as some people supposed; nor that its essence is annihilated and another person is brought into existence; nor that its essence is transformed into another essence, for all that is impossible. Rather, luminous substances are singled out with the power of appearing in whichever person they wish, as Allah said: 'Then We sent to her Our Spirit, and it assumed for her the likeness of a perfect man' [19:17], and as He said: 'And if We had made him an angel, We would have made him a man' [6:9]. And we find no example of this in this world except the representation of the attachment of our souls to our bodies, except that representation demands a person complete in the moment, while attachment demands a person that comes into being stage by stage—descendant, sperm-drop, clot.
Source pages p. 462

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of erroneous views about how an angel appears to a prophet. The author lists three false views: (1) that the angel becomes dense like condensed air turning into a cloud, (2) that the angel's essence is annihilated and a new person is created, (3) that the angel's essence transforms into a different essence. All these are declared impossible. Then the correct view is given: luminous substances (i.e., angels) have the special power to appear in any form they wish. This is supported by two Quranic verses: the angel Gabriel appearing to Mary as a perfect man, and the statement that if Allah had sent an angel as messenger, He would have made him appear as a man. The author then draws an analogy: the closest example in this world is the representation (tamaththul) of the soul's attachment to the body. However, there is a difference: representation (of an angel) requires an immediate perfect person, whereas the soul's attachment to the body develops gradually from sperm-drop to clot to fetus. Thus the angelic appearance is instantaneous and perfect, unlike the gradual formation of the human body. This preserves the angel's true nature while explaining how a prophet can see an angel in human form.

Key Terms
التجسد
الجوهر النوراني
التمثل
التعلق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think angels physically turn into dense bodies or that their essence changes when appearing to prophets.
Correction: Angels appear by their own power of manifestation without any transformation of their essence.

Checkpoint
Which of the following views about angelic embodiment does the author reject?
A) The angel becomes dense like air turning into a cloud.
B) The angel's essence is annihilated and a new person appears.
C) The angel's essence transforms into another essence.
D) All of the above.

Key Takeaway
Angels appear to prophets by a special power of manifestation without any change in their luminous essence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever doubted the reality of angelic appearances because you could not imagine how it happens? After reading this lesson, how does the argument from impossibility (muhal) and the Quranic evidence remove that doubt? What concrete step will you take today to strengthen your belief in the angels?
?
The author warns us not to think of angelic embodiment in terms of physical change. Is there any area of your faith where you are tempted to imagine Allah's creation in terms of physical processes? How will you guard against such assumptions in your daily thoughts?
?
The analogy of the soul's attachment to the body is used but then distinguished. How does reflecting on your own soul's relationship with your body help you grasp the power of angelic manifestation? What does that teach you about the limitations of human analogies for divine matters?

Refutation of the Sabian Contradiction
Refutes the Sabian belief by showing its internal contradiction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical inconsistency in the Sabian position and the Hanafite affirmation of lordly persons as intermediaries.

Core Idea
The Sabians deny spiritual descent yet practice idol worship, exposing a logical inconsistency.

The Sabians deny that spiritual beings can descend onto physical forms, yet they themselves create idols as manifestations of spiritual temples. This passage exposes their contradiction and presents the orthodox view of prophet-like 'lordly persons' created from pure substances corresponding to spiritual realities.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to understand the argument structure.
Notice the rhetorical question addressed to the Sabians.
2
Identify the Sabian claim
Note that Sabians deny spiritual descent but believe in temples and corresponding persons.
3
Spot the contradiction
The author points out that Sabians themselves make idols as manifestations of those temples.
This shows they implicitly accept the descent they deny.
4
Understand the Hanafite alternative
The author affirms 'lordly persons' created by selection from pure substances, corresponding like light to light.
These are the prophets.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الستم تقولون معاشر الصابئة المحيلين نزول الروحاني على الجسماني: إن كل روحاني له هيكل يظهر به ويتصرف فيه ويستوي عليه، وكل هيكل في العالم العلوي له شخص في العالم السفلي يظهر به ويتصرف فيه ويستوي عليه، غير أنكم اتخذتم بصنعتكم أصناما آلهة وهي مظاهر تلك الهياكل التي هي مظاهر تلك الروحانيات؟ ونحن معاشر الحنفاء أثبتنا أشخاصا ربانية مفطورة بوضع الخلقة على اصطفاء من الجواهر واجتباء من العنصر مناسبة لتلك الجواهر الروحانية مناسبة النور للنور والظل للظل، وللنبي عليه السلام طرفان؛ بشرية ورسالية ﴿ قل سبحان ربي هل كنت إلا بشرا رسولا ﴾ [الإسراء: 93]، فبطرف يقبل الوحي وبطرف يؤدي الرسالة، والوحي هو إلقاء الشيء إلى الشيء بسرعة فكل صورة علمية يقبلها بطرفه الروحانية عن الملائكة الذين هم رسل ربهم إليه دفعة واحدة، كوقوع الصورة في المرآة، فهو وحي، وأقرب مثال له إلينا المنام الصادق، فإن الرائي يرى كأنه نزل بستانا واجتنى ثمارا وخاض في الماء، وتحدث أحاديث كثيرة من سؤال
Do you not say, O community of Sabaeans who deem impossible the descent of the spiritual onto the physical: that every spiritual being has a temple (haykal) through which it appears, acts, and over which it presides; and every temple in the upper world has a person in the lower world through which it appears, acts, and over which it presides; except that you have taken, by your craftsmanship, idols as gods, and they are manifestations of those temples which are manifestations of those spiritual beings? And we, the community of Hanifs, have affirmed lordly persons (ashkhas rabbaniyya), created by the formation of nature, by selection from substances and choice from the origin (unsur), corresponding to those spiritual substances as light corresponds to light and shadow to shadow. And the Prophet, peace be upon him, has two aspects: human and messenger ("Say: Glorified is my Lord; am I anything but a human messenger?" [Al-Isra: 93]). So by one aspect he receives revelation, and by the other he delivers the message. And revelation (al-wahy) is the swift casting of something to something; so every scientific form that he receives through his spiritual aspect from the angels who are messengers of their Lord to him, all at once, like the falling of an image in a mirror, that is revelation. And the closest example for us is the true dream; for the dreamer sees as if he descended into a garden and plucked fruits and waded in water and engaged in many conversations of questioning
Source pages p. 463

Commentary
This passage begins by addressing the Sabian community, who deny that spiritual beings can descend onto physical beings. The author points out a contradiction: the Sabians themselves believe that every spiritual being has a temple (haykal) through which it appears and acts, and that every temple in the upper world has a corresponding person in the lower world. Yet they reject the idea of spiritual descent while they make idols as manifestations of those temples. The author then states the Hanafite (orthodox) position: they affirm 'lordly persons' (ashkhas rabbaniyya) that are created by God from pure substances, chosen for their suitability, and they correspond to spiritual substances like light to light or shadow to shadow. These are the prophets. The Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) has two aspects: a human aspect and a messenger aspect, as indicated in Quran 17:93. Through his human aspect he receives revelation, and through his messenger aspect he delivers it. Revelation (al-wahy) is defined as the swift casting of something to something. The prophet receives scientific forms (images of knowledge) from the angels all at once, like an image falling into a mirror. The closest analogy is a true dream: a person sees himself doing things like descending into a garden, picking fruits, wading in water, and conversing with many questions. The passage emphasizes the instantaneous and non-material transmission of knowledge from the angel to the prophet.

Key Terms
هيكل
أشخاص ربانية
اصطفاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the Sabians were consistent in denying spiritual descent while rejecting idols, but the passage shows they do use idols.
Correction: The passage shows that Sabians actually create idols as manifestations of spiritual temples, thus they do accept a form of spiritual descent.

Checkpoint
What do the Sabians deny according to this passage?
A) The existence of spiritual beings.
B) The descent of the spiritual onto the physical.
C) The use of idols.
D) The existence of the upper world.

Key Takeaway
The Sabians' own practice of idol worship contradicts their denial of spiritual descent, and the Hanafites affirm divinely selected persons who correspond to spiritual substances.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The Hanafites affirm that prophets are selected by God from pure substances. Do you truly trust that God's chosen messengers are sufficient for your guidance, or do you rely on human-made systems more? What is one teaching of the Prophet ﷺ that you have neglected, and how will you act on it starting today?
?
The Sabians crafted idols with their own hands and worshipped them. What 'idols' have you created in your life—status, wealth, relationships—that you treat as ultimate? What step will you take today to dethrone that idol and place God first?

Two Aspects of the Prophet and Revelation
Explains the dual nature of the prophet and the instantaneous nature of revelation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the dual nature of the prophet (human and messenger) and how revelation occurs as instantaneous reception of knowledge from angels.

Core Idea
The prophet receives revelation through his spiritual aspect instantaneously, like an image in a mirror.

After refuting the Sabians, the author explains the nature of prophethood. The prophet has two aspects: a human aspect and a messenger aspect. Through the human aspect he receives revelation from angels, and through the messenger aspect he delivers it. Revelation is defined as swift casting, and the closest analogy is a true dream.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to understand the description of the prophet's two aspects.
Notice the Quranic verse cited.
2
Identify the two aspects
The prophet has a human aspect and a messenger aspect (Quran 17:93).
3
Understand the process of revelation
The human aspect receives revelation; the messenger aspect delivers it. Revelation is defined as swift casting.
4
Grasp the nature of revelation
Revelation is instantaneous, like an image in a mirror. The true dream is the closest analogy.
This helps us imagine how the prophet receives knowledge without sensory input.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الستم تقولون معاشر الصابئة المحيلين نزول الروحاني على الجسماني: إن كل روحاني له هيكل يظهر به ويتصرف فيه ويستوي عليه، وكل هيكل في العالم العلوي له شخص في العالم السفلي يظهر به ويتصرف فيه ويستوي عليه، غير أنكم اتخذتم بصنعتكم أصناما آلهة وهي مظاهر تلك الهياكل التي هي مظاهر تلك الروحانيات؟ ونحن معاشر الحنفاء أثبتنا أشخاصا ربانية مفطورة بوضع الخلقة على اصطفاء من الجواهر واجتباء من العنصر مناسبة لتلك الجواهر الروحانية مناسبة النور للنور والظل للظل، وللنبي عليه السلام طرفان؛ بشرية ورسالية ﴿ قل سبحان ربي هل كنت إلا بشرا رسولا ﴾ [الإسراء: 93]، فبطرف يقبل الوحي وبطرف يؤدي الرسالة، والوحي هو إلقاء الشيء إلى الشيء بسرعة فكل صورة علمية يقبلها بطرفه الروحانية عن الملائكة الذين هم رسل ربهم إليه دفعة واحدة، كوقوع الصورة في المرآة، فهو وحي، وأقرب مثال له إلينا المنام الصادق، فإن الرائي يرى كأنه نزل بستانا واجتنى ثمارا وخاض في الماء، وتحدث أحاديث كثيرة من سؤال
Do you not say, O community of Sabaeans who deem impossible the descent of the spiritual onto the physical: that every spiritual being has a temple (haykal) through which it appears, acts, and over which it presides; and every temple in the upper world has a person in the lower world through which it appears, acts, and over which it presides; except that you have taken, by your craftsmanship, idols as gods, and they are manifestations of those temples which are manifestations of those spiritual beings? And we, the community of Hanifs, have affirmed lordly persons (ashkhas rabbaniyya), created by the formation of nature, by selection from substances and choice from the origin (unsur), corresponding to those spiritual substances as light corresponds to light and shadow to shadow. And the Prophet, peace be upon him, has two aspects: human and messenger ("Say: Glorified is my Lord; am I anything but a human messenger?" [Al-Isra: 93]). So by one aspect he receives revelation, and by the other he delivers the message. And revelation (al-wahy) is the swift casting of something to something; so every scientific form that he receives through his spiritual aspect from the angels who are messengers of their Lord to him, all at once, like the falling of an image in a mirror, that is revelation. And the closest example for us is the true dream; for the dreamer sees as if he descended into a garden and plucked fruits and waded in water and engaged in many conversations of questioning
Source pages p. 463

Commentary
This passage begins by addressing the Sabian community, who deny that spiritual beings can descend onto physical beings. The author points out a contradiction: the Sabians themselves believe that every spiritual being has a temple (haykal) through which it appears and acts, and that every temple in the upper world has a corresponding person in the lower world. Yet they reject the idea of spiritual descent while they make idols as manifestations of those temples. The author then states the Hanafite (orthodox) position: they affirm 'lordly persons' (ashkhas rabbaniyya) that are created by God from pure substances, chosen for their suitability, and they correspond to spiritual substances like light to light or shadow to shadow. These are the prophets. The Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) has two aspects: a human aspect and a messenger aspect, as indicated in Quran 17:93. Through his human aspect he receives revelation, and through his messenger aspect he delivers it. Revelation (al-wahy) is defined as the swift casting of something to something. The prophet receives scientific forms (images of knowledge) from the angels all at once, like an image falling into a mirror. The closest analogy is a true dream: a person sees himself doing things like descending into a garden, picking fruits, wading in water, and conversing with many questions. The passage emphasizes the instantaneous and non-material transmission of knowledge from the angel to the prophet.

Key Terms
طرفان: بشرية ورسالية
الوحي
الصورة العلمية
المنام الصادق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the prophet's human aspect is passive and only the messenger aspect is active, but both are active: one receives, one delivers.
Correction: Both aspects are active: the human aspect actively receives revelation, and the messenger aspect actively delivers it.

Checkpoint
What is the closest analogy to revelation in this passage?
A) A teacher writing on a board.
B) A true dream.
C) A telephone call.
D) A book being read.

Key Takeaway
The prophet has two active aspects — human and messenger — and revelation is the instantaneous, mirror-like reception of knowledge from angels, likened to a true dream.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The prophet received revelation like an image in a mirror—instantaneously, without distortion. When you encounter a verse or hadith, do you allow it to imprint directly on your heart, or do you filter it through your own biases and desires? What would change if you approached the Quran with the same mirror-like readiness that the prophet's spiritual aspect had? Commit to reading one verse tomorrow with the intention of letting it reflect fully on your soul.
?
Your life has two aspects: receiving truth and acting on it. Which is stronger—your openness to divine guidance or your willingness to convey it to others? The prophet had both in balance. This week, identify one truth you have received but not shared, and ask yourself what fear is holding you back. Then, take one concrete step to deliver it, even if only to yourself in prayer.
?
The true dream is a fragment of prophecy. Have you ever had a dream that guided you toward righteousness or warned you against sin? If so, did you take it seriously? If not, are you living in a way that makes your soul sensitive to such signs? Evaluate your spiritual alertness and resolve to pay closer attention to the subtle ways Allah communicates with you outside of formal revelation.

The Prophet's Two Aspects and Revelation as Instantaneous
Explains the Prophet's dual nature and revelation as instantaneous like a true dream

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Prophet's dual nature (human and prophetic) and how revelation occurs instantaneously, akin to a true dream.

Core Idea
Revelation is immediate knowledge, not sequential thought.

The Prophet ﷺ is both a human being and a messenger of Allah. This lesson explores how these two aspects function: through his humanity he delivers the message, and through his spiritual side he receives revelation. The author then explains revelation as an instantaneous imparting of knowledge, using the familiar example of a true dream to illustrate how multiple meanings can be grasped in an instant.

Guided Path
1
Understand the dual nature
Read the opening line: the Prophet has two sides—bashariyya (humanity) and risaliyya (messengership). Notice the Qur'anic evidence cited. Ask yourself: why is this distinction important?
This sets the foundation for understanding how revelation works.
2
Define revelation (wahy)
The author defines wahy as 'the casting of a thing to a thing with speed.' Focus on the idea of speed and immediacy. It is not a drawn-out process.
3
Examine the analogy of the mirror
Revelation is compared to an image falling into a mirror—instant and complete. Reflect on how this differs from human learning.
The spiritual side receives knowledge 'all at once'.
4
Analyze the true dream analogy
Read the description of the true dream: complex events occurring in a moment. The author explains why this is possible—forms from the world of meanings do not require time or sequence.
This is the closest example to revelation we can experience.
5
Connect to prophecy
The passage concludes that true dreams are a part of prophecy, as are virtues like deliberation and good demeanor. Consider how this elevates the status of true dreams.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وللنبي عليه السلام طرفان؛ بشرية ورسالية ( قل سبحان [؟] هل كنت إلا بشرًا رسولًا ﴾ [الإسراء : ۹۳]، فبطرف يقبل الوحي وبطرف يؤدي الرسالة، والوحي هو إلقاء الشيء إلى الشيء بسرعة فكل صورة علمية يقبلها بطرفه الروحانية عن الملائكة الذين هم رسل ربهم إليه دفعة واحدة، كوقوع الصورة في المرآة، فهو وحي، وأقرب مثال له إلينا المنام الصادق، فإن الرائي يرى كأنه نزل بستانًا واجتنى ثمارًا وخاض في الماء، وتحدث أحاديث كثيرة من سؤال وجواب وأمر ونهي، بحيث لو أملاها ملأت أوراقا، وشحنت صحائف، وكل ذلك في غفوة كأنها لحظة وما ذاك إلا لأن الصور والفعلية القولية إذا كانت من عالم المعاني بواسطة تلك المنام لم يستدع زمانًا ولا ترتيبا، بحيث يستدعيها حال اليقظة، بل وقعت دفعة واحدة في نفس الرائي حتى انتقشت فيه، ثم غير عنه بعبارات كثيرة وعبر المعبر عن صورها الخيالية إلى معانيها العقلية. ولذلك صارت الرؤيا الصادقة جزءًا من أجزاء النبوة، كما صارت التؤدة والأناة وحسن السمت جزءا من أجزاء النبوة.
And the Prophet, peace be upon him, has two sides: a human side (bashariyya) and a messengership side (risaliyya). (Say: Glory be to [?] I am but a human messenger) [Al-Isra: 93]. So by one side he receives revelation (wahy) and by the other he delivers the message. And revelation is the casting of a thing to a thing with speed. So every scientific form (sura 'ilmiyya) that he receives by his spiritual side from the angels, who are the messengers of their Lord to him, all at once, like the falling of an image in a mirror, it is revelation. The closest example to us of this is the true dream (al-manam al-sadiq). For the dreamer sees as if he entered a garden, gathered fruits, waded in water, and engaged in many conversations of question and answer, command and prohibition, such that if they were written down they would fill pages and fill sheets, and all that in a doze like a moment. That is only because the forms, actual and verbal, when they come from the world of meanings by means of that sleep, do not require time or sequence as they would in wakefulness, but rather occur all at once in the dreamer's soul until they are imprinted in it, then they are expressed in many expressions and the interpreter passes from their imaginary forms to their intellectual meanings. Therefore, the true dream became a part of the parts of prophecy, just as deliberation (al-tu'da), composure (al-anat), and good demeanor (husn al-samt) became parts of the parts of prophecy.
Source pages p. 463

Commentary
This passage explains the dual nature of the Prophet and the nature of revelation. The Prophet has a human side and a prophetic side; through the human side he delivers the message, through the spiritual side he receives revelation. Revelation is defined as instantaneous imparting of knowledge, like an image falling into a mirror. The closest analogy in human experience is the true dream, where one experiences a comprehensive event in an instant, without temporal sequence. True dreams are therefore a part of prophecy, as are virtues like deliberation and composure.

النبي (the Prophet)
بشرية (humanity)
رسالة (messengership)
وحي (revelation)
المنام الصادق (true dream)
غفوة (doze)
انتقش (imprinted)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: People think revelation is a slow, sequential process like human thought or learning.
Correction: The passage clarifies that revelation is immediate and without temporal sequence, comparing it to an image in a mirror or a true dream.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the closest example to revelation (wahy) that humans can experience?
A) A metaphor
B) A true dream
C) A reflection in water
D) A spoken command

Key Takeaway
Revelation is instantaneous knowledge, not a step-by-step process, and the true dream is the closest human analogy to it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever had a dream so vivid that it felt like hours in a moment? How does that experience help you understand what it means for the Prophet to receive entire chapters of the Qur'an in an instant? Will you now view your dreams as a window into the possibility of instantaneous divine knowledge?
?

What would change in your relationship with the Qur'an if you truly internalized that every word was imprinted on the Prophet's heart all at once, from beyond time and sequence?
?
The author says that true dreams are a part of prophecy. When you have a dream that seems meaningful, do you brush it off or do you consider that it might be a message from the world of meanings? How can you train yourself to take such dreams seriously as a reminder of the prophetic experience?

Prophethood as Composite and Metaphorical Descent of Divine Speech
States that prophethood is composite and divine speech descent is metaphorical.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that prophethood is a composite whole with parts attainable by the righteous, and that the descent of divine speech is a metaphorical coming of the angel, not physical movement.

Core Idea
Prophethood is a whole with parts; divine speech descends metaphorically, not physically.

This passage from Niḥāyat al-Aqdām clarifies two important aspects of prophethood and divine speech. First, prophecy is not a simple gift but a composite of many parts, some of which can be attained by pious individuals through obedience. Second, the 'descent' of God's speech (the Qur'an) does not imply any physical movement or change in God; rather, it refers to the angel's metaphorical descent. Let's explore this carefully.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the two distinct topics: the composite nature of prophethood and the metaphorical descent of speech.
2
Understand the composite concept
The author explains that prophethood is a whole (jumla) with parts (ajzā’). The whole is only for prophets, but the parts can be attained by the righteous. The Prophet ﷺ's saying about truthful dreams is given as evidence.
3
Grasp the meaning of descent
The descent (nuzūl) of God's speech is not a physical relocation (intiql). Instead, it is the meaning of the angel descending with it. The author gives two linguistic examples: 'I have descended from my word' meaning I withdrew, and 'the prince descended from his right' meaning he relinquished it.
4
Reflect on theological implications
Consider why this distinction matters. It protects the transcendence of Allah and shows that prophetic gifts are both divine election and, in part, attainable through human effort.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فالنبوة إذا جملة ذات أجزاء، وتلك الجملة بمجموعها لا تتحقق إلا لمن اصطفاه الله تعالى لرسالته، وبعض أجزائها قد ثبت للصالحين من عباده، فيبلغون إلى ذلك الجزء بطاعتهم وعبادتهم، كما قال صلى الله عليه وسلم: أصدقكم رؤيا أصدقكم حديثا، أما مجموعها من حيث المجموع فلا يصل إليه أحد بكسبه واستطاعته. وأما نزول كلام الباري تعالى فمعنى نزول الملك به فليس يستدعي النزول انتقالا، فإنك تقول: نزلت عن كلامي، ونزل الأمير عن حقه.
So prophecy is a whole having parts, and that whole in its totality is realized only for whom God has chosen for His message. Some of its parts have been established for the righteous among His servants, and they attain that part through their obedience and worship, as he (peace be upon him) said: 'The most truthful of you in dreams are the most truthful in speech.' But as for its totality as a whole, no one reaches it by his own effort and capacity. As for the descent (nuzul) of the speech of the Exalted God (kalam al-Bari), it is the meaning of the descent of the angel with it, so it does not require descent as movement (intiqal). For you say: 'I have descended from my word,' and 'The prince descended from his right.'
Source pages p. 464

Commentary
This passage concludes the discussion on prophecy and clarifies the nature of the descent of divine speech. Prophecy is a composite of parts; the whole is only for prophets, but righteous individuals can attain some parts (like true dreams) through obedience. The descent of God's speech (the Qur'an) is not a physical movement but a metaphorical descent, as when one says 'I have descended from my word' meaning I withdrew from a promise. Similarly, the angel's descent with revelation is not a spatial relocation.

Key Terms
النبوة (prophethood)
جزء (part)
كلام الباري (divine speech)
نزول (descent)
انتقال (movement)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the descent of the Qur'an involves God physically moving or changing location.
Correction: The author clarifies that the descent is metaphorical, referring to the angel's descent with the speech, and uses linguistic examples to show that 'descending' often means revocation or abandonment, not spatial movement.

Checkpoint
What does the author mean by the 'descent' of divine speech?
A) God physically moves down
B) The angel descends with it metaphorically
C) The speech itself descends
D) It is a physical book descending

Key Takeaway
Prophethood is a composite whole; its parts are attainable through obedience, but the whole is unique to prophets. The descent of divine speech is metaphorical, not physical.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The descent of divine speech is metaphorical, not physical. Does that understanding deepen your reverence for the Qur'an, or does it make the revelation feel less real to you? How will you adjust your heart's attitude toward the Qur'an after realizing this?
?
If the whole of prophethood is unattainable by effort, do you still strive for its parts out of love for God, or have you given up because you cannot be a prophet? What one thing will you change to rekindle that striving?

The Truthful Dream as a Part of Prophethood
Author explains truthful dreams as a part of prophethood and the composite nature of prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why truthful dreams are considered a part of prophethood and how prophethood is a composite whole that cannot be fully attained by personal effort.

Core Idea
Truthful dreams are a divine gift, but prophethood as a whole is exclusive to God's chosen messengers.

In this passage, the author delves into the nature of prophethood, describing it as a composite whole made up of various parts. He illustrates how truthful dreams, which occur in an instant and convey vast meanings, are one such part. Understanding this helps clarify why some righteous individuals experience true dreams without becoming prophets.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how the author describes the instantaneous nature of dream revelation and the role of the interpreter.
Pay attention to the phrase 'دفعة واحدة' (all at once) — it's key.
2
Identify the analogy with other prophetic parts
The author says truthful dreams are a part of prophethood just like deliberation and good demeanor. Why do you think these qualities are also considered parts?
Think about how these traits are praiseworthy and connected to prophethood.
3
Distinguish between part and whole
The author emphasizes that the whole of prophethood is only for those chosen by Allah, but parts can be attained by the righteous. This is a crucial distinction to avoid misunderstanding.
The Prophetic hadith supports that truthfulness in speech relates to truthfulness in dreams.
4
Reflect on the misconception
Consider the common misunderstanding that having true dreams could mean one becomes a prophet. The author clarifies that the whole is not earned; it is a divine choice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجواب وأمر ونهي، بحيث لو أملاها ملأت أوراقا، وشحنت صحائف، وكل ذلك في غفوة كأنها لحظة وما ذاك إلا لأن الصور والفعلية القولية إذا كانت من عالم المعاني بواسطة تلك المنام لم يستدع زمانًا ولا ترتيبا، بل وقعت دفعة واحدة في نفس الرائي حتى انتقشت فيه، ثم غير عنه بعبارات كثيرة وعبر المعبر عن صورها الخيالية إلى معانيها العقلية. ولذلك صارت الرؤيا الصادقة جزءًا من أجزاء النبوة، كما صارت التؤدة والأناة وحسن السمت جزءا من أجزاء النبوة. فالنبوة إذا جملة ذات أجزاء، وتلك الجملة بمجموعها لا تتحقق إلا لمن اصطفاه الله تعالى لرسالته، وبعض أجزائها قد ثبت للصالحين من عباده، فيبلغون إلى ذلك الجزء بطاعتهم وعبادتهم، كما قال صلى الله عليه وسلم: أصدقكم رؤيا أصدقكم حديثا، أما مجموعها من حيث المجموع فلا يصل إليه أحد بكسبه واستطاعته.
And a response and command and prohibition, such that if he filled them they would fill pages and fill notebooks, and all that in a slumber like a moment, and that is only because the forms and the verbal actuality, when they are from the world of meanings by means of that dream, do not require time nor order, as wakefulness requires, but rather occur all at once in the soul of the dreamer until they are engraved in it, then they are expressed by many expressions and the interpreter expresses their imaginary forms into intellectual meanings. Therefore the truthful dream became a part of the parts of prophethood, just as deliberation and gentleness and good demeanor became a part of the parts of prophethood. So prophethood is a whole having parts, and that whole in its entirety is not actualized except for whom God Almighty has chosen for His message, and some of its parts have been established for the righteous among His servants, so they attain that part by their obedience and worship, as the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The most truthful of you in dreams are the most truthful in speech.' As for the whole, from the perspective of the whole, no one reaches it by his earning and capacity.
Source pages p. 464

Commentary
This passage defines the nature of prophethood as a composite whole and establishes that truthful dreams are one of its parts. The author begins by describing the phenomenon of dreams: in a state of slumber, a person may receive vast amounts of information—commands, prohibitions, answers—without the temporal extension and arrangement required in wakefulness. This is because the forms and verbal contents come from the world of meanings through the dream, occurring instantaneously and being impressed upon the dreamer's soul. The interpreter later translates these imaginary forms into intellectual meanings. Consequently, the truthful dream is designated as a part of prophethood, just as qualities like deliberation, gentleness, and good demeanor are also parts. The author then clarifies that prophethood is a composite whole (jumla dhāt ajzāʾ), and this whole in its totality is only actualized for the one God has chosen for His message. However, some parts of prophethood, such as truthful dreams, can be attained by the righteous through their obedience and worship. The Prophetic saying 'The most truthful of you in dreams are the most truthful in speech' supports this. The key nuance is that while parts can be gained by human effort, the complete status of prophethood—the whole—is exclusive to God's chosen prophets and cannot be earned by anyone through personal striving.

النبوة

Misconception: Some may think that if a righteous person has true dreams, they can become a prophet or attain full prophethood.
Correction: The author clarifies that the whole of prophethood is only for those chosen by Allah; parts like true dreams can be attained, but the complete status is not earned by human effort.

C) It is composed of parts that are all directly attainable.
D) It is earned by truthful speech alone.

Key Takeaway
Truthful dreams are a part of prophethood that can be attained by the righteous through worship, but the complete prophethood is exclusively for Allah's chosen messengers and cannot be earned.

Clarifying the Descent of Divine Speech and God's Sovereignty
The author clarifies the metaphorical descent of God's speech and establishes God's sovereignty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author reinterprets 'descent' of God's speech metaphorically and establishes God's absolute sovereignty as the basis for prophetic commands.

Core Idea
God's speech descends through angels, not by physical movement, and His sovereignty justifies His commands.

The author begins by addressing a potential confusion about God's speech descending. He clarifies that such descent does not imply spatial movement, using linguistic examples and Quranic verses. He then lays the groundwork for prophethood by affirming God's absolute kingship and His right to command and forbid.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully, noting how the author distinguishes between literal and metaphorical descent.
Pay attention to the linguistic examples.
2
Identify the key terms
Identify terms like 'نزول كلام الباري' and 'الأمر الأزلي' and understand their meanings.
3
Trace the argument
Follow the author's reasoning from clarifying descent to establishing God as King and Owner, which justifies command and prohibition.
This foundation is necessary for the later argument about prophethood.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider why the author emphasizes that God's descent is not literal. How does this affect our understanding of divine attributes?

وأما نزول كلام الباري تعالى فمعنى نزول الملك به فليس يستدعي النزول انتقالا، فإنك تقول : نزلت عن كلامي، ونزل الأمير عن حقه، وقد ورد إلي عن الخبر نزول الرب تعالى إلى السماء الدنيا، وورد في القرآن مجيئه وإتيانه، وذلك لا انتقالا كما حقق في التأويلات، ثم الكلام الذي هو أمره الأزلي يطلق عليه النزول إلا بمعنى نزول الآيات الدالة عليه، ثم الإلزام على الخصم إنما يظهر إذا أثبتنا له أمرًا ونهيًا، وإثبات الأمر إنما يظهر إذا توافقنا على أنه تعالى ملكاً ومالكا، وله أن يتصرف في ملكه بالأمر والنهي والتكليف على من ثبت له اختيار. وإذا حصل وفاقنا على هذه المراتب وعلمنا أن كل واحد من آحاد الناس لا يتأهل لقبول أمر الله تعالى وحيا إليه، تعين بالضرورة واحدا اصطفاه من عباده: وربك يخلق ما يشاء ويختار ما كان لهم الخيرة [القصص: 68]، فدعواه نفسها من الجائزات العقلية، وإذا كانت الدعوى مقرونة بدليل الصدق وجب التصديق، وأنه يجب لا يتراخى دليل الصدق عن نفس الخبر، فإن المخاطب مكلف بالتصديق في الحال، ولا يتراخى الوجوب عليه إلا أن يعرف الصدق، بل التمكن كاف كما بينا ولكن التمكن إنما تحقق من جانب المكلف بوجود العقل التام والعقل إنما يدرك إذا وجد دليل الصدق، فكما لا يتراخى الوجوب عن وقت التكليف، لا يتراخى أيضًا دليل الصدق عن نفس الدعوى، فليبحث هاهنا كل
As for the descent of the speech of God Most High, it is by the meaning of the descent of the angel with it, so it does not require the descent to be a transition, for you say: 'I descended from my word,' and 'the prince descended from his right,' and there has come to us the report of the descent of the Lord Most High to the heaven of this world, and there came in the Qur'an His coming and His arrival, and that is not a transition as has been verified in the interpretations. Then the speech, which is His eternal command, is called descent only in the sense of the descent of the verses indicating it. Then the obligation upon the opponent only appears when we affirm for Him a command and a prohibition, and the affirmation of the command only appears when we agree that He Most High is King and Owner, and He has the right to dispose in His kingdom by command, prohibition, and obligation upon whom has been established for him choice. And when we have agreement on these levels and we know that every single one of individual people is not qualified to accept the command of God Most High as revelation to him, then necessarily one is determined whom He has chosen from His servants: 'And your Lord creates what He wills and chooses; they have no choice' [al-Qasas (28):68]. So his claim itself is among the rational possibilities, and when the claim is accompanied by a proof of truthfulness, then belief is obligatory. And it is necessary that the proof of truthfulness is not delayed from the very report, for the addressee is obligated to believe immediately, and the obligation is not delayed upon him except that he knows the truthfulness; rather, the capacity is sufficient as we have explained. But the capacity is only actualized on the part of the obligated person by the existence of complete intellect, and the intellect only perceives when the proof of truthfulness exists. So just as the obligation is not delayed from the time of obligation, likewise the proof of truthfulness is not delayed from the very claim. So let everyone search here.
Source pages p. 464

Commentary
This passage argues for the necessity of a prophet and the requirement that his claim of prophethood be accompanied by an immediate proof of truthfulness (miracle). The author begins by clarifying that the 'descent' of God's speech is not a physical motion, but rather the descent of the angel bearing it; similarly, reports of God's descent to the lower heaven or His coming in the Qur'an are interpreted metaphorically without spatial movement. The eternal speech (al-amr al-azalī) is called 'descent' only in the sense of the descent of the verses that indicate it. Next, the author establishes that obligating the opponent depends on first affirming that God gives commands and prohibitions, which in turn rests on the recognition that God is King and Owner, having the right to dispose of His property by commanding, prohibiting, and obligating those who have free choice. Once these premises are accepted, since ordinary people cannot receive divine revelation directly, it follows that God must choose a specific person as a prophet, as the verse states: 'Your Lord creates what He wills and chooses; they have no choice.' The claim of prophethood is a rational possibility (min al-jāʾizāt al-ʿaqliyya), but for it to be binding upon others, it must be accompanied by a proof of truthfulness (dāll al-ṣidq) that compels belief. This proof must not be delayed from the very claim because the addressee is immediately obligated to believe upon hearing the claim; the obligation does not wait for the addressee to independently verify truthfulness through other means. Rather, the mere capacity to know (al-tamakkun) is sufficient, and that capacity is actualized when the intellect exists and the proof is present. Therefore, just as the obligation to believe is immediate, the proof must also be immediate—hence the required miracle must accompany the prophetic claim.

Key Terms
نزول كلام الباري
الأمر الأزلي
ملكاً ومالكا

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the descent of God's speech actually mean?
A) God moves from heaven to earth.
B) The angel descends with the speech.
C) The speech itself changes location.
D) God retracts His word.

Key Takeaway
God's descent is metaphorical; His eternal speech is called descent through the descent of verses, and His sovereignty justifies His commands and prohibitions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
You recite the Quran and assume it is God's speech. But do you live as if its commands are from the absolute Owner of all? Or do you pick and choose based on your convenience? Confess honestly: which command of God do you most struggle to obey because you forget He is the King and Owner?
?
God has placed obligation upon you because He gave you choice. Are you using your free will to submit to His sovereignty, or to rebel? What is one area of your life where you need to acknowledge His ownership and start obeying His command today?
